Free Trade Agreement between the United Mexican States,
the Republic of Colombia and the Republic of Venezuela (ACE No. 33)

PREAMBLE
The governments of the Republic of Venezuela, the United Mexican States and the Republic of Colombia,


CONSIDERING:
The condition that their countries have as Contracting Parties in the General Agreement on Customs Tariffs and Trade (GATT) and the commitments that derive from it for them.
The condition that their countries have as members of the Latin American Integration Association (ALADI) and the commitments derived from it for them, as well as the will to strengthen said Association as a convergence center of Latin American integration.
The status of Colombia and Venezuela as member countries of the Cartagena Agreement and the commitments derived from it for them
The coincidence in the policies of internationalization and modernization of the economies of their countries, as well as their decision to contribute to the expansion of world trade.
The priority of deepening economic relations between their countries and the decision to promote the process of Latin American integration.
RESOLVED TO:
Strengthen the special bonds of friendship, solidarity and cooperation between their peoples.
Contribute to harmonious development, the expansion of world trade and the expansion of international cooperation.
Create an expanded and secure market for goods and services produced in their territories.
Reduce distortions in trade.
Establish clear and mutually beneficial rules for your commercial exchange.
Ensure a predictable commercial framework for the planning of productive activities and investment.
Strengthen the competitiveness of their companies in world markets.
Encourage innovation and creativity by protecting intellectual property rights.
Create new employment opportunities, improve working conditions and living standards in their respective territories.
Preserve its ability to safeguard the public welfare.
Promote sustainable development.
Promote coordinated action by the Parties in international economic forums, particularly those related to Latin American integration processes.
Encourage the dynamic participation of the different economic agents, particularly the private sector, in efforts aimed at deepening economic relations between the Parties and developing and maximizing the possibilities of their joint presence in international markets.
THEY CELEBRATE THIS FREE TRADE AGREEMENT:
In accordance with the GATT and with the character of Partial Scope Agreement for Economic Complementation in accordance with the provisions of the 1980 Montevideo Treaty and Resolution 2 of the Council of Ministers of Foreign Affairs of the contracting parties to that treaty.
CHAPTER I: Initial provisions.
Article 1-01: Objectives.
The objectives of this Treaty, developed specifically through its principles and rules, including those of national treatment, most favored nation treatment and transparency, are the following:


a) stimulate the expansion and diversification of trade between the Parties;

b) eliminate trade barriers and facilitate the circulation of goods and services between the Parties;

c) promote conditions of fair competition in trade between the Parties;

d) substantially increase investment opportunities in the territories of the Parties;

e) protect and enforce intellectual property rights;

f) establish guidelines for further cooperation between the Parties, as well as at the regional and multilateral level aimed at expanding and improving the benefits of this Agreement;

g) create effective procedures for the application and fulfillment of this Agreement, for its joint administration and for the settlement of controversies;
h) Promote equitable relations between the Parties, recognizing differential treatment based on the categories of countries established in ALADI;


The Parties shall interpret and apply the provisions of this Agreement in light of the objectives set out in paragraph 1 and in accordance with the applicable rules of international law.
Article 1-02: Relationship with other international treaties.
The Parties confirm the rights and obligations in force between them in accordance with the GATT, the 1980 Montevideo Treaty and other international treaties and agreements ratified by them.


In case of inconsistency between the provisions of the treaties and agreements referred to in paragraph 1 and the provisions of this Agreement, the provisions of this Agreement shall prevail to the extent of the inconsistency.
Article 1-03: Relations between Colombia and Venezuela.
Chapters III, IV, V section A, VI, VIII, IX, XVI and XVIII will not apply between Colombia and Venezuela.


The chapters not included in paragraph 1 will be applied between Colombia and Venezuela, without prejudice to the obligations arising from the legal system of the Cartagena Agreement.


Paragraphs 1 and 2 do not affect the rights that Mexico may have under this Agreement.
Article 1-04: Observance of the Treaty.
Each Party shall ensure, in accordance with its constitutional provisions, compliance with the provisions of this Agreement in its territory at the central or federal, state or departmental, and municipal levels, except in cases where this Agreement provides otherwise.
Article 1-05: Succession of treaties.
Any reference to another international treaty or agreement shall be understood to be made in the same terms to any successor treaty or agreement to which all the Parties are party.
CHAPTER II: General definitions
Article 2-01: Definitions of general application.
For the purposes of this Agreement, unless otherwise specified, it shall be understood as:
good of a Party: national products as understood in the GATT, those goods that the Parties agree upon, and includes originating goods; a good of one Party may incorporate materials from other countries.
Customs Valuation Code: the Agreement Related to the Application of Article VII of the General Agreement on Customs Tariffs and Trade, including its interpretative notes.
Commission: the Administrative Commission established in accordance with article 20-01.
communication: official written communication or notification.
days: continuous, calendar or calendar days.
enterprise: any entity incorporated or organized under applicable law, whether or not for profit and privately or governmentally owned, including partnerships, foundations, companies, branches, trusts, shares, sole proprietorships, joint ventures, or other associations. Nothing in this Agreement shall be construed as obligating a Party to grant or recognize legal personality to entities that do not have legal personality under that Party's law.
state enterprise: an enterprise that is owned or controlled by a Party through equity participation.
existing: existing on the date of entry into force of this Agreement.
import tax: any import levy or duty and any charge of any kind applied in connection with the importation of goods, including any form of taxation or additional charge on imports, except:
a) any charge equivalent to an internal tax established in accordance with Article III:2 of the GATT with respect to like goods, direct competitors or substitutes of the Party, or with respect to goods from which it has been manufactured or produced in whole or in part the imported good;

b) any anti-dumping duty or quota or countervailing duty that is applied in accordance with the laws of a Party;

c) any duty or other charge related to importation, proportional to the cost of the services rendered; Y

d) any premium offered or collected on imported goods, derived from any bidding system, regarding the administration of quantitative restrictions on imports or tariffs-quota or tariff preference quotas.
measure: any law, regulation, procedure, administrative provision or practice, among others, adopted by a Party.
national: a physical or natural person who has the nationality of a Party under its law. It shall be understood that the term also extends to persons who, in accordance with the legislation of that Party, have the status of permanent residents in its territory.
originating: that complies with the rules of origin established in Chapter VI.
Party: any State for which this Treaty has entered into force.
Exporting Party: The Party from whose territory a good or service is exported.
Importing Party: The Party into whose territory a good or service is imported.
person: a physical or natural person, or a company.
Reduction Program: the one established in annex 1 to article 3-04.
Protocol: a protocol annexed to this Agreement, the provisions of which have the same hierarchy and binding force as those of this Agreement.
resolution: decision or resolution of an authority.
Harmonized System: the Harmonized Commodity Designation and Coding System, including the General Classification Rules and their explanatory notes.
CHAPTER III: National treatment and market access for goods
Section A - Definitions
Article 3-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, the following shall be understood as:
FOB: free on board (LAB).
tariff fraction: an eight- or ten-digit Harmonized System tariff classification code.
samples with no commercial value: goods representative of a class of goods already produced or of a model of goods whose production is projected. It does not include identical goods imported by the same person or sent to a single consignee in such quantity that, taken globally, they constitute an ordinary import subject to the payment of import taxes.
used: those goods that at the time of import show signs of wear or tarnish due to use; those that, even without having been used, have a considerable time since their manufacture; balances, imperfect, second and waste.
Section B - Scope of application and national treatment
Article 3-02: Scope of application.
This Chapter applies to the trade in goods of the Parties, except as otherwise provided in this Agreement.
Article 3-03: National Treatment.
Each Party shall grant national treatment to the goods of another Party in accordance with Article III of the GATT, including its interpretative notes. For this purpose, Article III of the GATT and its interpretative notes are incorporated into this Agreement and are an integral part thereof.
The provisions of paragraph 1 mean, with respect to a state or department, or a municipality, a treatment no less favorable than the most favorable treatment that that state or department, or municipality grants to any similar goods, direct competitors or substitutes, as the case may be. of the Party of which it is a member.
Paragraphs 1 and 2 do not apply to the measures listed in the annex to this article.
Section C - Import Taxes
Article 3-04: Deduction of import taxes.
Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, neither Party may increase any existing import tax, or adopt any new import tax, on originating goods.
Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, each Party shall progressively eliminate its import taxes on originating goods in accordance with the provisions of Annex 1 to this Article.
Paragraphs 1 and 2 of this article are not intended to:
(a) prohibit a Party from increasing an import tax on originating goods to a level no higher than that established in the Reduction Schedule, when previously that Party had unilaterally reduced that import tax to a level lower than that established in that schedule;
(b) prevent a Party from increasing an import tax on originating goods when that increase is authorized as a result of a GATT dispute settlement procedure between those Parties.
(c) prevent a Party from creating a new tariff breakdown or split, provided that the import tax applicable to the corresponding originating goods is not greater than that applicable to the broken or split tariff code.
Unless otherwise provided, this Agreement incorporates the previously negotiated tariff preferences between the Parties, the regional tariff preference (PAR) for the tariff universe and the extension of the PAR between Mexico and Venezuela, as reflected in the Agreement. annex 1 to this article. As of the entry into force of this Agreement, the preferences previously negotiated or granted between the Parties within the framework of ALADI shall be without effect.
For purposes of deducting import taxes in accordance with this article, the transition tariff rates or tariffs will be approximated downwards, at least to the nearest tenth of a percent or, if the tariff rate is expressed in monetary units, at least least to the nearest .001 of the official monetary unit of the Party.
In addition to the provisions of Annex 2 to this Article, at the request of any Party, the Commission will hold consultations to examine the possibility of accelerating the deduction of import taxes for one or more goods or of including one or more goods in the Program of Deduction and will make the pertinent recommendations to the Parties. Once the corresponding legal requirements have been met, the accelerated relief of import taxes on a good that is achieved for two or more Parties will prevail over any import tax or relief period for that good between those Parties. The inclusion of assets in the Reduction Program that is achieved between two or more Parties will begin to govern those assets between those Parties once the corresponding legal procedures are fulfilled.
Article 3-05 : Customs valuation.
Except as provided in the annex to this article, the customs value of an imported good shall be determined in accordance with the principles of the Customs Valuation Code.
The taxable base on which import taxes will be applied to goods imported from another Party shall not be the value of a good produced in the territory of the importing Party, nor an arbitrary or fictitious value.
In accordance with article 13 of the Customs Valuation Code, if in the course of determining the customs value of imported goods it is necessary to delay the final determination of that value, the importer may withdraw them from customs if, when so requires, provides sufficient security in the form of a bond or, if the importer so chooses, by other means of security provided by the law of the Party. The guarantee will cover the payment of taxes to which the goods may ultimately be subject.
Each Party will establish the appropriate documentation to prove that the customs value is correct, which will not be greater than what can reasonably be requested to comply with the provisions of Article VII of the GATT.
The guarantee granted under the terms of paragraph 3 will be released within a period not to exceed twenty business days from the date on which the importer delivers the appropriate documentation to the customs authority, unless the customs authority itself has initiated the exercise of their powers of verification or verification.
Each Party may determine, in accordance with paragraph 3, the goods imported from another Party that will be subject to the aforementioned guarantee when the customs value declared by the importer is less than the estimated price determined by the customs authority of the importing Party with based on antecedents of transaction values ​​previously obtained and analyzed.
Before adopting the estimated price referred to in paragraph 6, the Party shall communicate to the other Parties the description of the good, its tariff fraction, the estimated price that it intends to establish and the reasons on which it is based to adopt the measure.
The Parties understand that the estimated price referred to in paragraph 6 shall not be considered as the base price for the determination of import taxes.
Article 3-06: Temporary importation of goods.
Each Party shall authorize the temporary importation free of import tax or with suspension of payment thereof, at least for the goods listed below, which are imported from another Party, regardless of their origin and whether they are in the territory of the Party importer similar goods, direct competitors or substitutes are available:
a) professional equipment necessary for the exercise of the activity, trade or profession of a business person;
b) equipment for the press or for the broadcast of radio or television signals and cinematographic equipment;
c) goods imported for sporting purposes or intended for exhibition or demonstration, including components, auxiliary devices and accessories; Y
d) commercial samples and publicity films.
Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, each Party may subject the temporary importation free of import tax or with suspension of payment thereof, of a good of the type indicated in paragraph 1, literals a), b) or c), to any of the following conditions, without additional conditions being able to be adopted:
a) that are introduced by natural or legal persons legally established in the Party, or by nationals of another Party;
b) that the property is used exclusively by the person who enters temporarily or under his personal supervision, in the performance of his activity, trade or profession;
c) that the property is not sold or leased or transferred in any other way while it remains in its territory;
d) that the temporary importation is guaranteed by a bond or other guarantee that does not exceed 110% of the charges that would be caused by the final importation of the good, which will be released at the time of re-exportation;
e) that the good is susceptible to identification when re-exported;
f) that the good is re-exported upon departure of the person or within a term that reasonably corresponds to the purpose of the temporary importation, which may not exceed in any case six months extendable to nine months;
g) that the good is imported in quantities not greater than what is reasonable according to the intended use; Y
h) that the good is re-exported in the same form in which it was imported.
Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, the Parties may subject the temporary importation free of import tax or with suspension of payment thereof, of a good of the type indicated in paragraph 1, literal d) to any of the following conditions , without the possibility of adopting additional conditions:
a) that the good is imported only for the purpose of obtaining orders for goods or services that are supplied from the territory of another Party or from another country that is not a Party;
b) that the property is not subject to sale or lease and is used only for demonstration or exhibition while it remains in its territory;
c) that the good is susceptible to identification when re-exported;
d) that the good be re-exported within a term that reasonably corresponds to the purpose of temporary importation, which may not exceed in any case six months, extendable to nine months; Y
e) that the good is imported in quantities not greater than what is reasonable according to the intended use.
When a good that is imported temporarily free of import duty pursuant to paragraph 1 fails to meet any of the conditions that a Party imposes pursuant to paragraphs 2 and 3, that Party may require payment of import duty and any other charge that would be caused by the definitive importation of the good.
Article 3-07 : Import of samples without commercial value.
Each Party shall authorize the importation free of import duty of samples without commercial value originating from another Party.
Article 3-08: Temporary flexibility levels for certain goods classified in chapters 51 to 63 of the Harmonized System
Until December 31, 1999, the Parties indicated in the annex to this article shall grant to goods classified in chapters 51 to 63 of the Harmonized System that comply with the provisions of article 6-19, the preferential treatment corresponding to originating goods established in the Reduction Program, in accordance with the provisions of that annex.
Section D - Non-tariff measures
Article 3-09: Import and export restrictions.
Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, neither Party may adopt or maintain any prohibition or restriction on the importation of any good of another Party or on the export or sale for export of any good destined for the territory of another Party, except as provided in GATT Article XI, including its interpretative notes. For this purpose, Article XI of the GATT and its interpretative notes are incorporated into this Agreement and are an integral part thereof.
The Parties understand that the rights and obligations of the GATT incorporated in paragraph 1 prohibit, in all circumstances in which any other type of restriction exists, the establishment of minimum export and import prices, except as permitted for the application of sanctions and commitments regarding antidumping duties and quotas or countervailing duties.
In cases where a Party adopts or maintains a prohibition or restriction on the import of goods from a non-Party or on the export of goods destined for a non-Party, nothing in this Agreement shall be construed in the sense of preventing:
a) limit or prohibit the importation of the goods of the country that is not a Party, from the territory of another Party; either
b) require as a condition for the export of goods to the territory of another Party, that they not be directly or indirectly re-exported to the country that is not a Party, without being processed or manufactured in the territory of the other Party in a way that gives rise to a substantial change in the value, form or use thereof or to the production of another good.
In the event that a Party adopts or maintains a prohibition or restriction on the importation of a good from a country that is not a Party, at the request of either Party, they shall consult in order to minimize undue interference or distortion in the pricing, marketing and distribution mechanisms in another Party.
Paragraphs 1 to 4 shall not apply to the measures set out in the annex to this article.
Article 3-10: Customs duties.
Neither Party shall increase or establish any customs duty for the service provided by customs on originating goods and shall eliminate such duties on originating goods within 5 and a half years after the entry into force of this Agreement.
Article 3-11: Export taxes.
Except as provided in this Article, no Party shall adopt or maintain any tax, levy or charge on the export of a good to the territory of another Party, unless they are adopted or maintained on the export of that good to the territory of all other Parties. , and that good, when it is destined for internal consumption.
Each Party may maintain or adopt any tax, levy or charge on the export of the essential goods listed in Annex 1 to this Article, their ingredients, or the goods from which these food products are derived, if such tax , lien or charge is adopted or maintained for the export of those goods to the territory of all other Parties, and is used:
a) so that the benefits of a domestic food assistance program that includes such food are received only by consumers in the Party applying that program; either
b) to ensure the availability of sufficient quantities of the food good for internal consumption, or of sufficient quantities of its ingredients or of the goods from which those food goods are derived for a national processing industry, when the internal price of that food good is maintained below the world price as part of a government stabilization program, provided that such taxes, levies or charges do not have the effect of increasing the protection granted to that national industry, and are maintained only for the period necessary to maintain the integrity of that program.
Notwithstanding paragraph 1, each Party may adopt or maintain a tax, levy or charge on the export of any food good to the territory of another Party if such tax, levy or charge is applied temporarily to alleviate a critical shortage of that nutritional good. For purposes of this paragraph, "temporarily" means up to one year, or a longer period agreed by all Parties.
Paragraph 1 shall not apply to the measures set out in Annex 2 to this Article.
Article 3-12: Marking of country of origin.
The annex to this article shall apply to measures related to country of origin marking.
Section E - Publication and communication
Article 3-13: Publication and communication.
Neither Party shall apply before its official publication any measure of a general nature that has the effect of increasing an import tax or other charge on the importation of goods from another Party or the exportation of goods destined for another Party, or that imposes a new or most burdensome measure, restriction or prohibition for the aforementioned imports or exports or for the transfers of funds related to them.
At the request of one Party, another Party will identify, in terms of the tariff fractions and the nomenclature that corresponds to them in accordance with the Harmonized System, the measures, restrictions or prohibitions on the import or export of goods for reasons of national security, public health, preservation flora or fauna, the environment, phytosanitary and zoosanitary standards, technical standards, labeling, international commitments, public order requirements or any other regulation.
CHAPTER III: National treatment and market access for goods
Annex to Article 3-03: Exceptions to Article 3-03
Colombian Measures
Notwithstanding the provisions of article 3-03, Colombia reserves the departmental monopoly on the production of liquors and the faculty of the departments to establish taxes on the importation of liquors from other departments or countries.
Article 3-03 shall not apply to measures adopted by Colombia regarding the export or import of energy goods when they are necessary to ensure compliance with a constitutional provision.
For the purposes of paragraph 2, those described in paragraph 2 of Section B of the annex to article 3-09 are considered as energy goods.
Annex 1 to article 3-04: Tax Reduction Program
Except as otherwise provided in this Annex or elsewhere in this Agreement, each Party shall progressively eliminate its import taxes on originating goods in ten equal stages, as follows:
a) the first reduction will take place on January 1, 1995; Y
b) the residual import tax will be eliminated in nine equal annual stages as of July 1, 1996, so that these goods will be free of import tax as of July 1, 2004.
The rebate described in paragraph 1 shall be applied from the import tax that is specified in the "base rate" column of the list of each Party in the Rebate Schedule.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 1 and unless otherwise provided in this Agreement, the import tax applicable to originating goods included in a tariff item marked with the code "P" in the schedule of a Party to the Program of Deduction will be the lesser of:
a) the import tax resulting from applying paragraphs 1 and 2; either
b) 4.4% ad valorem .
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 1 and unless otherwise provided in this Agreement, the import tax applicable to originating goods included in a tariff item marked with the code "R" in the schedule of a Party to the Program of Deduction will be the lesser of:
a) the import tax resulting from applying paragraphs 1 and 2 from an import tax of 10% ad-valorem ; either
b) the import tax specified in the "base rate" column.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 1 and unless otherwise provided in this Agreement, the import tax applicable to originating goods included in a tariff item marked with the code "B" in the schedule of a Party in the Program of Tax relief will be eliminated in five equal stages according to the following:
a) the first reduction will take place on January 1, 1995; Y
b) the residual import tax will be eliminated in four equal annual stages beginning on July 1, 1996, so that these goods will be free of import tax as of July 1, 1999.
Notwithstanding Article 3-04 and paragraphs 1 and 2, and in accordance with Article 5-04 and Annex 2 to Article 3-04, a Party may adopt or maintain import taxes in accordance with its obligations. and rights derived from GATT, on the goods included in a tariff fraction identified with the code "EXCL" in the list of a Party in the Reduction Program until the moment in which the contrary is agreed between the Parties in accordance with the provisions of this Treaty. For goods included in a tariff item identified with the code "EXCL" and which, according to the list of a Party in the Reduction Program and paragraph 7, is not identified with the code "PAR",
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 6, the following shall apply to originating goods included in a tariff item identified with the code "PAR" in the list of a Party in the Tariff Reduction Program:
a) Mexico will apply a tariff preference of 28% on that proportion of the current import tax that is expressed as a percentage of the customs value of the imported good ( ad-valorem ), but in no case on that proportion of the current import tax that is Express in monetary units per unit of measure; either
b) Colombia and Venezuela will apply a tariff preference of 12% on that proportion of the current import tax that is expressed as a percentage of the customs value of the imported good ( ad-valorem ), but in no case on that proportion of the current import tax that is expressed in monetary units per unit of measure.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 1 and unless otherwise provided in this Agreement, the import tax on originating automotive goods included in the tariff headings marked with the code "M" in the list of a Party in the Program of Deduction will be applied according to the following:
a) before December 31, 2006, as long as there is no agreement in the Automotive Sector Committee in accordance with chapter IV, the import tax applicable to originating goods will be the one specified in the base rate column or, if it exists, the specified in parentheses after the "M" code for each tariff item in the schedule of a Party to the Reduction Schedule;
b) before December 31, 2006 and after, where appropriate, there is an agreement in the Automotive Sector Committee in accordance with chapter IV, the import tax applicable to originating goods will be eliminated in equal annual stages between the date after December 1 § January 1997 determined by that Committee and December 31, 2006, from the base rate specified for each tariff fraction in the "base rate" column of the list of a Party in the Reduction Program; Y
c) As of January 1, 2007, these goods shall be free of import tax, unless the Parties agree to a longer period pursuant to Article 4-04.
The provisions of paragraph 8 shall not apply to originating goods that are not automotive goods.
Notwithstanding the provisions of Chapter VI, in cases where there is no equal tariff treatment between the Parties for the same originating good, in order to determine the import tax applicable by a Party, the following shall apply:
a) Colombia will apply the provisions of this annex in accordance with its list in the Tax Reduction Program to originating goods for which the last substantial production process, other than minor processing, has been carried out in the territory of Mexico.
b) Venezuela will apply the provisions of this annex in accordance with its list in the Reduction Program to originating goods for which the last substantial production process, other than minor processing, has been carried out in the territory of Mexico.
c) Mexico will apply the provisions of this annex in accordance with the "Colombia" column of its list in the Tariff Reduction Program to originating goods for which the last substantial production process, other than processing, has been carried out in the territory of Colombia. minor.
d) Mexico will apply the provisions of this annex in accordance with the "Venezuela" column of its list in the Tariff Reduction Program to originating goods for which the last substantial production process, other than processing, has been carried out in the territory of Venezuela. minor.
For the purposes of paragraph 10, minor processing will include, among others, the following:
a) simple dilution in water or another substance that does not materially alter the characteristics of the good;
b) cleaning, including removal of rust, grease, paint or other coatings;
c) application of preservative or decorative coatings, including lubricants, preservative or decorative paint, or metallic coatings;
d) trimming or roughing small amounts of excess materials;
e) unloading, loading or any other operation necessary to keep the good in good condition;
f) packaging, repackaging, packaging, repackaging or filling of containers in small doses;
g) test, mark, separate, or classify;
h) ornamental or finishing operations incidental to the production of a textile good, the purpose of which is to improve the commercial appeal or ease of care of a product, such as dyeing and printing, embroidery and application of engravings or markings, hemming, pleats or darts, stone or acid wash, permanent press, or sew-on accessories and ornaments;
For the purposes of paragraph 10, production shall be understood as established in article 6-01.
