export subsidy:
a) the granting, by a government or a public body, to a branch of production, to producers of a good in the agricultural sector, to a cooperative or other association of such producers, to a marketing council or to any other type of company, direct subsidies, including payments in kind, subject to export performance;
b) the sale or placement for export, by a government or by a public body, of non-commercial stocks of goods from the agricultural sector at a price lower than the comparable price charged for a similar good to buyers in the domestic market;
c) payments for the export of goods in the agricultural sector financed by virtue of government measures, regardless of whether or not such payments imply a charge in the public budget, including those financed from income derived from a lien imposed on the property of the agricultural sector in question or to the good of the agricultural sector from which the exported good is obtained;
d) the granting of subsidies to reduce the marketing costs of exports of goods from the agricultural sector, except generally available services in the area of ​​export promotion and advice, including handling costs, and the costs of international transport and freight ;
e) the costs of transportation and internal freight of export shipments, established or imposed by a government in more favorable terms than for internal shipments; either
f) subsidies for goods in the agricultural sector subject to their incorporation into exported goods.
Article 5-02: Scope of application.
This section applies to measures adopted or maintained by a Party related to trade in goods from the agricultural sector.
In the event of any inconsistency between any provision of this section and any other provision of this Agreement, the provisions of this section shall control to the extent of the inconsistency.
Article 5-03: Intergovernmental Agreements.
A Party, before adopting a measure under an intergovernmental agreement on an agricultural sector good under GATT Article XX(h) that may affect trade in an agricultural sector good between the Parties, shall consult with the other Parties to avoid the annulment or impairment of a concession granted by that Party in its Reduction Schedule.
Article 5-04: Access to markets.
The Parties will facilitate access to their respective markets by reducing or eliminating import and export barriers in the reciprocal trade of goods from the agricultural sector, such as: import restrictions, import taxes, and technical and quality standards. agricultural marketing.
The Parties renounce the use of quantitative restrictions on imports, price bands or price stabilization mechanisms and variable tariffs for the goods included in the Tariff Reduction Program in their reciprocal trade, without prejudice to the provisions of Annex 1 to this article.
The Parties exempt from the Reduction Program the goods of the agricultural sector in accordance with annex 2 to this article.
Once a year from the entry into force of this Agreement, the Agricultural Trade Committee established in article 5-10, will review the possibility of incorporating into the Reduction Program the goods of the agricultural sector contained in annex 2 to this article. and will make the pertinent recommendations to the Parties. This incorporation can be done in accordance with the methodologies described in Annex 1 to this article.
The trade of goods included in annexes 3 and 4 to this article will be governed by the provisions of the same.
Article 5-05: Special Safeguards.
Mexico and Venezuela may, according to their list contained in the Reduction Program, maintain or adopt a special safeguard in the form of tariffs-quota on a good of the agricultural sector that is included in their section of the annex to this article. Notwithstanding the provisions of Article 3-04, a Party may not apply a duty rate or tariff on the excess quota under a special safeguard that exceeds the lesser of the following:
a) the most favored nation rate or tariff in effect at the entry into force of this Agreement; Y
b) the most favored nation rate or tariff prevailing at that time.
With respect to the same good of the agricultural sector and to the same Party, no Party may simultaneously apply a rate or tariff rate on the surplus of the quota in accordance with paragraph 1 and adopt a safeguard measure provided for in Chapter VIII.
Article 5-06: Refund of import taxes on products exported in identical or similar conditions.
As of the date of entry into force of this Agreement, neither Party may refund the amount of import taxes paid, nor exempt or reduce the amount of import taxes owed, in relation to any good of the agricultural sector imported into its territory that is:
a) replaced by a good of the agricultural sector of that Party, identical or similar, subsequently exported to the territory of another Party;
b) substituted by a good of the agricultural sector of that Party, identical or similar used as a material in the production of another good subsequently exported to the territory of another Party.
Article 5-07: Internal Support Measures.
The Parties recognize the existence of internal support measures for the agricultural sector and that these measures can distort trade and affect production. In addition, they recognize that commitments on the reduction of internal support may arise in the multilateral negotiations on agriculture within the framework of the GATT. Therefore, when a Party decides to support its agricultural producers, it shall endeavor to move towards domestic support policies that:
a) have no or minimal distorting effects on trade or production; either
b) are exempt from any commitment to reduce internal support that could be negotiated under the GATT.
Any Party may modify its domestic support measures, including those that may be subject to reduction commitments, in accordance with its rights and obligations under the GATT.
Article 5-08: Export subsidies.
The Parties share the objective of achieving the multilateral elimination of export subsidies for goods in the agricultural sector and will cooperate in the effort to reach agreements within the GATT framework.
The Parties will gradually eliminate export subsidies for agricultural sector goods included in the Reduction Program as follows:
a) from the incorporation into the Tax Reduction Program of a good from the agricultural sector, the Parties may maintain the export subsidy prevailing the year prior to its incorporation for up to three years;
b) from the fourth year after the good of the agricultural sector has been incorporated into the Tax Reduction Program, the corresponding export subsidies will be eliminated in equal stages until they reach zero when the tax relief for that good ends.
Once the tax relief has ended, neither Party may maintain or introduce export subsidies for goods from the agricultural sector in their reciprocal trade. Likewise, the Parties renounce the rights that the GATT confers on them to use export subsidies of goods from the agricultural sector in their reciprocal trade, as well as the rights regarding the use of these subsidies that could result from multilateral negotiations on agricultural matters in the GATT framework.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 2 and 3, a Party may, if so requested by another Party and there is an agreement between both, adopt or maintain an export subsidy for a good in the agricultural sector that is exported to that other Party.
Article 5-09: Technical standards and agricultural marketing.
The Parties create an Agricultural Technical and Marketing Standards Working Group made up of representatives of each of them, which will meet annually or as agreed. The Working Group will review the application and effects of the technical or marketing standards for goods in the agricultural sector that affect trade between the Parties, and will recommend possible solutions to the issues that may arise in relation thereto. This Group will present a report to the Committee on Agricultural Trade after each meeting.
Each Party shall grant to goods imported from another Party a treatment no less favorable than that granted to its goods in the application of technical or commercialization standards to goods of the agricultural sector in the aspects of packaging, grades, quality and size of the goods.
Article 5-10: Committee on Agricultural Trade.
The Parties create a Committee on Agricultural Trade, made up of representatives of each Party.
It will correspond to the Committee:
a) monitoring and fostering cooperation to apply and administer this chapter;
b) the establishment of a forum for the Parties to consult on aspects related to this chapter;
c) submitting an annual report to the Commission on the implementation of this section.
The Committee will meet at least once a year and when so agreed.
Section B - Phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures
Article 5-11: Definitions.
For the purposes of this section, it shall be understood as:
animal: among others, domestic animals, fish and wildlife;
good: animals, plants, their products and by-products.
contaminant: among others, residues of pesticides and veterinary drugs and other foreign substances.
disease: the more or less serious alteration of the animal body.
risk assessment: an assessment of:
a) the probability of introduction, establishment and spread of a pest or disease and the possible biological and economic consequences;
b) the probability of adverse effects to human and animal life or health from the presence of an additive, contaminant, toxin, or disease-causing organism in a food or feed.
scientific information: data or information derived from the use of scientific principles and methods.
phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure: a measure, including a criterion related to the final good; a process or production method directly related to the good; a test, inspection, certification, or approval procedure; a relevant statistical method; a sampling procedure; a risk assessment method; a packaging and labeling requirement directly related to food safety; and a quarantine regime, such as a relevant requirement associated with the transport of animals or plants, or with material necessary for their survival during transport, that a Party adopts, maintains or applies to:
a) protect animal life and health and plant health in its territory from the risks arising from the introduction, establishment or spread of a pest or disease;
b) protect human and animal life and health in their territory from risks arising from the presence of an additive, contaminant, toxin or disease-causing organism in food or feed;
c) protect human life and health in its territory from risks arising from an organism that causes disease or a pest carried by an animal or plant or a derivative thereof; either
d) prevent or limit other damage in its territory from the introduction, establishment and spread of a pest or disease.
adequate level of phytosanitary or zoosanitary protection: the level of protection that the Party that establishes the phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure deems appropriate to protect the life or health of people and animals or to preserve plant health in its territory.
international standard, guideline or recommendation: a standard, guideline or recommendation, relating to:
a) food safety, established by the Codex Alimentarius Commission, including that related to product spoilage, prepared by the Codex Alimentarius Committee on Fish and Fishery Products, food additives, contaminants, hygienic practices and methods analysis and sampling;
b) animal health and zoonoses, prepared under the auspices of the International Office of Epizootics;
c) plant health, prepared under the auspices of the Secretariat of the International Plant Protection Convention; Y
d) what is established by other international organizations agreed upon by the Parties or developed in accordance with those organizations.
pest: without limitation , any living state of any insect, mite, nematode, slug, snail, protozoan, or other invertebrate animal, bacteria, fungus, other parasitic plant or reproductive part thereof, virus, mycoplasma, weed, or any similar organism or the same associated with any of the above or any infectious substance that may directly or indirectly cause damage to plants or animals or their products or by-products.
approval procedure: any registration, communication or any other mandatory administrative procedure.
control or inspection procedure: any procedure used, directly or indirectly, to determine whether a phytosanitary or animal health measure is being complied with, including sampling, testing, inspection, evaluation, verification, monitoring, auditing, evaluation of the application of phytosanitary and animal health measures , accreditation, registration, certification, other procedures that involve the physical examination of a good, its packaging or the equipment or facilities directly related to the production, commercialization or use of the good. Approval procedures are excluded from this definition.
transport: among others, the means of mobilization, the form of packaging and the mode of transportation.
vegetable: among other crops of economic, scientific, medicinal, ornamental and wild flora interest.
zone: a country, part of a country, parts of several countries, or all parts of several countries.
area of ​​low pest or disease prevalence: an area in which a specific pest or disease occurs at low levels.
pest or disease free zone: an area in which a specific pest or disease is not present.
Article 5-12: Scope of application.
In order to establish a framework of disciplines and rules that guide the development, adoption, and compliance of phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures, the provisions of this section apply to any such measure that, when adopted by a direct Party or indirectly, may affect trade between the Parties.
This section applies to measures adopted or maintained by a Party related to trade in goods from the agricultural sector.
In the event of any inconsistency between any provision of this section and any other provision of this Agreement, the provisions of this section shall control to the extent of the inconsistency.
Article 5-13: Right to adopt phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures.
Each Party may, in accordance with this section, adopt, apply or maintain any phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure necessary for the protection of human, animal and plant health and life in its territory. The measure may be stricter than an international standard, guideline or recommendation.
Article 5-14: Right to set the level of protection.
Notwithstanding any other provision of this section, each Party may, in order to protect human, animal and plant health and life, set its appropriate levels of protection, in accordance with the provisions of Article 5-22.
Article 5-15: Scientific principles.
Each Party shall ensure that any phytosanitary or animal health measure it adopts, applies or maintains:
a) is based on scientific principles, taking into account, where appropriate, relevant factors, such as different geographical conditions;
b) is not maintained when there is no longer a scientific basis to support it; Y
c) is based on a risk assessment appropriate to the circumstances that gave rise to it.
Article 5-16: Non-discriminatory treatment.
Each Party shall ensure that a phytosanitary or animal health measure it adopts, applies or maintains does not arbitrarily or unreasonably discriminate between its goods and similar goods of another Party, or between goods of another Party and similar goods of any other country, when phytosanitary conditions exist. or identical or similar animal health.
Article 5-17: Unnecessary obstacles.
Each importing Party shall ensure that any phytosanitary or animal sanitary measure it adopts, applies or maintains is put into practice only to the degree necessary to achieve its appropriate level of protection, taking into account technical and economic feasibility.
Article 5-18: Covert restrictions.
No Party may adopt, apply or maintain any phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure that has the purpose or consequence of creating a disguised restriction on trade between the Parties.
Article 5-19: Action of non-governmental organizations.
Each Party shall ensure that any non-governmental body that it relies on for the application of a phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure acts in a manner consistent with this section.
Article 5-20: International standards and international standardization organizations.
Without reducing the level of protection of human, animal and plant health and life, each Party shall use, as a basis for its phytosanitary or zoosanitary measures, international standards, guidelines or recommendations, in order to make them equivalent or, when corresponds, identical to those of the other Parties.
A phytosanitary or animal health measure of a Party that is equal to an international standard, guideline or recommendation shall be considered consistent with Articles 5-13 to 5-19. A measure by a Party that provides a level of phytosanitary or animal health protection different from that which would be achieved by a measure based on an international standard, guideline or recommendation is not, for that reason alone, considered inconsistent with the provisions of this section.
Nothing in paragraph 1 shall be construed as preventing a Party from adopting, applying, or maintaining, in accordance with the other provisions of this section, a phytosanitary or animal health measure that is stricter than the international standard, guideline, or recommendation. relevant.
When a Party has reason to assume that a phytosanitary or animal health measure of another Party affects or may adversely affect its exports, and the measure is not based on relevant international standards, guidelines or recommendations, it may request to be informed of the reasons for the measure and the other Party will inform in writing within a period of forty days.
Each Party shall participate, to the fullest extent possible, in relevant international standard-setting organizations, including the Codex Alimentarius Commission, the International Office of Epizootics, and the International Plant Protection Convention, for the purpose of promoting the development and periodic review of international standards, guidelines and recommendations.
Article 5-21: Equivalence.
Without reducing the level of protection of human, animal and plant health and life, the Parties shall seek, to the greatest extent possible and in accordance with this section, the equivalence of their respective phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures.
The importing Party:
a) treat a phytosanitary or animal sanitary measure adopted, applied or maintained by an exporting Party as equivalent to its own when the exporting Party, in cooperation with the importing Party, provides it with scientific or other information, in accordance with quality assessment methods; risks agreed by the Parties, to objectively demonstrate, in accordance with subparagraph b), that the measure of the exporting Party achieves the appropriate level of protection of the importing Party;
b) may, when there is a scientific basis for it, determine that the measure of the exporting Party does not reach the level of protection that the importing Party deems appropriate; Y
c) provide the exporting Party in writing, upon request, with its reasons for a finding in accordance with subparagraph b).
For the purpose of establishing equivalence between the measures, the exporting Party, at the request of the importing Party, shall adopt the mechanisms available to it to facilitate access to its territory for purposes of inspection, testing and other pertinent procedures.
The Parties may consider, when developing a phytosanitary or animal health measure, the relevant existing or proposed phytosanitary or animal health measures of the Parties.
Article 5-22: Risk assessment and adequate level of protection.
Each Party shall take into account, when carrying out a risk assessment:
a) relevant risk assessment methods and techniques developed by international standard-setting organizations;
b) relevant scientific information;
c) relevant production, processing, handling and packaging methods;
d) suitable methods of inspection, sampling and testing;
e) the existence of pests or diseases that must be taken into account, including the existence of pest- or disease-free areas, and areas of low prevalence of these, recognized by the Parties;
f) ecological and other environmental conditions that need to be considered; Y
g) the quarantine measures and applicable treatments that satisfy the importing Party, such as quarantines, chemical and physical treatments, destruction, reshipment and others accepted by the Parties.
In addition to paragraph 1, in establishing its appropriate level of protection in relation to the risk associated with the introduction, establishment, or spread of an animal or plant pest or disease, and in assessing the risk, each Party shall also take into account account, where relevant, of the following economic factors:
a) loss of production or sales that could be a consequence of the pest or disease;
b) costs of control or eradication of the pest or disease in its territory; Y
c) the cost-effectiveness of other options to limit risks.
Each Party, in establishing its appropriate level of protection:
a) take into account the objective of minimizing negative effects on trade; Y
b) will avoid, in order to achieve consistency in the practical application of the concept of adequate level of protection, making arbitrary or unjustifiable distinctions, under different circumstances, that may cause arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination against a good of another Party or constitute a disguised restriction on trade between the Parties.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 1 to 3 and Article 5-15, letter c), when carrying out a risk assessment a Party concludes that the corresponding scientific information available or other information is insufficient to After completing the assessment, it may adopt a provisional phytosanitary or animal health measure, based on available pertinent information, such as that from international standard-setting organizations and the other Parties' phytosanitary or animal health measures. The Party shall conclude the evaluation within a period of sixty days from the date sufficient information is presented to it to complete it, review the provisional measure and, when appropriate, modify it.
An importing Party may achieve its appropriate level of protection through the application of phytosanitary and animal health measures immediately or gradually. When the application of this last modality is requested by one Party, the other may grant such application or make specific exceptions, taking into account the export interests of the requesting Party.
Article 5-23: Adaptation to regional conditions.
Each Party shall adapt any of its phytosanitary or zoosanitary measures related to the introduction, establishment or spread of an animal or plant pest or disease, to the phytosanitary or zoosanitary characteristics of the area where a good subject to such measure is produced and the area in which it is produced. its territory to which the good is destined, taking into account the pertinent conditions, including those related to the transportation and handling of cargo between those zones. When evaluating such characteristics of an area, taking into account whether it is an area free of pests or diseases and can be conserved as such, or it is an area with a low prevalence of these, each Party shall take into account, among other factors:
a) the prevalence of pests or diseases in that area;
b) the existence of eradication or control programs in that area; Y
c) any relevant standard, guideline or recommendation.
In addition to the provisions of paragraph 1, each Party, when establishing whether an area is an area free of pests or diseases, or an area of ​​low prevalence of these, shall base its opinion on factors such as geographic conditions, ecosystems, surveillance epidemiological and the effectiveness of phytosanitary or zoosanitary controls in that area.
Each importing Party shall recognize that an area in the territory of the exporting Party is, and may be conserved as, a pest-free or disease-free area or an area of ​​low pest prevalence, where the exporting Party provides the importing Party with scientific or of another class sufficient to demonstrate it to the satisfaction of the importing Party. To this end, each exporting Party shall allow the importing Party, upon request, access to its territory for inspection, testing, and other pertinent procedures.
Each Party, taking into account any relevant conditions, including those related to the transportation and handling of cargo, may, in accordance with this section:
a) adopt, apply or maintain a different risk assessment procedure for an area free of pests or diseases than for an area of ​​low pest or disease prevalence; Y
b) make a different determination for the disposition of a good produced in an area free of pests or diseases than for one produced in an area of ​​low prevalence of these.
When adopting, applying or maintaining a phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure in relation to the introduction, establishment or spread of an animal or plant pest or disease, each Party shall grant to a good obtained in a pest or disease free zone in the territory of another Party , a treatment no less favorable than that granted to a good obtained in an area free of pests or diseases in another country that presents the same level of risk. The Party shall use equivalent risk assessment techniques to assess relevant conditions and controls in the pest or disease free zone and in the area adjacent to that zone, and shall take into account any relevant conditions, including those related to transport and storage. load.
Each importing Party shall seek agreement with the exporting Party, upon request, on specific requirements compliance with which allows a good obtained in an area of ​​low pest or disease prevalence in the territory of an exporting Party to be imported into the territory of the importing Party. .
Article 5-24: Control, inspection and approval procedures.
Each Party, in relation to any control or inspection procedure that it carries out:
a) initiate and conclude the procedure in the most expeditious manner possible and no less favorable for an asset of the other Party than for a similar asset of the Party or of any other country;
b) will publish the normal duration of the procedure or communicate to whoever requests it, the expected duration of the procedure;
c) ensure that the competent body:
i) upon receipt of an application, promptly examine the documentation for completeness and inform the applicant accurately and fully of any insufficiencies;
(ii) as soon as possible, convey to the applicant the results of the procedure accurately and completely, so that the applicant can take any necessary corrective action;
iii) when the request is insufficient, continue, as far as possible, with the procedure if the requester so requests; Y
iv) report, at the request of the applicant, on the status of the application and the reasons for any delay;
d) limit the information that the applicant must present to that necessary to carry out the procedure;
e) will grant to the confidential or reserved information that derives from the conduct of the procedure for an asset of the other Party or that is presented in relation to it:
i) treatment no less favorable than for an asset of the Party; Y
(ii) in any case, treatment that protects the legitimate business interests of the applicant to the extent provided by the law of that Party;
f) limit to what is reasonable or necessary any requirement regarding individual specimens or samples of a property;
g) by carrying out the procedure, it shall not impose a duty that is greater for a good of another Party than is equitable in relation to any duty it charges on its own goods or on the goods of any other country, taking into account the costs communication, transportation and other related costs;
h) will use criteria to select the location of the facilities where the procedure is carried out, in such a way that it does not cause inconvenience to an applicant or his representative;
i) use criteria to select samples of goods that do not cause unnecessary inconvenience to an applicant or his representative; Y
j) in the case of a good that has been modified after the determination that it complies with the requirements of the applicable phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure, it will limit the procedure to what is necessary to establish that it continues to comply with the requirements of that measure.
When a phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure of the importing Party requires carrying out a control or inspection procedure at the production stage, the exporting Party shall adopt, at the request of the importing Party, the measures available to facilitate access to its territory and shall provide the necessary assistance to facilitate the importing Party to carry out its control or inspection procedure.
The Parties will apply, with the necessary modifications, regarding their approval procedures, the pertinent provisions of paragraph 1, letters a) to h).
An importing Party that maintains an approval procedure may require that its authorization for the use of an additive, or the establishment of a tolerance level for a contaminant in a food or feed, be obtained in accordance with that procedure, before granting approval. access to their domestic market to a food or feed that contains that additive or contaminant. When that Party so requires, it may authorize a relevant international standard, guideline or recommendation, as a basis for granting access to such assets until it completes the procedure.
Article 5-25: Communication, publication and provision of information.
When proposing the adoption or modification of a phytosanitary or animal health measure of general application in their respective territories, each Party:
a) at least 60 days in advance, publish a notice and communicate to the other Parties of its intention to adopt or modify that measure, when it is not a law, and publish and provide to the other Parties the full text of the proposed measure, in a way that allows interested parties to become familiar with the proposal;
b) will identify in the notice and in the communication the good to which the measure would be applied, and will include a brief description of the objective and the reasons for it;
c) provide a copy of the proposed measure to any Party or any interested party that so requests and, where possible, identify any provision that deviates materially from relevant international standards, guidelines or recommendations; Y
d) without discrimination, allow other Parties and interested persons to make comments in writing and, upon request, discuss them and take into account the results of those discussions.
Through appropriate measures, each Party shall seek to ensure, with respect to any phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure of a competent authority of a state or department, or of a municipality of that Party:
a) That the notice and communication of the type required in paragraph 1, literals a) and b) be made at an appropriate initial stage, prior to its adoption; Y
b) that the provisions of paragraph 1, letters c) and d) be observed.
When a Party considers it necessary to address an urgent problem related to plant or animal health protection, it may omit any of the steps set out in paragraphs 1 or 2 provided that, once a phytosanitary or animal health measure has been adopted:
a) notify the other Parties immediately, in accordance with the requirements established in paragraph 1, letter b), including a brief description of the emergency;
b) deliver a copy of the measure to any of the Parties or interested parties who so request; Y
c) allow, without discrimination, the other Parties and interested parties to submit comments in writing and, upon request, discuss them and take into account the results of those discussions.
Each Party shall allow, except when necessary to deal with an urgent problem referred to in paragraph 3, a reasonable period of time to elapse between the publication of a phytosanitary or animal sanitary measure of general application and the date of its entry into force, with the in order to allow time for the interested parties to adapt to the measure.
Each Party shall designate a governmental authority responsible for the implementation, in its territory, of the communication provisions of this article and shall communicate it to the other Parties. When a Party designates two or more government authorities for this purpose, it shall provide the other Parties with complete and unambiguous information on the scope of responsibilities of those authorities.
When an importing Party denies entry into its territory to a good of another Party because it does not comply with a phytosanitary or animal health measure, the importing Party shall provide, upon request, a written explanation to the exporting Party, identifying the corresponding measure. as well as the reasons why the good does not comply with that measure.
Article 5-26: Information centers.
Each Party shall ensure that there is at least one information center capable of answering all reasonable questions from the other Parties and interested parties, as well as providing relevant documentation in relation to:
a) any phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure of general application, including any control or inspection procedure, or approval, proposed, adopted or maintained in its territory;
b) the Party's risk assessment processes and the factors it takes into consideration in conducting the assessment and in establishing its appropriate level of protection;
c) the Party's membership and participation in international and regional phytosanitary and animal health agencies and systems, and in bilateral and multilateral agreements within the scope of this section, as well as the provisions of those agencies, systems, or agreements; Y
d) the location of notices published pursuant to this section, or where such information may be obtained.
Each Party shall ensure that, in accordance with the provisions of this section, when another Party or an interested party requests copies of documents, they are provided at a price no higher than their internal sale price, in addition to the cost of shipping.
Article 5-27: Technical cooperation.
Each Party, at the request of another Party, shall facilitate the provision of technical advice, information and assistance, under mutually agreed terms and conditions, to strengthen phytosanitary and animal health measures and related activities with that other Party, including research, processing technologies, infrastructure and the establishment of national regulatory bodies. Such assistance may include credits, grants, and funds for the acquisition of technical skills, training, and equipment that will facilitate the Party's adjustment to and compliance with a Party's phytosanitary or animal health measure.
Each Party, at the request of another Party:
a) provide that Party with information on its technical cooperation programs concerning phytosanitary or zoosanitary measures in areas of particular interest; Y
b) may consult with that Party, during the elaboration of any phytosanitary or zoosanitary measure, or prior to the adoption of that measure or a change in its application.
Article 5-28: Limitations on the provision of information.
Nothing in this section shall be construed to require a Party to provide any information the disclosure of which it believes would impede compliance with its laws, be contrary to the public interest, or be detrimental to any legitimate business interest.
Article 5-29: Committee on Phytosanitary and Zoosanitary Measures.
The Parties create a Committee on Phytosanitary and Zoosanitary Measures, made up of representatives of each Party with responsibilities in phytosanitary and zoosanitary matters.
Each Party, when designating its representatives, will communicate it to the other Parties. When a Party designates more than one representative for this purpose, it shall provide the other Parties with complete and unambiguous information on the scope of responsibilities of those representatives.
The Committee will facilitate and encourage:
a) expedited consultations on specific phytosanitary or animal health matters;
b) the activities of the Parties in accordance with the provisions of this section, particularly the provisions of Articles 5-20 and 5-21;
c) technical cooperation between the Parties, including cooperation in the development, application and enforcement of phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures; Y
d) improvement of phytosanitary and zoosanitary conditions in the territory of the Parties.
The committee:
a) seek, to the greatest extent possible, the assistance of relevant international standard-setting organizations, in order to obtain available scientific and technical advice and to minimize duplication of effort in the exercise of its functions;
b) may establish the modalities, which it deems appropriate, for the coordination and expeditious solution of matters that are referred to it, among others:
i) draw on experts and expert organizations; Y
ii) establish working groups and determine their objectives and fields of action;
c) will comply with the instructions of the Commission;
d) report annually to the Commission on the application of this section; Y
e) will meet at least once a year, unless otherwise agreed.
Article 5-30: Technical consultations.
A Party may request consultations with another Party on any issue covered by this section.
Each Party may use the good offices of relevant international standard-setting organizations, including those mentioned in Article 5-20, for advice and assistance on phytosanitary and animal health matters within the framework of their respective mandates.
A Party that asserts that a phytosanitary or animal sanitary measure of another Party is inconsistent with this section will have to prove that inconsistency.
When the Parties involved have resorted to consultations facilitated by the Committee, they will constitute, if they so agree, the consultations provided for in Chapter XIX.
Annex 1 to article 5-04: Methodology for the incorporation of goods from the agricultural sector to the Tax Reduction Program.
For the goods of the agricultural sector described in paragraph 1 of annex 2 to article 5-04 that, at the time of the meetings provided for in article 5-04, paragraph 4, are subject to a prior import license or permit in Colombia or Mexico , the Tariff Reduction Program for Colombia and Mexico may be developed through a tariffication methodology in which a minimum access and an equivalent tariff are negotiated. The tax relief term of the latter may not exceed ten years from the incorporation of the asset to the Tax Relief Program.
Notwithstanding the provisions of the preceding paragraph:
a) If Mexico tariffifies a good in the agricultural sector on the basis of the most favored nation in the GATT after having incorporated it into the Tariff Elimination Program, Colombia and Venezuela will be entitled to the best treatment between the most favored nation in the GATT and the one that these countries have agreed to the incorporation made in accordance with paragraph 1;
b) If Colombia tariffifies a good in the agricultural sector on the basis of the most favored nation in the GATT after having incorporated it into the Tariff Elimination Program, Mexico will be entitled to the best treatment between the most favored nation in the GATT and the one that this country has. according to the incorporation made pursuant to paragraph 1.
If a good of the agricultural sector included in paragraph 1, of annex 2 to article 5-04, is tariffied prior to the meetings provided for in article 5-04, paragraph 4 on the basis of the most favored nation rate or tariff in the GATT, its incorporation into the Tariff Reduction Program in this Agreement will be done as follows:
a) In the case of prior import permits from Mexico, by negotiating a minimum access and an equivalent tariff for Colombia and Venezuela and a reduction that does not exceed ten years from the incorporation of the good into the Reduction Program ;
b) In the case of prior import licenses from Colombia, by negotiating a minimum access and an equivalent tariff for Mexico and a reduction that does not exceed ten years from the date of incorporation into the Reduction Program.
For the goods of the agricultural sector included in paragraph 2, of annex 2, to article 5-04 that, at the time of the meetings provided for in article 5-04, paragraph 4, are subject to price bands or price stabilization programs In Colombia and Venezuela, the Tax Reduction Program for Colombia and Venezuela with respect to Mexico may be developed through the total reduction of both the rate or tariff applicable to the most favored nation for that good of the agricultural sector at the time of its incorporation into the Program of Deduction, such as the variable tariff rate or tariff applicable according to the stabilization system in force in Colombia and Venezuela on the date of entry into force of this Agreement.The reduction will be made in a term not to exceed ten years from the incorporation of the asset to the Reduction Program.
If a good of the agricultural sector included in paragraph 2 of annex 2 to article 5-04, is tariffied on the basis of the most favored nation rate or tariff in the GATT, prior to the meetings provided for in article 5-04 , paragraph 4, its incorporation into the Reduction Program will be made using the most favored nation rate or tariff applicable the day prior to tariffication and the average of the variable tariff rates or tariffs applicable during the sixty months prior to tariffication or, if their validity is less, during the term that they have been applicable in Colombia and Venezuela prior to the tariffication, through a reduction that does not exceed ten years from the incorporation of the good to the Reduction Program.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 5, if at the time of the incorporation of a good of the agricultural sector in the Tariff Reduction Program, the treatment that results from the tariffication that has been carried out in accordance with paragraph 5, turns out to be a better treatment for Mexico than the mechanism provided in paragraph 4, Mexico will be entitled to the rate or tariff resulting from the tariffication which will be eliminated through a reduction that does not exceed ten years from the incorporation of the good to the Reduction Program.
For the goods of the agricultural sector included in paragraph 3, of annex 2 to article 5-04, the Reduction Program will be applied by means of the elimination of the import tax, immediately or in a term that does not exceed ten years from from the date on which it is incorporated into the Tax Reduction Program. The Party that incorporates the good into the Reduction Program, prior agreement between the Parties, may make use of a tariff-quota type safeguard, as long as it does not exceed ten years. The quota will be subject to the import tax that would correspond to it according to the Reduction Program. The excess of the quota will be subject to an import tax that will not exceed the most favored nation rate or tariff applicable for that good of the agricultural sector,
In any case, for the goods subject to a prior import license in Colombia included in the Colombian list in paragraph 1 of annex 2 to article 5-04, their incorporation into the Reduction Program may only be done in accordance with paragraph 1 or 3.
The Parties shall establish the rules of origin for the goods of the agricultural sector described in Annex 2 to Article 5-04, at the time of their incorporation into the Reduction Program.
Annex 2 to article 5-04: Assets Excluded from the Reduction Program.
Notwithstanding any other provision of this Agreement, Colombia and Mexico may maintain their prior import licenses or permits for the following goods in the agricultural sector:
Prior permits from Mexico

Annex 3 to Article 5-04: Trade in sugar
The Parties create a Sugar Analysis Committee made up of the Secretary of Commerce and Industrial Development and the Secretary of Agriculture and Hydraulic Resources on behalf of Mexico, by the Minister of Agriculture and the Minister of Foreign Trade on the part of Colombia and by the Minister of Agriculture and Breeding and the President of the Institute of Foreign Trade on behalf of Venezuela or by whom they designate. Its function will be to seek an agreement by consensus on sugar trade between the Parties.
The Committee will seek, within the six months following the entry into force of this Agreement, to define the participation of sugar originating in and coming from Colombia and Venezuela in the tariff-quota that Mexico undertakes, in case of agreement by consensus in the Committee, to be adopted within the two years following the entry into force of this Treaty. The Committee will also define the mechanism by which sugar originating in and coming from Mexico will participate in the Colombian and Venezuelan markets, respectively.
The Committee will seek to obtain an agreement between the Parties regarding the size of the quota and its distribution between Colombia, Venezuela and Central America, without prejudice to the commitments that Mexico has with third countries in commercial agreements, including the Free Trade Agreement of North America and the agreements derived from the Uruguay Round of the GATT. In the event that Mexico is not an importer of sugar in a particular year, the quota will be zero, therefore, for that year there will be no concession of preferential access for Colombia and Venezuela.
For the establishment of the tariff-quota for sugar by Mexico described in paragraph 2 and, notwithstanding the provisions of Article 5-04, paragraph 2, Mexico may maintain its rights and obligations under the GATT. In addition, and notwithstanding the provisions of article 5-04 paragraph 2 and the preferential access to sugar that would be granted to Mexico by Colombia and Venezuela, in the event of an agreement in the Committee, they may maintain the mechanism of price bands for sugar. prices or price stabilization.
In case the Committee reaches an agreement:
a) the minimum tariff preference for sugar will be equivalent to the PAR;
b) the assets included in annex 4 to article 5-04 will continue definitively in the Reduction Program.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 1 to 5, in the event that the Committee does not reach an agreement:
a) The Parties will not grant any preferential concession of access to sugar in their reciprocal trade nor will there be any commitments derived from this annex, therefore sugar will form part of the list of exclusions as follows:
i) for Colombia and Venezuela those mentioned in paragraph 2 of annex 2 to article 5-04; Y
ii) for Mexico, the one mentioned in paragraph 3 of annex 2 to article 5-04.
b) the goods included in annex 4 to article 5-04, will be excluded from the Tax Reduction Program and the most favored nation rate or rate or the preferential rate or rate will be applied to them if there is a tariff preference on these goods before the entry into force of this Agreement and will be included in the list of exclusions in paragraph 3 of Annex 2 to Article 5-04.
The Committee, within the period indicated in paragraph 2, shall submit a report to the Commission.
Annex 4 to article 5-04: Temporary incorporation into the Tax Reduction Program
Subject to the provisions of Annex 3 to Article 5-04, the Parties shall deduct, as of the entry into force of this Agreement, the goods of the agricultural sector included in paragraph 4 in the following manner:
a) in the following 6 years, the tariff rate or rate applicable on that date will be reduced by a total of 15% proportionally and in equal stages;
b) from the seventh to the tenth year, the tariff preference achieved at the end of the sixth year will be maintained;
c) from the eleventh to the fifteenth year, the applicable rate or tariff rate in accordance with literal b) will be reduced linearly in equal stages until it is totally eliminated.
From the eleventh to the fourteenth year, the Parties may adopt a special safeguard in the form of a tariff-quota for the goods included in paragraph 4 as follows:
a) In the eleventh year, the corresponding rate or tariff rate will be applied according to the Deduction Program to the amount established in literal b), corresponding to the amount within the deduction quota. From the twelfth to the fourteenth year that amount will increase by 10% annually;
b) the amount within the quota will be equal to the imports of the good in question, originating and coming from that Party in the tenth year plus 10%. In the event that imports originating in and coming from that Party have not been registered in the tenth year, the amount will be the average of said imports made from the sixth to the ninth year. If this average is zero, the Agricultural Trade Committee will set an amount in the last fifteen days of the tenth year;
c) the importing Party may apply the tariff rate or rate corresponding to the tenth year to the surplus of the quota.
With respect to the same property and the same Party, no Party may simultaneously:
a) apply a rate or tariff rate on the surplus of the quota in accordance with paragraph 2, literal c); Y
b) adopt a safeguard measure provided for in Chapter VIII.
The following goods will be temporarily included in the Reduction Program:
Temporary inclusions of Mexico
