CHAPTER VI: Rules of origin
Article 6-01: Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
fungible goods: goods that are interchangeable for commercial purposes, whose properties are essentially identical, and it is impractical to distinguish them by simple visual examination from one another.
non-originating good or non-originating material: a good or a material that does not qualify as originating in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
goods wholly obtained or produced entirely in the territory of one or more Parties:
a) minerals extracted in the territory of one or more Parties;
b) products of the vegetable kingdom, harvested in the territory of one or more Parties;
c) live animals, born and raised in the territory of one or more Parties;
d) goods obtained from hunting or fishing in the territory of one or more Parties;
e) goods such as fish, crustaceans and other marine species obtained from the sea by ships registered, enrolled, flagged or reputed as such, by any of the Parties, according to their legislation, through modalities such as affiliation, lease or charter;
f) Goods produced on board factory ships of any of the Parties, from the goods identified in literal e), provided that such factory ships are registered, enrolled, flagged or reputed as such, by any of the Parties, according to its legislation, through modalities such as affiliation, leasing or chartering;
g) property obtained by a Party or a person of a Party from the seabed or subsoil outside territorial waters, provided that the Party has rights to exploit that seabed or subsoil;
h) waste and scrap derived from:
i) production in the territory of one or more Parties; either
ii) used goods, collected in the territory of one or more Parties, provided that such goods serve only for the recovery of raw materials; and
i) goods produced in the territory of one or more of the Parties exclusively from the goods mentioned in subparagraphs a) to h) or their derivatives, at any stage of production.
shipping containers and packaging materials: goods that are used to protect a good during transportation, other than retail containers and materials.
total cost: in relation to a good, the sum of the following elements, in accordance with the provisions of the annex to this article:
a) the cost or value of direct manufacturing materials used in the production of the good;
b) the cost of direct labor used in the production of the good; Y
c) a reasonable amount for direct and indirect costs and expenses of manufacturing the good.
FOB: free on board (LAB).
place where the producer is located: in relation to a good, the production plant of that good.
material: a good used in the production of another good.
self-made material: a material produced by the producer of a good and used in the production of that good.
fungible materials: materials that are interchangeable for commercial purposes and whose properties are essentially identical.
indirect material: a good used in the production, testing or inspection of a good, but not physically incorporated into the good; or a good that is used in the maintenance of buildings or in the operation of equipment related to the production of a good, including:
a) fuel and power;
b) tools, dies and molds;
c) spare parts or spare parts and materials used in the maintenance of equipment and buildings;
d) lubricants, greases, compound materials and other materials used in production or to operate equipment or buildings;
e) gloves, glasses, footwear, clothing, equipment and safety accessories;
f) equipment, devices and attachments used for the verification or inspection of the goods;
g) catalysts and solvents; Y
h) any other good that is not incorporated into the good, but whose use in the production of the good can reasonably be shown to be part of that production.
intermediate material: self-produced materials used in the production of a good, and designated in accordance with article 6-07.
related person: "link between people" as established in article 15.4 of the Customs Valuation Code.
production: the growing, extracting, harvesting, fishing, hunting, manufacturing, processing, or assembling of a good.
producer: a person who grows, mines, harvests, fishes, hunts, manufactures, processes, or assembles a good.
used: employed or consumed in the production of goods.
transaction value of a good: the price paid or payable for a good related to the transaction of the producer of the good in accordance with the principles of article 1 of the Customs Valuation Code, adjusted in accordance with the principles of article 8.1, 8.3 and 8.4 thereof, without considering that the good is sold for export.
transaction value of a material: the price paid or payable for a material related to the transaction of the producer of the good in accordance with the principles of article 1 of the Customs Valuation Code, adjusted in accordance with the principles of article 8.1, 8.3 and 8.4 thereof, without considering that the material is sold for export.
Article 6-02: Interpretation and application.
For the purposes of this chapter:
a) the basis of tariff classification is the Harmonized System;
b) the determination of the transaction value of a good or a material will be made in accordance with the principles of the Customs Valuation Code;
c) when applying the Customs Valuation Code to determine the origin of a good:
i) the principles of the Customs Valuation Code will be applied to internal transactions, with the modifications that circumstances require, as they would be applied to international ones; Y
ii) the provisions of this chapter and chapter VII, will prevail over the Customs Valuation Code, in that in which they are incompatible;
d) for purposes of the definition of transaction value of a good established in article 6-01, the seller referred to in the Customs Valuation Code will be the producer of the good;
e) For purposes of defining the transaction value of a material established in article 6-01, the seller referred to in the Customs Valuation Code will be the supplier of the material, and the buyer referred to in the Valuation Code Customs will be the producer of the good;
f) all costs mentioned in this chapter shall be recorded and maintained in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles applicable in the territory of the Party where the good is produced; Y
g) The provisions of Articles 6-10 and 6-11 shall prevail over the specific rules of origin indicated in the annex to Article 6-03.
Article 6-03: Original goods.
A good shall originate in the territory of a Party when:
a) is wholly obtained or produced entirely in the territory of one or more Parties as defined in Article 6-01;
b) is produced in the territory of one or more Parties exclusively from materials that qualify as originating in accordance with this Article;
c) is produced in the territory of one or more Parties from non-originating materials that comply with a change in tariff classification and other requirements as specified in the annex to this article and the good complies with the other applicable provisions of this chapter;
d) is produced in the territory of one or more Parties from non-originating materials that meet a change in tariff classification and other requirements, and meets a regional value content requirement, as specified in the annex to this article, as well as with the other applicable provisions of this chapter;
e) is produced in the territory of one or more Parties and complies with a regional value content requirement as specified in the annex to this article, as well as with the other applicable provisions of this chapter;
f) except for goods included in chapters 61 to 63 of the Harmonized System, is produced in the territory of one or more Parties, but one or more of the non-originating materials used in the production of the good do not comply with a change in tariff classification because:
i) the good has been imported into the territory of a Party without assembly or disassembly, but has been classified as an assembled good in accordance with General Rule 2(a) of the Harmonized System; either
(ii) the heading for the good is the same for both the good and its parts and that heading is not divided into subheadings or the subheading is the same for both the good and its parts;
provided that the regional content value of the good, determined in accordance with article 6-04, is not less than the percentage established in the annex to this article or in article 6-18, and the good complies with the other applicable provisions of This chapter.
For the purposes of this chapter, the production of a good from non-originating materials that comply with a change in tariff classification and other requirements, as specified in the annex to this article, must be made entirely in the territory of one or more Parties, and any regional content requirement for a good must be fully satisfied in the territory of one or more Parties.
Article 6-04: Regional value content.
Each Party shall provide that the regional value content of a good be calculated by the exporter or producer in accordance with the transaction value method provided in paragraph 2.
To calculate the regional content value of an asset based on the transaction value method, the following formula will be applied:
 	VCR= [(VT-VMN)/VT]100

where

 	VCR: regional content expressed as a percentage.

 	VT: transaction value of a good adjusted on the basis
 	FOB, except as provided in paragraph 6.

 	VNM: value of non-originating materials used by the
 	producer in the production of the determined good in accordance
 	with the provisions of article 6-05.
Each Party shall provide that the transaction value of an asset shall be calculated:
a) in accordance with the principles of articles 1 and 8 of the Customs Valuation Code; either
b) in the event that there is no transaction value or that the transaction value of the good cannot be determined in accordance with the provisions of paragraphs 4 and 5, in accordance with the principles of article 6.1 of the Customs Valuation Code, except paragraph 1 of the interpretative note to that article.
For the purposes of paragraph 3, there will be no transaction value when the good is not the subject of a sale.
For the purposes of Paragraph 3, the transaction value of the asset cannot be determined when:
a) there are restrictions on the transfer or use of the asset by the buyer, except for those that:
i) imposed or required by the law or the authorities of the Party in which the buyer of the good is located;
ii) limit the geographic territory where the good can be resold; either
iii) do not significantly affect the value of the property;
b) the sale or the price depend on a condition or consideration whose value cannot be determined in relation to the good;
c) reverts directly or indirectly to the seller any part of the proceeds of the resale or any subsequent assignment or use of the good by the buyer, unless the due adjustment can be made in accordance with the provisions of article 8 of the Customs Valuation Code ; either
d) the buyer and seller are related persons and the relationship between them influences the price, except as provided in article 1.2 of the Customs Valuation Code.
For purposes of determining the transaction value of a good, when the producer of the good does not export it directly, the transaction value will be adjusted up to the point within the territory of the producer where the buyer receives the good.
Article 6-05: Value of non-originating materials.
The value of a non-originating material used in the production of a good:
a) will be the transaction value of the material, calculated in accordance with the principles of articles 1 and 8 of the Customs Valuation Code; either
b) in the event that there is no transaction value or the transaction value of the material cannot be determined in accordance with the principles of article 1 of the Customs Valuation Code, it will be calculated in accordance with the principles of articles 2 to 7 of the Customs Valuation Code; Y
c) include, when they are not considered in literals a) or b):
i) freight, insurance, packaging costs and all other costs incurred for the transportation of the material to the port authorized for importation in the Party where the producer of the good is located, except as provided in paragraph 2 ; Y
ii) the cost of waste and scrap resulting from the use of the material in the production of the good, less any recovery of these costs, provided that the recovery does not exceed 30% of the value of the material determined in accordance with subparagraphs a) and b).
When the producer of the good acquires the non-originating material within its territory, the value of the material will not include freight, insurance, packaging costs and all other costs incurred for the transportation of the material from the supplier's warehouse to the place where the producer is located.
For purposes of calculating the regional value content in accordance with Article 6-04, the value of non-originating materials used by the producer in the production of a good will not include:
a) the value of non-originating materials used by another producer in the production of an originating material that is acquired and used by the producer of the good in the production of that good; either
b) the value of non-originating materials used by the producer of the good in the production of an originating material of its own manufacture and designated by the producer as an intermediate material in accordance with Article 6-07.
Article 6-06: De Minimis.
A good will be considered originating if the value of all non-originating materials used in the production of the good that do not comply with the corresponding change in tariff classification established in the annex to article 6-03 does not exceed 7% of the transaction value of the good. determined in accordance with section 6-04. When the same good is also subject to the regional value content requirement, the value of those non-originating materials will be taken into account in the calculation of the regional value content of the good.
Paragraph 1 does not apply to:
a) goods included in chapters 50 to 63 of the Harmonized System, except as provided in paragraph 3.
b) a non-originating material that is used in the production of goods covered by chapters 1 through 27 of the Harmonized System, unless the non-originating material falls under a different subheading than the good for which origin is being determined in accordance with this article.
A good classified in chapters 50 to 63 of the Harmonized System that is not originating because the fibers, threads or yarns used in the production of that good do not comply with the change in tariff classification provided in the annex to article 6-03, it will be considered as originating provided that, in the case of:
a) thread or yarn, the fiber that does not comply with the tariff classification change established in article 6-03, used in the production of thread or yarn does not exceed 7% of the total weight of the yarn;
b) fabric, the fiber, thread or yarn that does not comply with the tariff classification change established in article 6-03, used in the production of fabric does not exceed 7% of the total weight of the fabric; Y
c) garments, fiber, thread or yarn that do not comply with the tariff classification change established in article 6-03, used in the production of the fabric that contains the material that determines the tariff classification of the good does not exceed 7% of the total weight of that fabric.
Article 6-07: Intermediate materials.
For purposes of calculating the regional value content in accordance with Article 6-04, the producer of a good may designate as an intermediate material any self-manufactured material used in the production of the good provided that, if such intermediate material is subject to a regional value content requirement, no other self-produced material subject to the regional value content requirement used in the production of that intermediate material may itself be designated by the producer as an intermediate material.
The value of an intermediate material will be:
a) the total cost incurred with respect to all goods produced by the producer of the good, which can be reasonably allocated to that intermediate material in accordance with the provisions of the annex to article 6-01; either
b) the sum of each cost that is part of the total cost incurred with respect to the intermediate material, that can be reasonably assigned to that intermediate material in accordance with the provisions of the annex to article 6-01.
When an intermediate material is designated and is subject to a regional content value requirement, for purposes of calculating the regional content value of the intermediate material, the transaction value referred to in article 6-04 shall be the value indicated in paragraph 2 .
Article 6-08: Accumulation.
For the purposes of establishing whether a good is originating, an exporter or producer may accumulate the production, with one or more producers in the territory of one or more Parties, of materials that are incorporated into the good so that the production of the materials is considered as carried out by that exporter or producer, provided that the provisions of Article 6-03 are complied with.
When an exporter or producer chooses to accumulate the production of materials in accordance with paragraph 1 and the good is subject to a regional value content requirement, for purposes of calculating the regional value content of the good, the value of the materials does not originating materials used by the producer of the good shall be the sum of the value of those materials determined in accordance with Article 6-05, less any of the elements of the total cost of the producer of the material except the value of the non-originating materials used by the producer of the material.
Article 6-09: Expendable goods and materials.
For the purposes of establishing whether a good is originating:
a) where originating and non-originating fungible materials are used in the production of a good that are physically mixed or blended in inventory, the origin of the materials need not be established by identifying a specific fungible material, but may be defined through one of the inventory management methods established in paragraph 2; Y
b) when originating and non-originating fungible goods are physically mixed or combined in inventory, and before their export they do not undergo any production process or any other operation in the territory of the Party in which they were physically mixed or combined, other than unloading, reloading or any other movement necessary to keep the goods in good condition or transport them to the territory of another Party, the origin of the good may be established based on one of the inventory management methods established in paragraph 2.
The inventory management methods applicable to materials or consumables will be the following:
a) "PEPS" (first in, first out) is the inventory management method by which the origin of the number of units of materials or consumables that were first received in inventory is considered as the origin in equal number of units of the materials or consumables that first come out of inventory;
b) "LUEP" (last in-first out) is the inventory management method by which the origin of the number of units of materials or consumables that were received last in inventory is considered as the origin in equal number of units of the materials or consumables first removed from inventory; either
c) "averaging" is the inventory management method by which:
i) The determination as to whether the materials or consumables are original shall be made, except as provided in numeral ii), through the application of the following formula:
 	PMO = (TMO/TMOYN)100

where

 	PMO: average of materials or consumables
 	originating.

 	TMO: total units of materials or goods 
 	originating consumables that are part of the inventory  
 	prior to departure.

 	TMOYN: total sum of units of materials or 
 	originating and non-originating fungible goods that form 
 	part of pre-departure inventory.
ii) in the case in which the good is subject to a regional content value requirement, the determination of the value of non-originating materials will be made through the application of the following formula:
 	PMN= (TMN/TMOYN)100

where

 	PMN: average of non-originating materials.

 	TMN: total value of non-expendable materials
 	originating that are part of the inventory prior to the
 	exit.
    

 	TMOYN: total value of expendable materials
 	originating and non-originating that are part of the
 	pre-departure inventory.
Once one of the inventory management methods established in paragraph 2 has been selected, it must be used throughout the fiscal year.
Article 6-10: Games or assortments.
The goods that are classified as sets or assortments according to the provisions of General Rule 3 of the Harmonized System, as well as the goods whose description according to the Harmonized System nomenclature is specifically that of a set or assortment, will qualify as originating provided that each one of the goods contained in the game or assortment complies with the rule of origin that has been established for each good in this chapter.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 1, a set or assortment of goods shall be considered originating if the value of all non-originating goods used in the formation of the set or assortment does not exceed 7% of the transaction value of the set or assortment, determined in accordance with article 6-04.
Article 6-11: Operations and practices that do not confer origin.
A good will not be considered as originating when it is only subject to the following operations or practices:
a) dilution in water or in another substance that does not materially alter the characteristics of the good;
b) simple operations intended to ensure the conservation of goods during transport or storage, such as aeration, refrigeration, removal of damaged parts, drying or addition of substances;
c) dusting, screening, classification, selection, washing, cutting;
d) packaging, repackaging or packaging for retail sale;
e) assembly of goods to form sets or assortments;
f) application of trademarks, labels or similar distinctive signs;
g) cleaning, including removal of rust, grease, paint or other coatings; Y
h) any activity or practice of price fixing, in respect of which it can be demonstrated based on sufficient evidence that its objective is to evade compliance with the provisions of this chapter.
Article 6-12: Transhipment and direct dispatch.
A good shall not be considered as originating even when it has been produced in accordance with the requirements of article 6-03, if after that production, the good undergoes a subsequent process or is subject to any other operation outside the territories of the Parties. , except for unloading, reloading or any other movement necessary to keep it in good condition or transport it to the territory of a Party.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 1, a good shall not lose its originating status when, while in transit through the territory of one or more non-Party countries, with or without transshipment or temporary storage, under the surveillance of the customs authority competent in those countries:
a) the transit is justified for geographical reasons or for considerations related to transport requirements;
b) is not intended for trade, use or employment in the transit country(ies); Y
c) during its transport and storage it is not subjected to operations other than packaging, packaging, loading, unloading or handling to ensure its conservation.
Article 6-13: Indirect materials.
Indirect materials will be considered as originating without taking into account the place of their production and the value of these materials will be their cost that is reported in the accounting records of the producer of the good.
Article 6-14: Accessories, spare parts or spare parts and tools.
Accessories, spare parts or spare parts and tools delivered with the good as part of the good's usual accessories, spare parts or spare parts and tools are considered to be originating if the good is originating and will not be taken into account in determining whether all materials non-originating goods used in the production of the good comply with the corresponding change in tariff classification established in the annex to article 6-03, provided that:
a) the accessories, spare parts or spare parts and tools are not invoiced separately from the good, regardless of whether they are broken down or detailed separately in the invoice itself; Y
b) the quantities and value of those accessories, spare parts or spare parts and tools are the usual ones for the good.
When the good is subject to a regional value content requirement, the value of accessories, spare parts or spare parts and tools will be taken into account as originating or non-originating materials, as the case may be, when calculating the regional value content of the good. .
Article 6-15: Containers and packaging materials for retail sale.
Containers and packaging materials in which a good is presented for retail sale, when classified with the good they contain, shall not be taken into account in deciding whether all non-originating materials used in the production of the good comply with the corresponding change in tariff classification established in the annex to article 6-03. When the good is subject to the regional value content requirement, the value of the containers and packaging materials for retail sale will be considered as originating or non-originating, as the case may be, to calculate the regional value content of the good.
Article 6-16: Shipping containers and packing materials.
The containers and packaging materials in which a good is packed for transport will not be taken into account for the purposes of establishing whether all the non-originating materials used in the production of the good comply with the corresponding change in tariff classification established in the annex to the article 6-03. When the good is subject to the regional value content requirement, the value of the shipping packaging materials in which a good is packaged for transport shall be considered as originating or non-originating, as the case may be, to calculate the value content. area of ​​the good
When the good is subject to the regional value content requirement, the value of the shipping packaging material will be the cost of that material that is reported in the records of the producer of the good.
Article 6-17: Consultation and modifications.
The Parties create a Rules of Origin Working Group, made up of representatives of each Party that will meet at least twice a year, as well as at the request of any Party.
It will correspond to the Working Group:
a) ensure the effective implementation and administration of this chapter;
b) reach agreements on the interpretation, application and administration of this chapter; Y
c) attend to any other matter agreed upon by the Parties.
The Parties shall consult regularly to ensure that this Chapter is applied effectively, uniformly and in accordance with the spirit and objectives of this Agreement and shall cooperate in the application of this Chapter.
Any Party that considers that this chapter needs to be modified due to changes in the development of production processes or other matters, may submit to the Working Group for its consideration a proposal for modification and the reasons and studies that support it. The Working Group will submit a report to the Commission for it to make the pertinent recommendations to the Parties.
The Parties indicated in the annex to this article may carry out consultations through the Rules of Origin Working Group in accordance with the provisions of that annex.
Article 6-18: Provisions on regional content.
The regional content expressed as a percentage will be:
a) for goods classified in chapters 28 to 40 of the Harmonized System:
i) 40% during the first three years from the entry into force of this Agreement;
ii) 45% during the fourth and fifth year from the entry into force of this Agreement; Y
iii) 50% from the first day of the sixth year from the entry into force of this Agreement;
b) for goods classified in chapters 72 to 85 and 90 of the Harmonized System, 50% from the entry into force of this Agreement;
c) for goods not included in subparagraphs a) and b):
i) 50% during the first five years from the entry into force of this Agreement; Y
ii) 55% from the first day of the sixth year from the entry into force of this Agreement.
d) The regional content percentages established in subparagraph c) do not apply to goods for which a different percentage is specified in the annex to article 6-03, section B.
Article 6-19: Special provisions.
For the purposes of the preferences indicated in the Reduction Program for goods that do not have a specific rule of origin in this Agreement, as well as for goods included in a fraction or tariff heading identified with the code "EXCL" in the Reduction Program , Resolution No. 78 of the ALADI Representatives Committee will be applied. The provisions of Chapter VII shall apply with respect to the assets referred to in this paragraph.
The annex to this article applies to the Parties indicated therein.
Article 6-20: Regional Inputs Integration Committee.
The Parties establish the Committee for the Regional Integration of Inputs (CIRI).
Each Party shall designate, for each case that arises, a representative of the public sector and a representative of the private sector to integrate the CIRI, except in the case of goods classified in chapters 50 to 63 in which the CIRI will be integrated only by representatives of Colombia and Mexico, until the rules of origin are agreed between Mexico and Venezuela for the goods classified in those chapters.
The CIRI will operate for a period of 10 years from the entry into force of this Agreement. However, if during the last three years waivers have been granted under the terms of paragraph 2 of article 6-23, the term will be extended for the period and for the goods agreed upon by the Parties.
Article 6-21: Functions of the CIRI.
The CIRI will evaluate the real and proven incapacity in the territory of the Parties of a producer of goods, to dispose under normal commercial conditions, of opportunity, volume, quality and prices, for equivalent transactions, of the materials referred to in paragraph 3 used by the producer in the production of a good.
For purposes of paragraph 1, producer means a producer of goods for export to the territory of another Party under preferential tariff treatment.
The materials used in the production of a good referred to in paragraph 1 are only those specified in the annex to this article.
Article 6-22: Procedure.
For the purposes of Article 6-21, the CIRI will carry out an investigation procedure that may be initiated at the request of the Party or at the request of the Commission. This procedure will begin within five days of receipt of the request and supporting documentation.
During this procedure, the CIRI will evaluate the evidence presented to it.
Article 6-23: Opinion to the Commission.
The CIRI will issue an opinion to the Commission within forty days from the date of initiation of the investigation procedure.
The CIRI will rule:
a) on the inability of the producer to dispose of materials in the terms indicated in paragraph 1 of article 6-21; Y
b) when the disability referred to in subparagraph a) is established, on the amounts and terms of the waiver required in the use of the materials referred to in paragraph 3 of article 6-21, so that a good can receive tariff treatment preference.
The CIRI will forward its opinion to the Commission within five days of its issuance.
Article 6-24: Resolution of the Commission.
If the CIRI issues an opinion under the terms of article 6-23, the Commission will issue a resolution within a period of no more than ten days from receipt of the opinion, in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 3 of article 6-23. , unless you agree to a different term.
When the disability referred to in paragraph 1 of article 6-21 is established, the resolution of the Commission will establish a waiver, in the amounts and terms agreed upon by the CIRI in its opinion, for the use of the materials referred to in the paragraph 3 of article 6-21, with the modifications it deems appropriate.
If the Commission has not ruled within the period indicated in paragraph 1, the opinion of the CIRI will be considered ratified.
The resolution referred to in paragraph 2 will be valid for a maximum of one year from its issuance. The Commission may extend, at the request of the interested Party, within the six months prior to its expiration and prior review by the CIRI, its resolution for an equal term if the causes that gave rise to it persist.
Any Party may request, at any time during its validity, the review of the resolution of the Commission.
Article 6-25: Referral to the Commission.
If the CIRI does not issue the opinion referred to in article 6-23 within the periods mentioned therein, because there is insufficient information or consensus on the case being dealt with, the consultations referred to in article 19 will be considered concluded. -05 and will forward it to the Commission within the five days following the expiration of that term.
The Commission will issue a resolution in the terms of paragraph 2 of article 6-23 within a period of 10 days. If the Commission does not issue a resolution, the provisions of articles 19-07 to 19-17 shall apply, subject to the provisions of paragraphs 3 to 7.
The term for the installation and issuance of the final resolution of the arbitral tribunal referred to in article 19-07, will be fifty days.
For the purposes of paragraph 2, it will be understood that the mission of the arbitral tribunal will be to issue a decision in the terms of literals a) and b) of paragraph 2 of article 6-23.
The final decision of the arbitral tribunal will be binding on the Parties and, if it decides on the waiver referred to in subparagraph b) of paragraph 2 of article 6-23, it will be valid for a maximum of one year. The Commission may extend, at the request of the interested Party within the six months prior to its expiration and prior review by the CIRI, the resolution of the arbitral tribunal for an equal term, if the causes that gave rise to it persist.
The complaining Party may avail itself of the provisions of paragraphs 1 to 3 of article 19-17, if the arbitral tribunal rules in its favor and the defendant Party does not comply with the final resolution within the term that the arbitral tribunal has set.
The defendant Party may avail itself of the provisions of paragraphs 4 and 5 of article 19-17.
Article 6-26: Regulation of operation.
By January 1, 1995 at the latest, the Parties will agree on CIRI operating regulations.
The regulation will include the operating rules of the CIRI and the conditions regarding delivery times, quantity, quality and prices of the materials referred to in paragraph 3 of article 6-21.
Annex to article 6-01: Calculation of the total cost
For the purposes of this annex, it shall be understood as:
allocation base: any of the following allocation bases that can be used by the producer to calculate the percentage of the cost in relation to the good:
a) the sum of the direct labor cost and the direct material cost or value of the good;
b) the sum of the cost of direct labor, the cost or value of the direct material and the direct costs and expenses of manufacturing the good;
c) direct labor hours or costs;
d) units produced;
e) machine hours;
f) amount of sales;
g) plant area; Y
h) any other bases that are considered reasonable and quantifiable.
direct manufacturing costs and expenses: the costs and expenses incurred in a period that are directly related to the good, other than direct material costs or value and direct labor costs.
manufacturing overhead costs and expenses: Costs and expenses incurred in a period other than direct manufacturing costs and expenses, direct labor costs, and direct material costs or value.
for internal management purposes: any allocation procedure used for tax filing, financial statements or reports, internal control, financial planning, decision making, pricing, cost recovery, cost control management, or performance measurement.
When the producer of a good uses a cost allocation method for internal management purposes to calculate the total cost for the good to allocate direct material costs, direct labor costs, or direct and indirect manufacturing costs and expenses, or portions thereof, and that method reasonably reflects direct material costs, direct labor costs, or direct and indirect manufacturing costs and expenses incurred in the production of the good , that method will be considered a method of reasonable allocation of costs and expenses and may be used to allocate costs to the good.
For purposes of calculating the total cost, the producer of the good may determine a reasonable amount for costs and expenses that have not been assigned to the good, as follows:
a) for direct material costs and direct labor costs, based on any method that reasonably reflects the direct material and direct labor costs used in the production of the good; Y
b) in relation to direct and indirect manufacturing costs and expenses, based on the provisions of paragraph 6.
Any method of reasonable allocation of costs and expenses that a producer chooses for the purposes of this chapter, will be used throughout his fiscal year.
The following concepts will not be assigned to a good and these concepts will be considered as excluded costs and expenses:
a) costs and expenses of a service provided by the producer of a good to another person, when the service is not related to the good;
b) costs and losses resulting from the sale of a part of the producer's company, which constitutes a discontinued operation;
c) costs related to the cumulative effect of changes in the application of accounting principles;
d) costs or losses resulting from the sale of a producer's capital good;
e) costs and expenses related to acts of God or force majeure; Y
f) profits obtained by the producer of the good regardless of whether they were retained by the producer or paid to other persons, such as dividends or taxes paid on these profits, including taxes on capital gains.
In order to allocate direct and indirect manufacturing costs and expenses, the producer may choose one or more allocation bases that reflect a relationship between direct and indirect manufacturing costs and expenses and the good.
In relation to each base chosen, the producer may calculate a percentage of the cost for each good produced, in accordance with the following formula:
         	PC = (BA/BTA)100

 	where

 	PC: the percentage of the cost or expense in relation to the good.

 	BA: the allocation base for the good.

 	BTA: the total allocation base for all assets
      	produced by the producer of the good.
The costs or expenses with respect to which an allocation base is chosen, are assigned to a good according to the following formula:
           	CAB = AC x PC

 	where

 	CAB: the costs or expenses assigned to the good.

 	CA: the costs or expenses that will be assigned.

 	PC: the percentage of the cost or expense in relation to the good.
When the costs or expenses mentioned in paragraph 5 are included in the costs or expenses assigned to the good, the percentage of the cost or expense in relation to the good used to assign that cost or expense to the good will be used to determine the amount of the costs. or excluded expenses that will be subtracted from the costs or expenses that were assigned to the property.
Any cost or expense assigned in accordance with any reasonable cost allocation method used for internal administration purposes will not be considered reasonably assigned when it can be shown from sufficient evidence that its objective is to evade compliance with the provisions of this chapter.
Annex to article 6-03: Specific rules of origin
Section A - General interpretative note
For the purposes of this annex, it shall be understood as:
chapter: a chapter of the Harmonized System.
tariff fraction: an eight- or ten-digit Harmonized System tariff classification code.
Heading: A four-digit Harmonized System tariff classification code.
section: a section of the Harmonized System.
subheading: a Harmonized System tariff classification code at the six-digit level.
The specific rule or set of rules that applies to a heading, subheading, or tariff item is stated next to the heading, subheading, or tariff item.
The rule applicable to a tariff fraction shall have priority over the rule applicable to the heading or subheading that includes that tariff fraction.
A change of classification requirement applies only to non-originating materials.
Any reference to weight in the rules for goods included in chapters 1 to 24 of the Harmonized System, means net weight unless otherwise specified in the Harmonized System.
For any reference to a regional content value requirement in the specific rules of origin, the provisions of article 6-18 shall be taken into account.
For the tariff fractions described in annex 2 to article 5-04, the rules of origin will apply in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 9 of annex 1 to article 5-04.
The description of the tariff fractions expressed with letters in the text of the specific rules of origin is contained in section C.

Annex to article 6-17
From the 1st January 2000, Colombia and Mexico may carry out consultations through the Rules of Origin Working Group to evaluate the conditions of supply availability of fibers, threads and fabrics in Colombia or Mexico to produce goods classified in chapters 50 to 63 of the Harmonized System and, where appropriate, design rules of origin that resolve possible supply problems that may have arisen.
Annex to article 6-19: Special provisions related to goods classified in chapters 50 to 63 and in heading 39.03 of the Harmonized System
Section A - Colombia and Mexico
For the purposes of applying the temporary flexibility levels established in article 3-08, the treatment of originating goods will be granted to goods classified as:
a) Chapters 51 to 60 of the Harmonized System that meet the following conditions:
i) Threads and yarns classified in headings 51.06 to 51.10, 52.04 to 52.07, 53.07 to 53.08 and 55.08 to 55.11 of the Harmonized System must be entirely produced in the territory of the exporting Party from fiber or filament imported or not from outside the the territories of Colombia or Mexico;
ii) textile goods classified in headings 54.01 to 54.06 of the Harmonized System must be entirely produced in the territory of the exporting Party from materials imported or not from outside the territories of Colombia or Mexico;
iii) fabrics classified in headings 51.11 to 51.13, 52.08 to 52.12, 53.10 to 53.11, 54.07 to 54.08, 55.12 to 55.16 and 60.01 to 60.02 of the Harmonized System must be entirely produced in the territory of the exporting Party from fiber, yarn or yarns imported or not from outside the territories of Colombia or Mexico; Y
iv) textile goods classified in chapters 56 to 59 of the Harmonized System must be entirely produced in the territory of the exporting Party from fiber, thread, yarns or cloth imported or not from outside the territories of Colombia or Mexico;
b) Chapters 61 through 63 of the Harmonized System referred to in Article 3-08 that are wholly cut (or woven to shape) and sewn or otherwise assembled in the territory of the exporting Party from fiber, yarn, yarns or fabric imported or not from outside the territories of Colombia or Mexico and must comply with a regional content requirement of not less than 50%, in accordance with the provisions of article 6-04.
For the purposes of determining the origin of a good classified in chapters 50 to 63, Venezuela will be considered as a non-Party country.
Section B - Mexico and Venezuela
During the first two years from the entry into force of this Agreement, Mexico and Venezuela will carry out negotiations and will do their best to reach an agreement regarding the applicable rules of origin between them for goods classified in chapters 50 to 63. of the Harmonized System.
Section C - Colombia, Mexico and Venezuela
During the first two years from the entry into force of this Agreement, the Parties will carry out negotiations and make their best effort to reach an agreement regarding the applicable rules of origin between them for goods classified in heading 39.03 of the Harmonized System. .
Annex to article 6-21
For a good classified in the tariff codes of the Harmonized System described below, the materials referred to in paragraph 1 of article 6-21, are those used in the production of the good classified in those tariff codes when their use is required by the rule of origin established in the annex to article 6-03 for that good:
CHAPTER VII: Customs procedures
Article 7-01: Definitions.
The definitions of chapter VI are incorporated into this chapter.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
competent authority: the authority that, according to the internal legislation of each Party, is responsible for the administration of its laws and its customs, tax or commercial regulations.
Identical Goods: Goods that are the same in all respects, including their physical characteristics, quality, and goodwill. Small differences in appearance do not prevent them from being considered identical;
preferential tariff treatment: the application of the import tax to an originating good in accordance with the annex to article 3-04.
Article 7-02: Declaration and certification of origin.
The certificate of origin established in annex 1 to this article, will serve to certify that a good that is exported from the territory of one Party to the territory of another Party, qualifies as originating. This certificate may be modified by agreement of the Parties.
Each Party shall provide that for the export to another Party of a good for which the importer is entitled to claim preferential tariff treatment, the exporter completes and signs a certificate of origin with respect to that good. The exporter's certificate of origin will require validation by the competent authority of the exporting Party.
In the event that the exporter is not the producer of the good, he will fill out and sign the certificate of origin based on a declaration of origin in accordance with annex 2 to this article that covers the good that is the object of export, filled out and signed by the exporter. producer of the good and provided voluntarily to the exporter. The declaration of origin filled out and signed by the producer will not be validated under the terms of paragraph 2.
The authority of the exporting Party:
a) will maintain the administrative mechanisms for the validation of the certificate of origin filled out and signed by the exporter;
b) provide, at the request of the importing Party, information regarding the origin of imported goods with preferential tariff treatment; Y
c) shall notify the other Parties of the list of officials authorized to validate the certificates of origin with their corresponding seals, signatures and facsimile. Modifications to this relationship will take effect thirty days after receipt of the respective communication.
Each Party shall provide that the certificate of origin filled out and signed by the exporter and validated by the competent authority of the exporting Party may cover a single importation of one or more goods and shall be valid for 1 year from the date of its signature.
Article 7-03: Obligations regarding imports.
Each Party shall require the importer requesting preferential tariff treatment for a good of another Party, that:
a) declare in writing, in the import document based on a valid certificate of origin, that the good qualifies as originating;
b) have the certificate of origin in their possession at the time of making that declaration; Y
c) present or deliver the certificate of origin when requested by the competent authority.
Each Party will require the importer to present or deliver a corrected declaration and pay the corresponding import taxes, when the importer has reason to believe that the certificate of origin on which his import declaration is based contains incorrect information. If you submit the aforementioned declaration spontaneously, in accordance with the internal legislation of each Party, you will not be penalized.
Each Party shall provide that when the importer does not comply with any of the requirements established in paragraph 1, preferential tariff treatment shall be denied to the good imported from another Party for which preference has been requested.
The request referred to in paragraph 1, literal c) will not prevent the customs clearance or release of the merchandise under conditions of preferential tariff treatment requested in the import declaration.
Article 7-04: Obligations regarding exports.
Each Party shall provide that an exporter or producer of that Party who has completed and signed a certificate or declaration of origin, deliver a copy of the validated certificate or declaration of origin to the competent authority upon request.
An exporter or producer who has completed and signed a certificate or declaration of origin and has reason to believe that this certificate or declaration contains incorrect information, must communicate without delay and in writing, any changes that could affect the accuracy or validity of the certificate. or declaration to all persons to whom it has been delivered as well as, in accordance with the legislation of the Party in question, to the competent authority of the exporting Party. In this case, you will not be penalized for having submitted an incorrect certificate or statement.
Each Party shall provide that a false certificate or declaration of origin made by an exporter or a producer shall have the same administrative consequences as false declarations or declarations made in its territory by an importer in contravention of its customs laws and regulations, with the modifications that circumstances may require.
Article 7-05: Exceptions.
The certificate of origin shall not be required in the case of the importation of a good for which the Party into whose territory it is imported has waived the requirement of presentation of a certificate of origin.
Article 7-06: Accounting records.
Each Party shall provide that an exporter or producer who completes and signs a certificate or declaration of origin, keep for a minimum of five years from the date of signing the certificate or declaration, all records and documents relating to the origin of the good. , including those referring to:
a) the acquisition, costs, value and payment of the good that is exported from its territory;
b) the acquisition, costs, value and payment of all materials used in the production of the good that is exported from its territory; Y
c) the production of the good in the form in which it is exported from its territory.
Each Party shall provide that the exporter or producer shall provide to the competent authority of the importing Party the records and documents referred to in paragraph 1. When the records and documents are not in the possession of the exporter or producer, the exporter or producer may request the producer or supplier of the materials, the records and documents so that they are delivered through it to the competent authority that performs the verification.
Each Party shall provide that an importer who requests preferential tariff treatment for a good imported from another Party, shall keep for a minimum of five years from the date of importation, the certificate of origin and all documentation related to the importation. required by the importing Party.
Article 7-07: Procedures to verify origin.
Before carrying out a verification in accordance with the provisions of this article, the competent authority of the importing Party may request information regarding the origin of the exported goods from the competent authority of the exporting Party.
To determine whether a good imported from another Party qualifies as originating, each Party may, through the competent authority, verify the origin of the good by:
a) written questionnaires addressed to exporters or producers in the territory of the other Party; either
b) verification visits to an exporter or a producer in the territory of the other Party, with the purpose of examining the records and documents that prove compliance with the rules of origin in accordance with Article 7-06, and inspecting the facilities that used in the production of the good and, where appropriate, those used in the production of the material.
The provisions of this paragraph shall be done without prejudice to the powers of inspection or review of the importing Party over its own importers, exporters or producers.
When the exporter or producer receives a questionnaire in accordance with paragraph 2, literal a), it will respond and return that questionnaire within a period of thirty days. During this period, the exporter or producer may request in writing to the importing Party that is carrying out the verification, an extension which shall not exceed thirty days. This request shall not entail the denial of preferential tariff treatment.
In the event that the exporter or producer does not return the duly answered questionnaire within the corresponding period, the importing Party may deny preferential tariff treatment in accordance with paragraph 11.
The importing Party that carries out a verification by means of a questionnaire, will have a period of 45 days from the receipt of the response to it, to send the notification referred to in paragraph 6, if it deems it appropriate.
Before carrying out a verification visit in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 2, literal b), the importing Party shall be obliged, through its competent authority, to communicate in writing its intention to carry out the visit at least thirty days of anticipation. The notification shall be sent to the exporter or producer to be visited, to the competent authority of the Party in whose territory the visit is to take place and, if requested by the latter, to the embassy of the latter Party in the territory of the importing party. The competent authority of the importing Party shall obtain the written consent of the exporter or the producer whom it intends to visit.
The communication referred to in paragraph 6 will contain:
a) the identification of the competent authority making the communication in writing;
b) the name of the exporter or producer you intend to visit;
c) the date and place of the proposed verification visit;
d) the purpose and scope of the proposed verification visit, making specific mention of the good or goods subject to verification to which the certificate(s) of origin refer;
e) the names and titles of the officials who will carry out the verification visit; Y
f) the legal basis of the verification visit.
Any change in the number, name or position of the officials referred to in subparagraph e) of paragraph 7, shall be communicated in writing to the exporter or producer and to the authority of the exporting Party before the verification visit. Any modification of the information referred to in subparagraphs a), b), c), d) and f) of paragraph 7, will be notified in the terms of paragraph 6.
If within thirty days of receipt of the communication regarding the verification visit proposed in accordance with paragraph 6, the exporter or producer does not give its written consent for the verification visit, the importing Party may deny tariff treatment. preferential to the good or goods that would have been the reason for the visit.
Each Party will allow the exporter or producer whose good is the subject of a verification visit, to designate two witnesses who are present during the visit, provided that the witnesses intervene only in that capacity. If there is no designation of witnesses by the exporter or the producer, this omission will not result in the postponement of the visit.
The Party that has carried out a verification shall provide the exporter or producer whose good or goods have been subject to verification, a document containing the decision in which it determines whether or not the good or goods qualify as originating, and includes the grounds. factual and legal determination.
When the verification carried out by a Party indicates that the exporter or producer has falsely or unfoundedly certified or declared more than once that a good qualifies as originating, the Party may suspend preferential tariff treatment to identical goods that that Party person exports or produces, until it proves that it complies with the provisions of Chapter VI.
Each Party shall provide that the decision that determines that a certain good imported into its territory does not qualify as originating in accordance with the tariff classification or with the value applied by the Party to one or more materials used in the production of the good, and this differs from the tariff classification or the value applied to the materials by the exporting Party, does not take effect until it is communicated in writing to both the importer of the good and the exporter or producer who has completed and signed the certificate or declaration of origin that covers it.
The Party shall not apply the decision adopted in accordance with paragraph 13, to an import made before the date on which the decision takes effect when the competent authority of the exporting Party has issued a resolution or an advance criterion on the tariff classification or the value of materials, about which certainty can be obtained under the customs laws and regulations of that exporting Party.
When a Party denies preferential tariff treatment to a good pursuant to a decision made in accordance with paragraph 13, that Party shall postpone the effective date of the denial for a period not to exceed ninety days, provided that the importer of the good or The exporter or producer who has completed and signed the certificate or declaration of origin that protects it, accredits having relied in good faith, to its own detriment, on the tariff classification or the value applied to the materials by the competent authority of the exporting Party.
Each Party will maintain the confidentiality of the information collected in the origin verification process in accordance with the provisions of the domestic legislation of the Parties involved.
Article 7-08: Review and challenge.
Each Party shall grant exporters and producers of another Party the same rights to review and challenge decisions to determine origin and advance criteria provided for importers in its territory who:
a) fill out and sign a certificate or declaration of origin covering a good that has been the subject of an origin determination decision in accordance with paragraph 11 of Article 7-07; either
b) has received advance judgment in accordance with Article 7-10.
Each Party, in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 1, shall grant access to at least one level of independent administrative review of the official or agency responsible for the decision subject to review, and access to one level of judicial review of the initial decision. or the decision made at the final level of administrative review. The administrative or judicial review shall be made in accordance with the internal legislation of each Party.
Article 7-09: Sanctions.
Each Party shall establish or maintain criminal, civil or administrative sanctions for violations of its laws and regulations related to the provisions of this chapter.
Article 7-10: Advance criteria.
Each Party shall provide that, through its competent authority, advance criteria be promptly issued in writing, prior to the importation of a good from another Party into its territory. The anticipated criteria will be issued at the request of the importer in its territory or of the exporter or producer in the territory of the other Party, based on the facts and circumstances stated by them regarding whether the goods qualify as originating in accordance with the rules of origin. of chapter VI.
a) if the non-originating materials used in the production of a good comply with the corresponding change in tariff classification indicated in the annex to article 6-03 of chapter VI as a result of the production being carried out in the territory of one or more Parties;
b) if the good complies with the regional content value requirement established in the annex to article 6-03 of chapter VI;
c) if the method for calculating the value of a good or of the materials used in the production of a good, which must be applied by the exporter or producer in the territory of another Party, in accordance with the principles of the Customs Valuation Code and with the in order to determine if the good meets the regional value content requirement in accordance with the annex to article 6-03 of chapter VI; either
d) other matters that the Parties agree.
Each Party shall adopt or maintain, upon publication, procedures for the issuance of advance criteria that include:
a) a detailed description of the information reasonably required to process a request;
b) the power of its competent authority to request additional information at any time from the person requesting the early judgment during the application evaluation process;
c) the obligation to issue the advance judgment within a period of one hundred and twenty days counted from the moment in which the authority has obtained all the necessary information from the person requesting it; Y
d) the obligation to fully explain the well-founded and motivated reasons for the anticipated criterion when it is unfavorable for the applicant.
Each Party shall apply advance criteria to imports on or after the date of issuance of the criteria, unless the advance criteria is modified or revoked in accordance with paragraph 6.
Each Party shall grant the same treatment, the same interpretation and application of the provisions of Chapter VI, referring to the determination of origin, to all who request early judgment, when the facts and circumstances are identical in all substantial aspects.
The advance judgment may be modified or revoked by the issuing Party in the following cases:
a) when it contains or is based on an error:
i) in fact;
ii) in the tariff classification of a good or materials;
iii) whether the good meets the regional value content requirement;
b) when the anticipated criterion is not in accordance with an interpretation agreed between the Parties with respect to the rules of origin of this Agreement;
c) to comply with a judicial decision; Y
d) when the circumstances or facts that support the anticipated criterion change.
Each Party shall provide that any modification or revocation of an advance ruling shall take effect from the date it is issued or on a later date established therein. The modification or revocation of an advance criterion may not be applied to imports of a good made before those dates, unless the person to whom the criterion was issued has not acted in accordance with the terms and conditions of the initially issued criterion.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 7, the Party issuing the advance directive shall postpone the effective date of the modification or revocation for a period not to exceed ninety days, when the person to whom the advance directive was issued has supported this criterion in good faith and to his detriment.
Each Party shall provide that, when considering the regional value content of a good for which advance ruling has been issued, the competent authority shall assess whether:
a) the exporter or producer complies with the terms and conditions of the advance judgment;
b) the exporter's or producer's operations are consistent with the circumstances and substantial facts that support that criterion; Y
c) the supporting data and calculations used in applying the method to calculate the value are correct in all material respects.
Each Party shall provide that when the competent authority determines that any of the requirements established in paragraph 9 has not been met, it may modify or revoke the advance judgment, as the circumstances warrant.
Each Party shall provide that, when the competent authority decides that the advance judgment has been based on incorrect information, the party that issued it shall not be penalized, if it demonstrates that it acted with reasonable care and in good faith when stating the facts and circumstances that motivated the judgment. advance judgment.
Each Party may apply the measures that the circumstances warrant, when the competent authority has issued an advance judgment to a person who has falsely stated or omitted facts or substantial circumstances on which the advance judgment is based, or has not acted in accordance with the terms and conditions thereof.
The validity of an advance criterion will be subject to the permanent obligation of the person to whom it was issued to inform the competent authority of any substantial change in the facts or circumstances on which it was based to issue that criterion.
Article 7-11: Customs Procedures Working Group.
The Parties create a Customs Procedures Working Group made up of representatives of each Party that will meet at least twice a year, or at the request of any of the Parties.
It will correspond to the Working Group:
a) ensure that agreements are reached on:
i) the interpretation, application and administration of this chapter;
ii) tariff classification and valuation issues related to origin determinations;
iii) the procedures for the request, approval, modification, revocation and application of the anticipated criteria;
iv) changes to the certificate or declaration of origin; Y
v) any other matter submitted to it by a Party.
b) examine proposals for administrative or operational changes in customs matters that may affect the flow of trade between the Parties.
Chapter VIII : Safeguards
Article 8-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
Similar good: one that, although it does not coincide in all its characteristics with the good with which it is compared, has some identical characteristics, mainly in terms of its nature, use, function and quality.
serious damage: a general and significant impairment to a national production.
global measures: emergency measures on the importation of goods under Article XIX of the GATT.
national production: producer or producers of identical, similar or direct competitive goods that operate within the territory of one of the Parties and represent a substantial proportion of the total national production of those goods. From the fourth year after the entry into force of this Agreement, that substantial proportion will be at least 40%.
Article 8-02 : Safeguards regime.
The Parties may apply to imports of goods carried out in accordance with this Agreement a safeguard regime whose application will be based on clear, strict criteria and with a defined temporality. The safeguard regime provides for measures of a bilateral or global nature.
Section A - Bilateral measures.
Article 8-03 : Conditions of application.
If, as a result of the application of the Reduction Program, the importation of one or several goods originating from any of the Parties is carried out in quantities and under such conditions that, by themselves, they are the substantial cause of serious damage or threat of serious damage to domestic production of identical, similar or direct competitive goods, the importing Party may adopt bilateral safeguard measures, which shall be applied in accordance with the following rules:
a) when it is strictly necessary to counteract serious damage or the threat of serious damage caused by imports originating in the other Party, a Party may adopt safeguard measures within a period of fifteen years from the entry into force of this Treaty;
b) the measures will be exclusively of a tariff nature. The tariff determined in no case may exceed the one in force against third countries for that good at the time the safeguard is adopted;
c) the measures may be applied for a period of up to one year and may be extended only once, up to an equal and consecutive term, as long as the conditions that motivated them persist;
d) Upon completion of the measure, the rate or tariff will be the one that corresponds to the good object of the measure according to the Reduction Program.
Article 8-04 : Compensation for bilateral measures.
When the cause of the application of the bilateral safeguard measure is a threat of serious injury or when the Party intends to extend the measure, it will grant the exporting Party mutually agreed compensation, which will consist of temporary additional tariff concessions, whose effects on the trade of the exporting Party are equivalent to the impact of the safeguard measure.
The Parties will agree on the terms of the compensation referred to in paragraph 1 at the prior consultation stage established in Article 8-14.
If the Parties do not reach an agreement regarding compensation, the Party proposing to take the measure shall be empowered to do so and the exporting Party may take tariff measures that have trade effects equivalent to those of the measure taken.
Section B - Global measures
Article 8-05 : Rights under GATT.
The Parties confirm their rights and obligations under Article XIX of the GATT, in relation to any emergency measure adopted by a Party in the application of this Agreement.
Article 8-06 : Criteria for the adoption of a measure.
When a Party decides to adopt a global safeguard measure, it may only apply it to the other Party when imports of a good from the latter, considered individually, represent a substantial part of total imports and contribute significantly to serious injury or threat of damage. serious injury to the domestic production of the importing Party.
For the purposes of paragraph 1, the following criteria shall be taken into account:
a) Normally, imports from the other Party will not be considered substantial, if it is not one of the five main suppliers of the good subject to the procedure, based on its participation in those imports during the immediately preceding 3 years;
b) normally imports from the other Party shall not be considered to contribute significantly to serious injury or the threat of serious injury, if their growth rate during the period in which the injurious increase occurred is substantially less than the growth rate of total imports of the good to the Party proposing to take the measure, from all sources, during the same period.
Article 8-07 : Compensation for global measures.
The Party that adopts a global safeguard measure shall grant the exporting Party compensation in accordance with the provisions of the GATT.
Section C - Procedure
Article 8-08 : Adoption procedure.
The Party that intends to adopt a bilateral or global safeguard measure in accordance with this chapter, will comply with the procedure set forth in this section.
Article 8-09 : Investigation.
To determine the origin of the application of a safeguard measure, the competent authority of the importing Party will carry out an investigation, which may be ex officio or at the request of a party.
The purpose of the investigation referred to in the paragraph is:
a) Evaluate the volume and conditions in which the imports of the good in question are carried out;
b) verify the existence of serious injury or threat of serious injury to domestic production;
c) verify the existence of a direct causal relationship between the increase in imports of the good and the serious damage or the threat of serious damage to national production.
Article 8-10 : Determination of damage.
For the purposes of verifying the existence of serious damage or threat of serious damage, the competent authorities will evaluate the factors of an objective and quantifiable nature that are related to the national production affected, in particular the rate and amount of the increase in the imports of the good in question, in absolute and relative terms; the part of the internal market absorbed by the increase in imports; changes in the level of sales; internal prices; production; productivity; utilization of installed capacity; Profits; losses and employment.
Article 8-11 : Effect of other factors.
If there are other factors, other than the increase in imports from the other Party, that simultaneously harm or threaten to harm domestic production, the damage caused by those factors cannot be attributed to the referred imports.
Article 8-12 : Publication and communication.
The resolution that provides for the initiation of a safeguard investigation will be published in the respective official dissemination body of the importing Party and will be communicated to the interested parties, within ten business days following that publication.
Article 8-13 : Content of the communication.
The competent authority will make the communication referred to in article 8-12, which will contain sufficient information to support and motivate the initiation of the investigation, including:
a) the available name and address of national producers of identical or similar goods or direct competitors representative of national production; their participation in the national production of those goods and the reasons why they are considered representative of that sector;
b) the clear and complete description of the goods subject to the investigation, the tariff fractions in which they are classified and the current tariff treatment, as well as the identification of the identical, similar or direct competitive goods;
c) data on imports corresponding to the three years prior to the initiation of the investigation;
d) the data on the total national production of identical, similar or direct competitive goods, corresponding to the three years prior to the initiation of the proceeding;
e) the data that demonstrates that there are reasonable indications of serious injury or threat of serious injury caused by the imports to the domestic industry in question, and a summary of the grounds for alleging that the increase in imports of those goods, in relative or absolutes in relation to national production, is the cause of it; Y
f) If applicable, the criteria and objective information that demonstrate that the assumptions for the application of a global safeguard measure to the other Party established in this chapter are met.
Article 8-14 : Prior consultations.
If, as a result of the safeguard investigation, the competent authority determines, based on objective evidence, that the assumptions set forth in this chapter are met, the Party that decides to initiate a procedure that could result in the adoption of a safeguard measure, shall do so. communicate to the other Party, requesting consultations as provided in this chapter.
A third Party that expresses a substantial interest in the application of a bilateral safeguard measure because its trade could be affected by its application, may participate in the consultations referred to in paragraph 1.
The importing Party shall provide adequate opportunities for prior consultations to take place. The period for prior consultations will begin on the day after the exporting Party receives the communication containing the request to hold these consultations. The communication will contain the data that demonstrates the serious injury or the threat of serious injury caused by the imports subject to investigation, and the pertinent information on the safeguard measures that are intended to be adopted and their duration.
The period for prior consultations will be forty-five days, unless the Parties agree on another term.
Safeguard measures may only be adopted once the prior consultation period has concluded.
Article 8-15 : Confidential information.
The consultation procedure will not oblige the Parties to reveal the information that has been provided confidentially, the disclosure of which may violate their laws that regulate the matter or harm commercial interests.
Notwithstanding the foregoing, the importing Party that intends to apply the measure shall provide a non-confidential summary of the information that is confidential.
Article 8-16 : Observations of the exporting Party.
During the consultation period, the exporting Party will formulate the observations it deems pertinent, in particular the admissibility of invoking the safeguard and the proposed measures.
Article 8-17 : Extension.
If the importing Party determines that the reasons that gave rise to the application of the safeguard measure subsist, it shall notify the exporting Party of its intention to extend it, at least sixty days prior to the expiration of the validity of those measures. The extension procedure will be carried out in accordance with the provisions established in this chapter for the adoption of safeguard measures.
CHAPTER IX : Unfair international trade practices
Article 9-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
countervailing duty: antidumping duties and countervailing duties or duties, as the case may be.
Interested party: the producers, importers and exporters of the good subject to investigation, as well as foreign moral or legal persons that have a direct interest in the investigation in question.
final resolution: the resolution of the authority that decides whether or not to impose definitive countervailing duties.
Initial resolution: the resolution of the competent authority that formally declares the initiation of the investigation.
preliminary resolution: the resolution of the competent authority that decides whether or not to impose a provisional countervailing duty.
Article 9-02 : Export subsidies.
As of the entry into force of this Agreement, the Parties will not grant subsidies to the exports of industrial goods destined for the markets of the Parties. Subsidies for the export of goods from the agricultural sector will be governed in accordance with the provisions of Chapter V, Section A.
Article 9-03 : Compensatory quotas.
The importing Party, in accordance with its legislation and in accordance with the provisions of this Agreement, in the GATT, in the Agreement Regarding the Application of Article VI of the GATT (Anti-dumping Code), in the Agreement Regarding the Interpretation and Application of Articles VI, XVI and XXIII of the GATT (Subsidies and Countervailing Duties Code), may establish and apply countervailing duties in the event of situations in which, through an objective examination based on positive evidence:
a) the existence of imports is determined:
i) in dumped conditions; either
ii) goods that have received export subsidies, including subsidies other than those granted to exports, which adversely influence normal competition conditions; Y
b) the existence of damage or threat of damage to the domestic production of identical or similar goods in the importing Party or the significant delay in the start of that production is verified, as a consequence of those imports of identical or similar goods from another Party .
Article 9-04 : Minimum margins.
