The Party shall terminate the investigations referred to in Article 9-03, when the dumping margin is less than 2% of the normal value of the investigated good or when the amount of the subsidy is less than 1% ad valorem.
In addition, the investigations referred to in Article 9-03 will be terminated when the volume of the dumped or subsidized imports represents less than 1% of the domestic market for the similar good in the importing Party, except in the case in which the The volume of imports from the exporting Party is lower, individually considered, but accumulated, than imports at dumping or subsidized prices from other countries, representing more than 2.5% of that market.
Article 9-05 : Communications and deadlines.
Each Party shall communicate the resolutions on the matter directly to its importers and to the exporters of the other Party of which it is aware and, where appropriate, to the government of the exporting Party, to the responsible national body referred to in Chapter XX , and to the diplomatic mission of the exporting Party accredited to the Party conducting the investigation. Likewise, the actions tending to identify and locate the interested parties in the procedure will be carried out in order to guarantee the exercise of the right of defense.
The communication of the initial resolution shall be made within eight business days following its publication in the official dissemination body of the importing Party.
The communication of the initial resolution will contain, at least, the following information:
a) the terms and place for the presentation of allegations, evidence and other documents; Y
b) the name, address and telephone number of the office where information can be obtained, consultations made and the case file inspected.
With the communication, the exporters will be sent a copy of the respective publication in the official publication of the importing Party, as well as a copy of the public version of the complaint document and its annexes.
The Party will grant the interested parties of which it is aware, a response period of not less than thirty business days, counted from the publication of the initial resolution in the respective official dissemination body, in order for them to appear to state what they their right agrees, and will grant the interested parties an equal term for the same purposes counted from the publication of the preliminary resolution in that body.
Article 9-06 : Content of the resolutions.
The initial, preliminary and final resolution will contain at least the following:
a) the name of the applicant;
b) the indication of the imported good subject to the procedure and its tariff classification;
c) the elements and evidence used to determine the existence of the unfair practice, damage or threat of damage, and their causal relationship;
d) the factual and legal considerations that led the authority to initiate an investigation or to impose a countervailing duty; Y
e) the legal arguments, data, facts or circumstances that found and motivate the decision in question.
Article 9-07 : Rights and obligations of the interested parties.
For the purposes of the rights and obligations established in this chapter, each Party shall ensure that the parties interested in the administrative investigation have the same rights and obligations. The rights and obligations of the interested parties will be respected and observed, both in the course of the procedure and in the administrative and contentious instances that are instituted against the final resolutions.
Article 9-08 : Clarifications.
Once a compensatory, provisional or final quota has been imposed, the interested parties may request the authority that has issued the act, to decide whether a certain asset is subject to the imposed measure, or to clarify any aspect of the corresponding resolution.
Article 9-09 : Conciliation hearings.
In the course of the investigation, any interested party may request the competent authority to hold conciliatory hearings in order to reach a satisfactory solution.
Article 9-10 : Review.
Definitive countervailing duties may be reviewed by the competent authority before a change of circumstances in the market of the importing Party and the export market.
Article 9-11 : Validity of compensatory quotas.
A definitive compensatory quota will be eliminated automatically when after five years, counted from the validity of that quota, none of the interested parties has requested its review nor has the competent authority initiated it ex officio.
Article 9-12 : Access to the file.
Interested parties will have access to the administrative file of the procedure in question, except for the confidential information it contains.
Article 9-13 : Sending copies.
The parties interested in the investigation may send the other interested parties copies of each of the reports, documents and means of evidence that they present to the investigating authority in the course of the investigation.
Article 9-14 : Information meetings.
The competent authority of the importing Party, upon request of the interested parties, will hold information meetings, in order to disseminate the pertinent information on the content of the provisional and final resolutions.
With respect to a preliminary ruling, the request referred to in paragraph 1 may be submitted at any time during the investigation. In the case of a final resolution, this request must be submitted within five business days following the publication of the resolution in the respective official dissemination body. In both cases, the competent authority will hold the meeting within a period of fifteen business days from the presentation of the request.
In the information meetings referred to in paragraphs 1 and 2, the interested parties will have the right to review the reports or technical reports, the methodology, the spreadsheets and, in general, any element on which the corresponding resolution has been based, except confidential information.
Article 9-15 : Other rights of interested parties.
The competent authorities will hold, at the request of a party, conciliatory meetings in which the interested parties may appear and listen to their counterparts regarding the information or evidence that the investigating authority deems appropriate.
Interested parties will be given the opportunity to present their arguments after the evidence period. The allegations will consist of the written presentation of conclusions related to the information and arguments rendered in the course of the investigation.
Article 9-16 : Publication.
Each Party shall publish the following resolutions in its respective official dissemination body:
a) the initial, preliminary and final resolution;
b) the one that declares the administrative investigation concluded:
i) due to commitments with the exporting Party or with the exporters, as the case may be;
ii) due to commitments derived from the holding of conciliation hearings; either
iii) for any other reason.
c) those that reject the complaints; Y
d) those for which the withdrawals of the complainants are accepted.
Article 9-17 : Access to other files.
The competent authority of each Party will allow the interested parties, in the course of an investigation, access to the public information contained in the administrative files of any other investigation, once sixty business days have elapsed from the final resolution of this investigation. .
Article 9-18 : Reimbursement or reimbursement.
If a compensatory quota is determined in a final resolution that is lower than the one that has been provisionally determined, the competent authority of the importing Party shall return the amounts paid in excess.
Article 9-19 : Deadlines for provisional measures.
No Party shall impose a provisional compensatory duty until after sixty business days have elapsed from the date of publication of the initial resolution in its respective official dissemination body.
Article 9-20 : Amendments to national legislation.
When a Party decides to amend, add or repeal its legal provisions regarding unfair international trade practices, it shall notify the other Parties immediately after its publication in their respective official dissemination body.
The reforms, additions or abrogations will be compatible with the international regulations mentioned in article 9-03.
The Party that considers that the reforms, additions or abrogations are in violation of the provisions of this chapter, may resort to the dispute resolution mechanism of chapter XIX.
Article 9-21 : Substantiation of the procedure.
The Parties will substantiate the investigation procedures on unfair practices, through the competent national agencies, agencies or public entities, exclusively.
Article 9-22 : Settlement of disputes.
When the final decision of an arbitral tribunal declares that the application of a countervailing fee by a Party is inconsistent with any provision of this chapter, the Party shall cease to apply or adjust the countervailing fee in question with respect to the property of the Party or Complaining parties.
CHAPTER X : General principles on trade in services
Article 10-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
trade in services: the provision of a service:
a) from the territory of one Party to the territory of another Party;
b) in the territory of a Party to a consumer of another Party;
c) through the presence of companies providing services of one Party in the territory of another Party;
d) by physical or natural persons of a Party in the territory of another Party.
enterprise of a Party: an enterprise incorporated or organized under the laws of a Party, including branches located in the territory of a Party that carry out economic activities in that territory;
measures that a Party adopts or maintains: measures adopted or maintained by:
a) federal or central, state or departmental governments; Y
b) non-governmental organizations that exercise regulatory, administrative or other powers of a governmental nature that have been delegated to them by those governments.
service provider of a Party: a person of a Party who intends to provide or provides a service;
quantitative restriction: a non-discriminatory measure that imposes limitations on:
a) the number of service providers, whether through a quota, monopoly or an economic necessity test or by any other quantitative means; either
b) the operations of any service provider, whether through a fee or an economic need test, or by any other quantitative means.
professional services: services that require education or higher education or training for their provision and whose exercise is authorized or restricted by a Party, but does not include services provided by those who practice a trade or to the crew of merchant ships and aircraft.
Article 10-02 : Scope of application.
This Chapter applies to measures that a Party adopts or maintains on trade in services carried out by service providers of another Party, including those related to:
a) the production, distribution, marketing, sale and provision of a service;
b) the purchase, use or payment of a service;
c) access to and use of distribution and transportation systems;
d) access to public telecommunications services and the use of their networks;
e) the presence in its territory of a service provider of another Party; Y
f) The granting of a bond or other form of financial guarantee, as a condition for the provision of a service.
This chapter does not apply to:
a) subsidies or grants provided by a Party or a State enterprise, including government-supported loans, guarantees and insurance;
b) non-commercial services or government functions such as law enforcement, social rehabilitation services, income security or insurance, social security or insurance, social welfare, public education, public training, health and care for children;
c) financial services.
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to:
a) impose on a Party any obligation with respect to a national of another Party who intends to enter its labor market or who has permanent employment in the territory of the receiving Party, nor to confer any right on that national, with respect to that access or job;
b) impose any obligation or grant any right to a Party, with respect to government purchases made by a Party or a State enterprise referred to in Chapter XV.
The provisions of this chapter shall apply to the measures related to the services contemplated in annexes 1 and 2 to this article, only to the extent and terms established in those annexes.
Article 10-03 : Transparency.
Each Party shall publish promptly and, except in emergency situations, no later than the date of its entry into force, all relevant laws, regulations, administrative guidelines and other decisions, resolutions or measures of general application that refer to or affect the operation of this chapter, and have been put into effect by governmental institutions of the Party or by a non-governmental regulatory body of the Party. International agreements that refer to trade in services or affect it and those that are a development of this Agreement will also be published.
When the publication of the information referred to in paragraph 1 is not feasible or practical, it will be made available to the public in another way.
Each Party shall promptly inform the other Parties, at least annually, of the establishment of new laws, regulations or administrative guidelines that significantly affect the trade in services covered by its specific commitments under this Chapter, or of the modifications that it introduces. .
Each Party shall respond promptly to all requests for specific information made by the other Parties about all the measures mentioned in paragraph 1. In addition, each Party shall establish one or more centers to provide specific information to the other Parties that request it on all these issues, as well as those that are subject to the information obligation provided for in paragraph 3.
Article 10-04 : National treatment.
Each Party shall grant the services, as well as the providers of those services of another Party, treatment no less favorable than that granted, in similar circumstances, to its services or service providers.
Treatment accorded by a Party pursuant to paragraph 1 means, with respect to a state or department, treatment no less favorable than the most favorable treatment that state or department accords, in like circumstances, to service providers of the Party. Part of which is a member.
Article 10-05 : Most favored nation treatment.
Each Party shall accord to the services, as well as to the providers of those services, of another Party, treatment no less favorable than that accorded, in similar circumstances, to the services and to the providers of services of any other Party or of any country that is not Part.
The provisions of this Chapter shall not be construed to prevent a Party from conferring or granting advantages to countries with which it has a land border for the purpose of facilitating exchanges, limited to contiguous border areas, of services that are produced and consumed locally. .
Article 10-06 : Non-mandatory local presence.
No Party shall require a service provider of another Party to establish or maintain a representative office or other type of business, or to reside in its territory as a condition of providing a service.
Article 10-07 : Consolidation of measures.
No Party shall increase the degree of non-conformity of its existing measures with respect to Articles 10-04 to 10-06. Any amendment to these measures will not decrease the degree of compliance of the measure as it was in effect immediately prior to the amendment.
Within the eight months following the signing of the Treaty, the Parties will sign a Protocol that will consist of two lists that will contain the agreements of the negotiations that the Parties carry out during those eight months.
List 1 will contain the sectors and subsectors that each Party will reserve from compliance with the obligations established in paragraph 1.
List 2 will contain the federal and central measures inconsistent with articles 10-04 to 10-06 that each Party decides to maintain.
Within the two years following the signing of the Treaty, the Parties will sign a Protocol in which they will record state and departmental measures that do not conform to articles 10-04 to 10-06.
The Parties will not have the obligation to register the municipal measures.
Article 10-08 : Non-discriminatory quantitative restrictions.
The Parties will seek to negotiate periodically, at least every two years, the release or elimination of existing quantitative restrictions that they maintain at the federal or central, state or departmental level.
Within the year following the date of entry into force of this Agreement, the Parties will sign a Protocol that will contain the quantitative restrictions referred to in paragraph 1.
Each Party shall notify the other Parties of any quantitative restrictions, other than those at the municipal government level, that it adopts after the date of entry into force of this Agreement, and shall record the restriction in the Protocol referred to in paragraph 2.
The agreements resulting from the negotiation for the release referred to in paragraph 1 will be registered in Protocols.
Article 10-09 : Future release.
Through future negotiations that will be convened by the Commission, the Parties will deepen the liberalization achieved in the different service sectors, with a view to achieving the elimination of the remaining restrictions registered in accordance with article 10-07, paragraphs 3 to 5, and a global balance in the commitments.
Article 10-10 : Release of non-discriminatory measures.
The Parties may negotiate the release of quantitative restrictions, licensing requirements and other non-discriminatory measures. The commitments acquired will be recorded in a Protocol signed by the Parties.
Article 10-11 : Reciprocity and global balance.
The Parties, in the negotiations referred to in articles 10-07, 10-08 and 10-10, will seek to reach agreements on the basis of reciprocity, aimed at achieving a global balance in the concessions granted.
Article 10-12 : Procedures.
No later than one month after the date of entry into force of this Agreement, the Parties shall jointly establish procedures to carry out the negotiations that will lead to the elaboration of the Protocols mentioned in articles 10-07, 10-08 and 10- 10, as well as for the communication of the measures contemplated in articles 10-07, paragraph 6 and 10-08, paragraphs 2 and 3.
Article 10-13 : Technical cooperation.
The Parties, within the following twenty-four months from the entry into force of this Agreement, shall establish a system to provide service providers with information regarding their markets in relation to:
a) the commercial and technical aspects of the provision of services;
b) the possibility of obtaining technology in terms of services; Y
c) those aspects that the Commission considers pertinent on this subject.
The Commission will recommend to the Parties the adoption of the necessary measures for due compliance with the provisions of paragraph 1.
Article 10-14 : Granting of licenses and certificates.
In order to ensure that any measure that a Party adopts or maintains in relation to the requirements and procedures for the granting of licenses or certifications to nationals of another Party does not constitute an unnecessary barrier to trade, each Party shall endeavor to ensure that such measures:
a) are based on objective and transparent criteria, such as the capacity and aptitude to provide a service;
b) are not more burdensome than necessary to ensure the quality of a service; Y
c) do not constitute a disguised restriction on the cross-border provision of a service.
When a Party revalidates or recognizes, unilaterally or by agreement with another country, licenses or certificates obtained in the territory of another Party or of any country that is not a Party:
a) nothing in Article 10-05 shall be construed to require that Party to revalidate or recognize education or studies, licenses or certificates or degrees obtained in the territory of another Party; Y
b) the Party shall provide any other Party with an adequate opportunity to demonstrate the reasons why the education or studies, licences, certificates or titles obtained in the territory of that Party should also be revalidated or recognized, or to negotiate or enter into an agreement have equivalent effects.
Each Party, within a period of two years from the date of entry into force of this Agreement, shall eliminate any requirement of nationality or permanent residence that it maintains for the granting of licenses, certificates or titles to professional service providers. from elsewhere. When a Party fails to comply with this obligation with respect to a particular sector, any other Party shall have, in the same sector and for the same period of time as the non-compliant Party, as its sole remedy the right to:
a) maintain a requirement equivalent to that included in the list referred to in article 10-07, paragraph 5.
b) reset:
i) any such requirements at the central or federal level that it has eliminated in accordance with this article; either
ii) any of those requirements at the state or departmental level that would have been in force on the date of entry into force of this Agreement, by means of communication to the non-compliant Party.
The annex to article 10-02 establishes procedures for the recognition of studies or education and experience, as well as other rules and requirements that govern professional service providers.
Article 10-15 : Denial of benefits.
A Party may, prior communication and consultation, deny the benefits derived from this chapter to a service provider of another Party, when it determines that the service is being provided by a company that does not carry out important business activities in the territory of any of the Parties. Parties and that, in addition, is owned or controlled by persons of a country that is not a Party.
Annex 1 to article 10-02 : Professional services
For the purposes of this annex, professional practice shall mean: the habitual performance of any professional act or the provision of any service specific to each profession that requires authorization in accordance with the legislation of each Party.
This annex will apply to all measures related to the criteria for the granting and mutual recognition of:
a) certificates or academic titles required in each Party for professional practice;
b) professional certificates or cards or any other type of authorization or requirement necessary for professional practice in accordance with the legislation of each Party.
The purpose of this annex is to establish the rules that the Parties will observe to gradually reduce and eliminate in their territory the barriers to the provision of professional services between them;
The Parties agree that the granting and mutual recognition processes referred to in paragraph 2 will be based on raising the quality of professional services through the establishment of standards and criteria for these processes while protecting consumers and safeguarding the public interest.
Each Party shall ensure that the relevant bodies, including the competent government agencies and professional associations and colleges, develop such criteria and standards referred to in paragraph 4 and formulate and submit recommendations on mutual recognition.
The elaboration of criteria and norms referred to in paragraphs 4 and 5, may consider the following elements: education or studies, examinations, experience, conduct and ethics, professional development and updating, renewal or updating of the documents or acts to which refers to paragraph 2, field of action, local knowledge and consumer protection.
In order to facilitate recognition or revalidation with the appropriate legality and justification, within six months from the entry into force of this Treaty, the Commission will establish a working group with the participation of the competent educational authorities of the Parties to establish a university information system that contains at least the following elements:
a) Higher Education institutions authorized by each Party;
b) academic programs and degrees offered;
c) characteristics and content of the academic programs; Y
d) other elements that the working group considers pertinent.
In order to put into practice the provisions of paragraphs 4 to 6, the Parties will provide the detailed and necessary information for the granting and mutual recognition of the documents and acts referred to in paragraph 2, including that corresponding to: academic courses, guides and study materials, payment of rights, exam dates, schedules, locations, affiliation with societies and/or professional associations. This information will include federal or central, state or departmental legislation, administrative guidelines and measures of general application and those prepared by governmental and non-governmental organizations.
Each Party shall endeavor to have the competent authority adopt the recommendations made pursuant to paragraph 5 to the extent that they are consistent with the provisions of this Agreement.
The Parties shall review at least once every three years, the application of the provisions of this annex.
Annex 2 to article 10-02 : Transport
The provisions of this chapter do not apply to air services, including national and international air transport, with and without a fixed itinerary, nor to auxiliary activities in support of air services, except:
a) aircraft repair and major maintenance services, subject to reciprocity;
b) specialized air services; Y
c) computerized reservation systems.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 1, the Parties undertake to develop and expand passenger and cargo air transport relations between them, in order to seek free market access. This will be carried out within the framework of the bilateral agreements between the Parties.
The Parties will have free access to cargo of any nature, transported by sea, generated by their foreign trade through national flag vessels, those operated, chartered or leased by their shipping companies, as well as those reputed to be the national flag in accordance with their own legislation.
The Parties will make multimodal transport regulations compatible in those aspects that require it.
The Parties will make efforts to advance in the study of measures that contribute to the development of land transport between them.
CHAPTER XI : Telecommunications
Article 11-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it is understood by:
intra- business communications: telecommunications through which a company communicates within itself or with its subsidiaries, branches and, according to the internal laws and regulations of each Party, with its affiliates, or these communicate with each other. For such purposes, the terms subsidiaries, branches and, where appropriate, affiliates shall be interpreted in accordance with the definition of the Party in question. Intra-company communications do not include commercial or non-commercial services provided to companies that are not subsidiaries, branches or related affiliates, or that are offered to clients or potential clients and, in general, to different moral or legal persons.
public telecommunications transport network: the physical infrastructure that allows the provision of public telecommunications services.
value-added services: telecommunications services that use computerized processing systems that act on the format, content, code, protocol or similar aspects of the information transmitted by the user, creating a new service different from the basic service and, to this extent, providing the client with additional, different or restructured information; or involving user interaction with stored information.
public telecommunications transport service: any telecommunications transport service that a Party expressly or de facto establishes, which is offered to the general public. Such services may include telegraph, telephone, telex, carrier service, and data transmission services, which typically involve the real-time transmission of customer-supplied information between two or more points without any end-to-end change in form. or content of that information.
telecommunications: any transmission, emission or reception of signs, signals, writings, images, sounds or information of any nature by wire, radioelectricity, optical means or other electromagnetic systems.
Article 11-02 : General principles.
The Parties acknowledge:
a) the right of each of them to regulate the provision of services in its territory, and to establish new regulations in this regard, in order to achieve the objectives of its national policy;
b) the specific characteristics of the telecommunications services sector and, in particular, its double function as an independent sector of economic activity and a fundamental means of supporting other economic activities.
Article 11-03 : Scope of application.
This Chapter applies to measures by each Party:
a) for the provision of value-added telecommunications services, under the terms established in article 11-05;
b) that affect access to public telecommunications transport networks and services and their use by value-added service providers;
c) that adopts or maintains related to the standardization of connection of terminal equipment or other equipment or system to public telecommunications networks.
This Chapter does not apply to any measure that a Party adopts or maintains in connection with the broadcasting or cable distribution of radio and television programming, or the provision of basic telecommunications services.
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to:
a) compel a Party to authorize a person of another Party to establish, build, acquire, lease, operate or supply telecommunications transport networks or services;
b) compel a Party to establish, build, acquire, lease, operate or provide telecommunications transport networks or services that are not offered to the general public, or to require any person to do so;
c) prevent a Party from prohibiting persons who operate private networks from using one of such networks to provide public telecommunications networks or services to third parties;
d) compel a Party to require any person who broadcasts or distributes radio or television programs by cable to provide its broadcasting or cable distribution infrastructure as a public telecommunications network.
In case of inconsistency between the provisions of this chapter and any other of this Agreement, the provisions of this chapter shall prevail to the extent of the inconsistency.
Article 11-04 : Access to public telecommunications transport networks and services and their use.
Each Party shall guarantee that any service provider of another Party is granted, under reasonable and non-discriminatory terms and conditions, in accordance with the rules established in the Party in question, access to public telecommunications transport networks and services. and the use thereof, for the supply of value-added services. This obligation will be fulfilled, among other ways, through the application of paragraphs 2 to 9.
Each Party shall endeavor to ensure that pricing for access to and use of public telecommunications transport networks and services is cost-based;
Each Party shall ensure that the service providers of the other Parties have access to and use any public telecommunications transport network or service offered within or through its borders, including private leased circuits. For these purposes, each Party shall ensure, without prejudice to the provisions of paragraphs 7 and 8, that these providers are allowed:
a) purchase or lease and connect the terminal equipment or other equipment that interfaces with the network and is necessary to provide the provider's services;
b) use the operating protocols chosen by the service provider to supply any service that is not necessary to ensure the availability of telecommunications transport networks and services for the general public.
Nothing in paragraphs 2 and 3 shall be construed to prevent cross-subsidization between public telecommunications transport services.
Each Party shall ensure that persons of another Party may have access to and use of public telecommunications networks or services to transmit information in its territory or across its borders, including for intra-business communications and for access to information contained in databases or stored in any other form that is readable by a machine in the territory of any Party, provided they are for private and exclusive use, without providing services to third parties and making the international connection through entities authorized to provide international basic services.
Notwithstanding paragraph 5, the Parties may take such measures as may be necessary to ensure the security and confidentiality of messages, provided that such measures are not applied in a manner that constitutes a means of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination or a disguised restriction on international trade in services.
Bearing in mind that access to public telecommunications transport networks and services and their use does not involve authorization to provide these services and that authorization is required in all cases, each Party shall guarantee that no further conditions are imposed on users. for access to public telecommunications transport networks or services and for their use, than those necessary for:
a) safeguard the public service responsibilities of providers of public telecommunications services or telecommunications networks, in particular their ability to make their networks or services available to the general public;
b) protect the technical integrity of public telecommunications networks or services; Y
c) guarantee that the service providers of the other Parties only supply value-added services when allowed in accordance with the commitments set forth in this chapter.
In the event that they satisfy the criteria established in paragraph 7, the conditions for access to their networks and services may include the following:
a) restrictions placed on the resale or sharing of such services;
b) the requirement to use specified technical interfaces, including interface protocols, for interconnection with such networks and services;
c) requirements when necessary, for the interoperability of such services and to promote the achievement of the objectives set out in article 11-08, paragraph 2;
d) type approval of terminal equipment or other equipment that interfaces with the network and technical requirements for the connection of that equipment to those networks;
e) restrictions imposed on the interconnection of private, leased or owned circuits with those networks or services, or with circuits leased by another service provider; either
f) communication, registration or licensing procedures.
Notwithstanding paragraphs 1 through 8, a Party may impose conditions on access to and use of public telecommunications transport networks and services that are reasonable, non-discriminatory, and necessary to strengthen its national telecommunications infrastructure and their ability to provide telecommunications services and to increase their participation in international trade in these services.
Article 11-05 : Conditions for the provision of value-added services.
Considering the strategic role of value-added services to increase the competitiveness of all economic activities in the region, the Parties will establish the necessary conditions for their provision, taking into account the procedures and information required for this purpose.
Each Party shall ensure that:
a) any procedure that it adopts or maintains to grant licenses, permits, registrations or communications regarding the provision of these services is transparent and non-discriminatory and that the requests are processed expeditiously; Y
b) the information required under such procedures is limited to that necessary to prove that the applicant has the financial and technical solvency to start rendering the service and that the applicant's services and terminal equipment or other equipment comply with the technical or regulations applicable in the Part.
No Party shall require a provider of these services:
a) Provide them to the general public, when they have been contracted by specific users and under defined technical conditions, or aimed at them;
b) justify their rates according to their costs;
c) interconnect their networks with any client or network in particular; either
d) Satisfy any particular standard or technical regulation, except for connection to a public telecommunications network, in which case the pertinent recommendations of the International Telecommunication Union will be taken into account.
Each Party may require the registration of a fee to:
a) a service provider, in order to correct a practice of this provider that the Party has considered in a particular case as anti-competitive, in accordance with its national legislation; either
b) a monopoly, to which the provisions of article 11-07 apply.
Article 11-06 : Measures related to standardization.
Each Party shall guarantee that within the measures related to standardization that refer to the connection of terminal equipment or other equipment or systems to public telecommunications networks, including those measures that refer to the use of test and measurement equipment for the procedure of conformity assessment, include at least those necessary for:
a) avoid technical damage to public telecommunications networks;
b) avoid technical interference with public telecommunications services or their deterioration;
c) avoid electromagnetic interference and ensure compatibility with other uses of the electromagnetic spectrum;
d) prevent billing equipment from malfunctioning; either
e) guarantee user security and access to public telecommunications networks or services and interworking with them.
The Parties may establish the approval requirement for terminal equipment or other systems and equipment, when these are intended to be connected to the public telecommunications network, provided that the approval criteria are compatible with the provisions of paragraph 1.
The user's terminal equipment may be approved or its approval may be required, according to the applicable conditions for connection to the public telecommunications network of the Party, in accordance with the provisions of this article. Terminal equipment type-approved by an authority recognized by the Party concerned shall be sufficient and no Party shall require additional authorization on type-approval aspects.
Each Party shall ensure that the end points of public telecommunications networks are defined on a reasonable and transparent basis.
Each Party, in relation to approval:
a) ensure that its conformity assessment procedures are transparent and non-discriminatory and that applications submitted for this purpose are processed expeditiously;
b) allow any technically qualified entity registered in the Parties to perform the required test on the terminal equipment or other equipment or system that will be connected to the public telecommunications network, in accordance with the evaluation procedures of the Party, without prejudice the company's right to review the accuracy and completeness of the test results; Y
c) shall ensure that the measures it adopts or maintains to authorize persons acting as agents of telecommunications equipment suppliers before the competent bodies for conformity assessment of the Party are not discriminatory.
Within the twelve months following the entry into force of this Agreement, each Party, through the Group of Three High-Level Telecommunications Group, shall adopt among its conformity assessment procedures, the necessary provisions to accept the results of the tests carried out, based on their established rules and procedures, by laboratories authorized and recognized by competent entities, which are located in the territory of another Party.
The Parties, through the High Level Telecommunications Group of the Group of Three, will design the work program for the implementation of the guidelines contained in this chapter and established in accordance with the provisions of this article.
Article 11-07 : Monopolies.
When a Party maintains or establishes a monopoly to provide public telecommunications networks and services, and that monopoly competes, directly or through subsidiaries, in the manufacture or sale of telecommunications goods, in the provision of value-added services, or other services telecommunications, the Party shall ensure that the monopoly does not use its monopoly position to engage in anti-competitive practices in those markets, either directly or through dealings with its affiliates, in such a way as to disadvantageously affect a person of other part. The prohibitions may refer to cross-subsidies between companies, behaviors that lead to abuse of dominant position and discriminatory access to public telecommunications networks and services.
Each Party shall adopt or maintain effective measures to prevent the anticompetitive conduct referred to in paragraph 1, such as:
a) accounting requirements;
b) structural separation requirements;
c) rules to ensure that the monopoly grants its competitors access to its networks or its telecommunications services, and the use of them, on terms and conditions no less favorable than those granted to itself or its subsidiaries; either
d) rules to ensure timely disclosure of technical changes in public telecommunications networks and their interfaces.
Each Party shall inform the other Parties of the measures referred to in paragraph 2.
Article 11-08 : Relationship with international organizations and agreements.
The Parties will do their best to stimulate the performance of regional and subregional organizations and promote them as forums to promote the development of telecommunications in the region.
The Parties, recognizing the importance of international standards to achieve global compatibility and interoperability of telecommunications networks or services, undertake to promote the application of standards issued by competent international organizations, such as the International Telecommunication Union and the International Organization for Standardization.
In case there are particular or joint technological developments of the Parties, the mechanisms tending to the application of regional standards related to these developments will be established.
Article 11-09 : Technical cooperation.
In order to stimulate the development of interoperable telecommunications infrastructure and services, the Parties will cooperate in the exchange of technological information, in the development of human resources in the sector, as well as in the creation and development of business exchange programs. , academic and intergovernmental.
The Parties shall encourage and support cooperation in the field of telecommunications at the international, regional and sub-regional levels.
Article 11-10 : Transparency.
Each Party shall make available to the public and to the other Parties information on measures relating to access to and use of public telecommunications networks or services, including measures relating to:
a) rates and other terms and conditions of service;
b) specifications of the technical interfaces with those services and networks;
c) information on the authorities responsible for the preparation and adoption of measures related to standardization that affect such access and use;
d) conditions applicable to the connection of terminal equipment or of another kind, to the public telecommunications network;
e) any communication, permit, registration or license requirements.
Article 11-11 : Denial of benefits.
A Party may deny the benefits of this chapter:
a) to a person of another Party that supplies value-added services, if it determines that the service and the facilities inherent to its provision are located in the territory of a country that is not a party to this Agreement; either
b) to a service provider that is a moral or legal person, if it establishes that the ownership or control of that person corresponds ultimately to persons from a country that is not a party.
Article 11-12 : Release schedule for value-added services.
For value-added services, the provisions of Chapter X shall apply.
The release of value-added services will be based on the following schedule:
a) each Party, upon the entry into force of this Agreement, shall permit:
i) cross-border provision of value-added services, with the exception of videotext services and enhanced packet-switched services;
ii) investment, up to 100%, by physical or natural persons or legal entities, including state companies of another Party, in companies established or to be established in its territory for the provision of value-added services, with exception of videotext services and enhanced packet-switched services;
b) the limitations established in literal a), regarding the videotext services and enhanced packet switching services, will be eliminated from the 1st. July 1995.
Article 11-13 : Other provisions.
Subject to the analysis of the integration achieved in value-added services, the Parties within the two years following the entry into force of this Agreement will make the pertinent consultations to determine the deepening and expansion of the coverage of the free trade area of ​​services. of telecommunications.
CHAPTER XII : Financial services
Article 12-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
company: any entity incorporated or organized under applicable law, whether or not for profit and privately or government owned, including companies, shares, sole proprietorships, joint ventures or other associations.
public entity: a central bank, or monetary authority of a Party, or any financial institution of a public nature owned or controlled by a Party.
financial institution: any financial intermediary or other enterprise that is authorized to do financial business and is regulated or supervised as a financial institution under the laws of the Party in whose territory it is located.
financial institution of another Party: a financial institution, located in the territory of a Party that is controlled by persons of another Party.
investment:
a) a company;
b) shares of a company;
c) a share in a company that entitles the owner to participate in the income or profits of the company;
d) a participation in a company that gives the owner the right to participate in the social assets of that company in a liquidation;
e) real estate or immovable property or other assets, tangible or intangible, acquired or used for the purpose of obtaining an economic benefit or for other business purposes; Y
f) benefits from allocating capital or other resources to the development of an economic activity in the territory of another Party, in accordance with, among others:
i) contracts involving the presence in the territory of another Party of assets of an investor, such as concessions, construction contracts and turnkey contracts; either
ii) contracts in which the consideration depends substantially on the production, income or profit of a company.
It will not be understood by investment:
a) pecuniary claims derived exclusively from:
i) commercial contracts for the sale of goods or services by a national or company in the territory of a Party to a company in the territory of another Party; either
ii) the granting of credit in connection with a commercial transaction, such as trade financing; either
b) any other pecuniary claim that does not entail the types of rights provided in the literals of the definition of investment;
c) a loan granted by a financial institution or a debt security owned by a financial institution, except in the case of a loan to a financial institution or a debt security of a financial institution that is treated as capital for regulatory purposes by the Party in whose territory the financial institution is located.
disputing investor: an investor of a Party that makes a claim under the terms of the rules relating to the settlement of disputes between a Party and an investor of another Party.
investment of an investor of a Party: an investment owned or controlled directly or indirectly by an investor of that Party in the territory of another Party.
non-Party investment: the investment of an investor that is not an investor of a Party.
investor of a Party: a Party or a State enterprise thereof, or a person of that Party, that intends to make, makes or has made an investment in the territory of another Party.
measure: any action, act or decision, adopted or that may be adopted by a Party, whether in the form of a law, regulation, rule, procedure, decision or administrative provision, requirement or practice, or in any other form.
new financial service: a financial service not provided in the territory of the Party that is provided in the territory of another Party, and includes any new form of distribution of a financial service, or sale of a financial product that is not sold in the territory of the Party. Part.
self-regulatory bodies: any non-governmental entity, including any stock or futures exchange or market, clearing house or any other association or organization that exercises its own or delegated authority for regulation or supervision over financial service providers or institutions financial.
person of a Party: a national or company of a Party, does not include a branch of a company of a non-Party country.
cross-border provision of financial services or cross-border trade in financial services:
a) the provision of a financial service from the territory of one Party to the territory of another Party;
b) in the territory of a Party by a person of that Party to a person of another Party; either
c) by a person of a Party in the territory of another Party.
financial service provider of a Party: a person of a Party who is engaged in the business of providing a financial service in the territory of the Party.
cross-border financial service provider of a Party: a financial service provider of a Party that seeks to provide or provides financial services through the cross-border provision of those services.
financial service: a service of a financial nature, including insurance, reinsurance, and any related or auxiliary service to a service of a financial nature.
Article 12-02 : Scope of application.
This Chapter refers to measures by a Party relating to:
a) financial institutions of another Party;
b) investors of another Party and investments of those investors in financial institutions in the territory of the Party; Y
c) cross-border trade in financial services.
This chapter does not apply to:
a) Activities or services that are part of public retirement plans or public social security systems;
b) the use of financial resources owned by the Party;
c) other activities or services on behalf of the Party or its public entities, or with its guarantee.
Each Party undertakes to progressively and gradually release, through successive negotiations, all financial restrictions or reserves with the purpose of making economic complementarity between them effective. 4. In the event of any inconsistency between the provisions of this Chapter and any other provision of this Agreement, the provisions of this Chapter shall prevail to the extent of the inconsistency.
Articles 17-08, 17-09 and 17-13 of Chapter XVII are an integral part of this chapter.
Article 12-03 : Self- regulated bodies.
Where a Party requires a financial institution or cross-border financial service provider of another Party to be a member of, participate in, or have access to a self-regulatory body to offer a financial service in or to its territory, the Party shall do everything in its power to its scope for that body to comply with the obligations of this chapter.
Article 12-04 : Right of establishment.
The Parties recognize the principle that investors of each Party engaged in the business of providing financial services in the territory of that Party should be permitted to establish a financial institution in the territory of another Party, through any of the modalities of establishment and operation that this allows.
A Party may impose at the time of establishment, terms and conditions that are consistent with Article 12-06.
Article 12-05 : Cross-border trade.
No Party shall increase the degree of non-conformity of its measures relating to cross-border trade in financial services by cross-border financial service providers of another Party after the entry into force of this Agreement.
Each Party shall permit persons located in its territory and its nationals, wherever they may be, to purchase financial services from cross-border financial service providers of another Party located in the territory of that other Party or of another Party. This does not obligate a Party to allow those service providers to do business or advertise in its territory. Pursuant to the provisions of paragraph 1, each Party may define what is "to do business" and "advertise" for the purposes of this obligation.
Without prejudice to other means of prudential regulation of cross-border trade in financial services, a Party may require the registration of cross-border financial service providers of another Party and of financial instruments.
Article 12-06 : National treatment.
In similar circumstances, each Party shall accord to investors of another Party treatment no less favorable than that it accords to its own investors with respect to the establishment, acquisition, expansion, administration, conduct, operation and sale or other forms of alienation of financial institutions and investments in financial institutions in its territory.
In similar circumstances, each Party shall accord to financial institutions of another Party and to investments of investors of another Party in financial institutions treatment no less favorable than that it accords to its own financial institutions and to investments of its own investors in financial institutions with respect to to the establishment, acquisition, expansion, administration, management, operation and sale or other forms of alienation of financial institutions and investments.
In similar circumstances, pursuant to Article 12-05, when a Party permits the cross-border provision of a financial service, it shall accord to cross-border financial service providers of another Party treatment no less favorable than it accords to its own financial service providers with respect to the provision of of such service.
A Party's treatment of financial institutions and cross-border financial service providers of another Party, whether identical or different from that accorded to its own institutions or service providers in similar circumstances, is consistent with paragraphs 1 through 3 if it provides equality of opportunities to compete.
A Party's treatment does not provide equal opportunity to compete if, in like circumstances, it disadvantages cross-border financial institutions and financial service providers of another Party in their ability to provide financial services, compared with their ability to the Party's own financial institutions and service providers to provide those services.
Article 12-07 : Most favored nation treatment.
Each Party shall accord to investors of another Party, financial institutions of another Party, investments by investors in financial institutions, and cross-border financial service providers of another Party, in like circumstances, treatment no less favorable than that accorded to investors, financial institutions , investments of investors in financial institutions and providers of cross-border financial services of another Party or of another country that is not a Party.
Article 12-08 : Recognition and harmonization.
When applying the measures included in this chapter, a Party may recognize the prudential measures of another Party or of a country that is not a Party. That recognition may be granted unilaterally, achieved through harmonization or other means, or based on an agreement or arrangement with the other Party or with the non-Party country.
The Party granting recognition of prudential measures in accordance with paragraph 1 shall provide appropriate opportunities for any other Party to demonstrate that there are circumstances for which there are or will be equivalent regulations, supervision and enforcement of the regulation, and if appropriate, procedures for sharing information between the Parties.
Where a Party grants recognition of prudential measures in accordance with paragraph 1 and the circumstances set forth in paragraph 2 exist, the Party shall provide appropriate opportunities for another Party to negotiate accession to the agreement or arrangement, or to negotiate a similar agreement or arrangement. .
Article 12-09 : Exceptions.
Nothing in this Agreement shall be construed as preventing a Party from adopting or maintaining reasonable prudential measures of a financial nature for reasons such as:
a) protect fund takers, as well as investors, depositors or other creditors, holders or beneficiaries of policies or creditors of fiduciary obligations in charge of a financial institution or a provider of cross-border financial services;
b) maintain the safety, soundness, integrity or financial responsibility of financial institutions or cross-border financial service providers; Y
c) ensure the integrity and stability of the financial system of that Party.
Nothing of the provisions of chapters X, XI, XIII, XVI, XVII of this Treaty applies to non-discriminatory measures of general application, adopted by public entities that are in charge of adopting or directing monetary policies or related credit policies. , or exchange policies. This paragraph shall not affect the obligations of a Party under Articles 17-04, 17-07 and 12-18.
Notwithstanding any other provision of this Agreement that allows a Party to restrict transfers, and notwithstanding the provisions of Article 12-18, paragraphs 1 through 3, a Party may prevent or limit transfers from a financial institution or provider of cross-border financial services to, an affiliate or a person related to, or for the benefit of, that institution or that service provider, through the fair and non-discriminatory application of measures related to maintaining the safety, soundness, integrity or financial liability of financial institutions or cross-border financial service providers.
Article 12-06 shall not apply to the granting of exclusive rights by a Party to a financial institution to provide one of the financial services referred to in Article 12-02, paragraph 2, letter a).
Article 12-10 : Transparency.
Each Party shall ensure that any measure it adopts on matters related to this Chapter is officially published or timely disclosed to the recipients thereof by some other written means.
The regulatory authorities of each Party will make available to interested parties the requirements to fill out an application for the provision of financial services.
At the request of the applicant, the regulatory authority will inform him about the status of his application. When that authority requires additional information from the applicant, it will communicate it without undue delay.
The regulatory authorities of each Party shall issue, within a period of 120 days, an administrative resolution regarding a complete application related to the provision of a financial service, presented by an investor in a financial institution, by a financial institution or by a provider of cross-border financial services of another Party. The authority will notify the interested party, without delay, of the resolution. The application will not be considered complete until all relevant hearings are held and all necessary information is received. When it is not feasible to issue a resolution within the 120-day period, the regulatory authority will notify the interested party without undue delay and will subsequently seek to issue the resolution within a reasonable period of time.
Nothing in this chapter requires a Party to either disclose or allow access to:
a) information relating to the financial affairs and accounts of individual clients of financial institutions or of cross-border financial service providers; either
b) any confidential information the disclosure of which would hinder law enforcement, or otherwise be contrary to the public interest, or harm the legitimate business interests of particular companies.
Each Party will maintain or establish one or more consultation centers, within 360 days after the entry into force of this Agreement, to respond as soon as possible to all reasonable questions from interested persons regarding the measures of general application adopted by that Party. part in connection with this chapter.
Article 12-11 : Financial Services Committee.
The Parties create the Financial Services Committee. The principal representative of each Party shall be an official of the competent authority of that Party.
The committee:
a) supervise the application of this chapter and its further development;
b) consider the aspects related to financial services that are presented to it by a Party;
c) will participate in dispute resolution procedures in accordance with articles 12-19 and 12-20;
d) Facilitate the exchange of information between supervisory authorities and cooperate, in terms of advice on prudential regulation, seeking the harmonization of regulatory frameworks as well as other policies when deemed appropriate.
The Committee will meet at least once a year to evaluate the operation of this Agreement with respect to financial services.
CHAPTER XII: Financial services
Article 12-12 : Consultations.
Each Party may request consultations with another regarding any matter related to this Agreement that affects financial services. The other Party shall favorably consider such request. The consulting Parties shall inform the Committee of the results of their consultations during the meetings it holds.
Officials from the competent authorities of the Parties will participate in the consultations provided for in this article.
Each Party may request that the regulatory authorities of another Party intervene in consultations conducted pursuant to this Article, to discuss measures of general application of that other Party that may affect the operations of cross-border financial institutions or financial service providers. in the territory of the Party that requested the consultation.
Nothing in this article shall be construed to oblige the regulatory authorities involved in inquiries pursuant to paragraph 3, to disclose information or to act in a manner that could interfere in particular regulatory, supervisory, administrative or application of measures.
In cases where, for supervisory purposes, a Party needs information on a financial institution in the territory of another Party or on cross-border financial service providers in the territory of another Party, the Party may turn to the responsible regulatory authority in the territory of the Party. another Party to request the information.
Article 12-13 : New financial services and data processing.
Each Party shall permit a financial institution of another Party to provide any new financial services of a type similar to those that that Party allows its financial institutions to provide, in accordance with its laws in similar circumstances. The Party may decide the institutional and legal modality through which said service is offered and may require authorization for its provision. When such authorization is required, the respective resolution will be issued within a reasonable period of time and authorization may only be denied for prudential reasons.
Each Party shall allow financial institutions of another Party to transfer information for processing within or outside the territory of the Party, using any of the means authorized by the Party, when necessary to carry out the ordinary business activities of those Parties. institutions.
Article 12-14 : Senior business management and management bodies.
No Party may compel financial institutions of another Party to hire personnel of any particular nationality to fill senior business management positions or other essential positions.
No Party may require that the board of directors or the board of directors of a financial institution of another Party be composed of a greater than simple majority of nationals of that Party, of residents in its territory, or of a combination of both.
Article 12-15 : Preparation of reservations.
The Parties will prepare, within eight months following the entry into force of this Agreement, a Protocol in which each Party will include reservations to Articles 12-04 to 12-07 and 12-14.
Those reservations will include the measures with respect to which neither Party will increase the degree of non-conformity with those articles as of the date of entry into force of this Agreement. Any amendment to any of those measures will not decrease the degree of compliance of the measure as it was in effect immediately prior to the amendment;
The reservations referred to in paragraph 1 shall contain the following elements:
a) sector refers to sectors for which each Party has adopted a reservation;
b) subsector refers to the specific sector in which the reservation has been taken;
c) industrial classification refers to the activity covered by the reservation, in accordance with the national industrial classification codes, when applicable;
d) type of reservation specifies the obligation among those mentioned in paragraph 1, about which a reservation is taken;
e) level of government indicates the level of government that maintains the measure on which the reservation is maintained;
f) measures identifies the measures that apply to the sector, subsector or activities covered by the reservation;
g) description describes the coverage of the sector, subsector or activities covered by the reservation.
h) phasing out refers to commitments, if any, for liberalization after the date of entry into force of this Agreement.
In the interpretation of a reservation, all the elements of the reservation will be considered.
When a Party has established, in chapters X, XI, XIII, XVI and XVII of this Agreement, a reservation to issues related to the right of establishment, cross-border trade, national treatment, most favored nation treatment, and business senior management and bodies of administration, the reservation will be understood to be made to articles from 04-12 to 07-12 and 12-14, as the case may be, to the extent that the measure, sector, subsector or activity specified in the reservation are covered by this chapter. .
Article 12-16 : Denial of benefits.
A Party may partially or totally deny the benefits derived from this Chapter to a financial service provider of another Party or to a cross-border financial service provider of another Party, prior communication and consultation, in accordance with Articles 12-10 and 12. -12, when the Party determines that the service is being provided by a company that does not carry out important business activities in the territory of any of the Parties or that is owned or controlled by persons from a country that is not a Party, without prejudice of what is established in the annex to this article.
Article 12-17 : Transfers.
Each Party shall allow all transfers related to the investment in its territory of an investor of another Party to be made freely and without delay. Those transfers include:
a) profits, dividends, interest, capital gains, royalty payments, administration expenses, technical assistance and other charges, profits in kind and other amounts derived from the investment;
b) products derived from the sale or liquidation, total or partial, of the investment;
c) payments made pursuant to a contract to which an investor or his investment is a party;
d) payments made in accordance with the article relating to expropriation and compensation; Y
e) payments that come from the settlement of disputes between a Party and an investor of another Party.
Each Party will allow transfers to be made in freely convertible currency, at the exchange rate prevailing in the market on the transfer date for cash transactions of the currency to be transferred, without prejudice to the provisions of article 12- 18.
No Party may require its investors to make transfers of their income, profits, or profits or other amounts derived from investments carried out in the territory of another Party, or attributable to them.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2, each Party may prevent transfers, through the equitable, non-discriminatory application of its laws in the following cases:
a) bankruptcy, insolvency or protection of the rights of creditors;
b) issue, trade, and operations of securities;
c) criminal or administrative offences;
d) reports of currency transfers or other monetary instruments;
e) guarantee of compliance with rulings in contentious proceedings.
Notwithstanding paragraph 1, each Party may restrict transfers of in-kind earnings, in circumstances where it could otherwise restrict those transfers as provided in this chapter.
Each Party may retain laws and regulations establishing income and supplementary taxes by means such as withholding taxes applicable to dividends and other transfers, provided they are not discriminatory.
Article 12-18 : Balance of payments and safeguard.
Each Party may adopt or maintain a measure to suspend, for a reasonable time, all or only some of the benefits contained in this chapter and in article 17-07, paragraph 1, when:
a) the application of any provision of this chapter or of chapter XVII results in a serious economic and financial disturbance in the territory of the Party, which cannot be adequately resolved through any other alternative measure; either
b) the balance of payments of a Party, including the state of its monetary reserves, is seriously threatened or faces serious difficulties.
The Party that suspends or intends to suspend benefits pursuant to paragraph 1 shall notify the other Parties as soon as possible:
a) what is the serious economic and financial disturbance caused by the application of this chapter or article 17-07, paragraph 1 or, as appropriate, the nature and extent of the serious threats to its balance of payments or serious difficulties that it faces;
b) the situation of the economy and foreign trade of the Party;
c) alternative measures available to you to correct the problem; Y
d) the economic policies that it adopts to face the problems mentioned in paragraph 1, as well as the direct relationship that exists between them and their solution.
The measure adopted or maintained by the Party, at all times:
a) avoid unnecessary damage to the economic, commercial and financial interests of the other Parties;
b) it will not impose greater burdens than those necessary to face the difficulties that cause the measure to be adopted or maintained;
c) it will be temporary and will be progressively released to the extent that the balance of payments, or the economic and financial situation of the Party, as the case may be, improves;
d) it will be applied trying at all times that this measure avoids discrimination between the Parties; Y
e) will endeavor to be consistent with internationally accepted criteria.
The Party that adopts a measure to suspend benefits contained in this Agreement shall inform the other Parties about the evolution of the events that gave rise to the adoption of the measure.
For the purposes of this article, reasonable time means the time during which the events described in paragraph 1 persist.
Article 12-19 : Settlement of disputes between the Parties.
In the terms in which this article modifies it, Chapter XIX applies to the solution of controversies that arise between the Parties regarding this chapter.
The Financial Services Committee shall create by consensus a list of up to fifteen individuals that includes up to five individuals from each Party, who have the necessary skills and dispositions to act as arbitrators in disputes related to this chapter. The members of this list must, in addition to meeting the requirements established in article 19-08, paragraph 2, literals b), c) and d), have specialized knowledge in matters of a financial nature or extensive experience derived from the exercise of responsibilities in the financial sector, or in its regulation.
For the purposes of constituting the arbitral tribunal referred to in article 19-09, the list referred to in paragraph 2 shall be used, except that the disputing Parties agree that individuals not included in that list may form part of the arbitral tribunal. , as long as they meet the requirements established in paragraph 2. The President will always be chosen from that list.
In any controversy in which the arbitral tribunal has found that a measure is incompatible with the obligations of this Agreement, when the suspension of benefits referred to in article 19-16 is applicable, and the measure affects:
a) only to the financial services sector, the complaining Party may suspend benefits only in that sector;
b) to the financial services sector and to any other sector, the complaining Party may suspend benefits in the financial services sector that have an effect equivalent to the effect of that measure in the financial services sector; either
c) any sector other than services, the complaining Party may not suspend benefits in the financial services sector.
Articles 12-20 : Disputes between an investor and a Party.
Except as provided in this article, the claims made by a disputing investor against a Party in relation to the obligations set forth in this chapter shall be resolved in accordance with the provisions of chapter XVII section B and with the procedural rules contained in the annex to article 17-16.
When the Party against which the claim is made invokes any of the exceptions referred to in Article 12-09, the following procedure shall be observed:
a) the arbitral tribunal shall refer the matter to the Financial Services Committee for its decision. The court may not proceed until it has received a decision from the Committee under the terms of this article or 60 days have elapsed from the date of receipt by the Committee;
b) once the matter has been received in accordance with subparagraph a), the Committee will decide whether and to what degree the exception of article 12-09 invoked is a valid defense against the investor's claim and will transmit a copy of its decision to the arbitral tribunal and the Commission. That decision will be binding on the court.
Annex to article 12-16
As of January 1, 2000, article 12-16 will read as follows:
Article 12-16: Denial of benefits.
A Party may partially or totally deny the benefits derived from this Chapter to a financial service provider of another Party or to a cross-border financial service provider of another Party, prior communication and consultation, in accordance with Articles 12-10 and 12. -12, when the Party determines that the service is being provided by a company that does not carry out important business activities in the territory of any of the Parties and that is owned or controlled by persons from a country that is not a Party.
CHAPTER XIII : Temporary entry of business people
Article 13-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
Immigration authorization: the immigration document from Mexico and the visa from Colombia and Venezuela.
labor certification: any procedure prior to migratory authorization that implies a government permit or authorization related to the labor market.
temporary entry: the entry of a business person of a Party into the territory of another Party, without the intention of establishing permanent residence.
national: a physical or natural person who has the nationality of a Party in accordance with its law.
business person: the national of a Party who participates in the trade of goods or provision of services, or in investment activities, in accordance with the categories referred to in the annex to article 13-04.
Article 13-02 : General principles.
The provisions of this chapter are intended to facilitate the temporary entry of business persons based on the principle of reciprocity and considering the need to establish transparent criteria and procedures for this purpose. All this as an instrument to ensure a preferential commercial relationship between the Parties. This chapter reflects the need to guarantee border security and to protect the work of their nationals and permanent employment in their respective territories.
Article 13-03 : General obligations.
Each Party shall apply, in accordance with Article 13-02, the measures related to this Chapter in an expeditious manner to avoid undue delay or prejudice in trade in goods and services, or in investment activities included in this Agreement.
The Parties shall develop and adopt common criteria, definitions and interpretations for the application of this Chapter.
Article 13-04 : Temporary entry authorization.
In accordance with the provisions of this chapter, including those contained in the annex to Article 13-04, each Party shall authorize the temporary entry of business persons who comply with current immigration regulations, with the other applicable measures related to health and safety. public, as well as with those referring to national security.
A Party may deny employment immigration authorization to a business person when their temporary entry adversely affects:
a) the solution of any labor conflict that exists in the place where they are employed or will be employed; either
b) the employment of any person involved in that conflict.
When a Party denies immigration authorization for employment, in accordance with paragraph 2, that Party:
a) notify the affected business person of the reasons for the refusal;
b) promptly communicate the reasons for the refusal to the Party whose national is refused entry.
No Party may adopt or maintain numerical restrictions on the migratory authorizations contemplated in this chapter.
Within the three months following the entry into force of this Agreement, the Parties will exchange the following company registers, which will be permanently updated through official communications from the competent government bodies:
a) trilateral register of companies that includes the companies of each one of the Parties;
b) trilateral registry that includes companies of one Party that have affiliates, subsidiaries or branches in the territory of another Party and transnational companies with affiliated or subsidiary branches in the territory of more than one Party.
Each Party shall limit the amount of the fees caused by the processing of temporary entry applications to the approximate cost of the processing services provided.
On the date of entry into force of the Treaty, each Party will prepare a list of the migratory measures in force in its territory.
Article 13-05 : Availability of information.
Each Party, in addition to the provisions of Article 21-02 of Chapter XXI:
a) provide the other Parties with the materials that allow them to learn about the measures related to this Chapter; Y
