b) within six months of the entry into force of this Agreement, prepare, publish and make available to interested parties, both in its territory and in that of the other Parties, a consolidated document with material explaining the requirements and procedures for temporary entry.
Each Party will compile, maintain and make available to the other Parties, in accordance with their domestic legislation, the information related to the granting of immigration authorizations issued in accordance with this chapter. This collection will include specific information for each occupation, profession or activity.
Article 13-06 : Working group.
The Parties create a Temporary Entry Working Group, made up of representatives of each of them, including immigration officials.
The Working Group will meet at least once a year to review:
a) the application and administration of this chapter;
b) the elaboration of measures that extend the facilities for the temporary entry of business persons in accordance with the principle of reciprocity;
c) exemption from labor certification tests or procedures of similar effect, for the spouse of the person to whom temporary entry has been authorized in accordance with sections B, C or D of the annex to article 13-04, when requesting work authorization; Y
d) proposals for modifications or additions to this chapter.
Article 13-07 : Settlement of disputes.
The Parties may not initiate the procedures provided for in Article 19-06 of Chapter XIX, with respect to a refusal to authorize temporary entry, nor with respect to any particular case included in Article 13-03, unless:
a) the matter refers to a recurring practice; Y
b) the affected business person has exhausted the administrative remedies available to him/her with respect to that particular matter.
The remedies mentioned in paragraph 1, literal b), will be considered exhausted when the competent authority has not issued a final resolution within six months from the start of the administrative procedure, and the issuance of the resolution has not been delayed for causes attributable to the affected business person.
Article 13-08 : Relationship with other chapters.
Except as provided in this chapter and in chapters I, II, XIX, XXI and XXIII, no provision of this Agreement shall impose any obligation on the Parties with respect to their immigration measures.
Annex to article 13-04 : Business persons
Section A - Business Visitors
Each Party shall authorize the temporary entry of the business person who, at the prior request of a company registered in the trilateral registry referred to in article 13-04, paragraph 5, literal a), intends to carry out any activity mentioned in the appendix to this section, without requiring labor certification or procedures with similar effects, provided that it complies with current immigration measures, applicable to temporary entry and exhibits:
a) proof of their nationality of a Party;
b) the prior request of a company established in the territory of one of the Parties; or documentation that proves that you will undertake such activities and indicates the purpose of your entry; Y
c) in the case of the provision of a service, proof of the international nature of the business activity that is proposed to be carried out and that the business person does not intend to enter the local labor market, demonstrating that:
i) the main source of remuneration for that activity is located outside the territory of the Party authorizing temporary entry; Y
ii) the main place of business and where most of the profits are obtained are outside this territory.
The Party will normally accept a declaration as to the principal place of business and the place of profit. When the Party requires additional verification, a letter from the employer registered in the trilateral register of companies stating these circumstances will normally be considered sufficient proof.
Each Party may authorize the temporary entry of a business person who intends to carry out an activity other than those indicated in the appendix to this annex, without requiring labor certification or procedures with similar effects, in terms no less favorable than those provided for in the current provisions of the measures indicated in the list referred to in article 13-04, paragraph 7, provided that the business person also complies with the immigration measures applicable to temporary entry.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 1 through 3, a Party may require that a business person requesting temporary entry under this section obtain, prior to entry, immigration authorization.
Section B - Investors
Each Party shall authorize temporary entry and provide the corresponding documentation to the business person who intends to establish, develop, manage or provide key technical advice or services, in supervisory, executive functions or involving essential skills, to carry out or manage a business. investment in which the business person or his company has committed, or is in the process of committing, a significant amount of capital, in accordance with the domestic legislation of each Party, provided that the business person also complies with immigration measures, applicable to temporary entry.
Neither Party may:
a) require proof of labor certification or other procedures of similar effect, as a condition for authorizing temporary entry pursuant to paragraph 1; neither
b) impose or maintain numerical restrictions in relation to temporary entry pursuant to paragraph 1.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 2, a Party may examine, at a peremptory time, the investment proposal of a business person to assess whether the investment complies with the applicable legal provisions.
Notwithstanding paragraph 2, a Party may require that a business person applying for temporary entry under this section obtain immigration authorization prior to entry.
Section C - Transfer of personnel within a company
Each Party shall authorize temporary entry and issue supporting documentation to the business person employed by a company registered in the trilateral register of companies referred to in article 13-04, paragraph 5, literal b), who intends to perform managerial, executive or that entail specialized knowledge, in that company or in one of its subsidiaries or affiliates, provided that it complies with the current immigration measures applicable to temporary entry. The Party may require that the business person has been an employee of the business, continuously, for 6 months within the year immediately preceding the filing date of the application.
No Party may require proof of labor certification or other procedures of similar effect as a condition for granting temporary entry under paragraph 1.
Notwithstanding paragraph 2, a Party may require that a business person applying for temporary entry under this section obtain immigration authorization prior to entry.
Section D - Professionals
Each Party will authorize temporary entry and issue supporting documentation to the business person who intends to carry out activities at a professional level, at the prior request of a company registered in any of the trilateral business registers referred to in article 13-04, paragraph 5, in the field of a profession indicated in the list referred to in paragraph 4 and based on the trilateral register of educational institutions referred to in paragraph 5, when the business person, in addition to meeting the requirements current immigration documents, applicable to temporary entry, show:
a) proof of their nationality of a Party; Y
b) Documentation that proves, based on the trilateral business registers, that the business person will undertake such activities and that indicates the purpose of their entry.
A Party may require that a business person applying for temporary entry under this section obtain immigration authorization prior to entry.
The temporary entry of a professional does not imply the recognition of titles or certificates, nor the granting of licenses for professional practice.
The Temporary Entry Working Group shall establish a list of professional activities to which this Annex shall apply, which shall be integrated in accordance with paragraph 5, within six months of the entry into force of this Agreement.
Within the three months following the entry into force of this Agreement, the Parties will exchange their respective registers of educational institutions, and will keep them updated through communications from the competent government bodies.
Addendum to Section A of the Addendum to Article 13-04: Categories of Business Visitors
Research and Design
- Technical, scientific and statistician researchers who carry out research independently or for a company located in the territory of another Party.
Cultivation, Manufacturing and Production
- Owners of harvesting machines who supervise a group of operators admitted in accordance with the applicable provisions.
- Purchasing and production personnel, at the managerial level, who carry out commercial operations for a company located in the territory of another Party.
Commercialization
- Market researchers and analysts who carry out research or analysis independently or for a company located in the territory of another Party.
- Trade fair and promotional staff who attend trade conventions.
Sales
- Sales representatives and agents who obtain orders or negotiate contracts for goods and services for an enterprise located in the territory of another Party, but who do not deliver the goods or provide the services.
Distribution
- Transport operators that carry out goods or passenger transport operations to the territory of a Party from the territory of another Party, or carry out cargo and goods or passenger transport operations from the territory of one Party to the territory of another, without carrying out in the territory of the Party to which entry is requested, loading or unloading operations, of goods that are in that territory or of passengers that board in it.
- Customs agents that provide advisory services in regard to facilitating the import or export of goods.
After sales services
- Installation, repair, maintenance and supervisory personnel who have the specialized technical knowledge essential to fulfill the seller's contractual obligation and who provide services, or train workers to provide those services, pursuant to a warranty or other contract of services related to the sale of commercial or industrial equipment or machinery, including computer programs purchased from a company located outside the territory of the Party from which temporary entry is requested, during the term of the guarantee or service contract.
General services
- Managerial and supervisory personnel involved in commercial operations for a company located in the territory of another Party.
- Tour bus operators entering the territory of a Party:
a) with a group of passengers on a tour bus trip that started in the territory of another Party and is going to return to it;
b) who is going to pick up a group of passengers on a tour bus trip that will take place and end for the most part in the territory of another Party; either
c) with a group of passengers in a tourist bus whose destination is in the territory of the Party to which temporary entry is requested, and that returns without passengers or with the group to transport it to the territory of another Party.
Definitions
For the purposes of this appendix, it shall be understood as:
tourist bus operator: the natural person required for the operation of the vehicle during the tourist trip, including relief personnel who accompany or join him later.
transport operator: the natural person, other than a tour bus operator, required for the operation of the vehicle during the trip, including relief personnel who accompany or join them later.
CHAPTER XIV : Technical Standards
Article 14-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, the terms presented in the sixth edition of ISO/IEC Guide 2: 1991, "General Terms and their Definitions in Relation to Standardization and Related Activities", shall have the same meaning when used in this chapter, unless they are defined differently here.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
make compatible: bring to the same level, different standardization measures but with the same scope, approved by different standardization bodies, so that they are identical, equivalent, or have the effect of allowing goods and services to be used interchangeably or for the same purpose. same purpose, in order to make it possible for those goods and services to be traded between the Parties.
standardization measures: standards, technical regulations or conformity assessment processes.
standard: the document approved by a recognized institution with standardization activities, which provides for common and repeated use, rules, guidelines or characteristics for goods or related processes and production methods or for services or their related methods of operation, and whose observance is not mandatory. It may also include or deal exclusively with terminology, symbols, packaging, marking or labeling requirements applicable to a good, service, process or related production method.
international standard: a standardization measure, or other guide or recommendation, adopted by an international standardization body and made available to the public.
legitimate objectives: among others, guaranteeing the safety and protection of human, animal and plant life and health, its environment and the prevention of practices that may mislead consumers, including matters related to the identification of goods or services, considering, among other aspects, when appropriate, fundamental factors of a climatic, geographical, technological or infrastructure type or scientific justification.
international standardization body: a standardization body, open to participation by relevant bodies of at least all parties to the GATT Agreement on Technical Barriers to Trade, including the International Organization for Standardization (ISO), the International Electrotechnical Commission (IEC), the Codex Alimentarius Commission, the World Health Organization (WHO), the International Telecommunication Union (ITU), or any other body designated by the Parties.
standardization body: a body whose standardization activities are recognized.
conformity assessment procedure: any procedure used, directly or indirectly, to determine that the relevant requirements established by technical regulations or standards have been met, including sampling, testing, inspection, evaluation, verification, assurance of conformity, accreditation , certification, registration or approval, used for such purposes, but does not mean an approval process.
approval process: registration, communication or any other mandatory administrative process to obtain a permit for a good or service to be marketed or used for defined purposes or under established conditions.
technical regulation: a document that establishes the characteristics of the goods or their related processes and production methods, or of the services or their related methods of operation, including the applicable administrative provisions, and compliance with which is mandatory. It may also include or deal exclusively with terminology, symbols, packaging or labeling requirements applicable to a good, service, process or related production method.
service: any of the services included in the framework of this Agreement, except financial services.
Article 14-02 : Scope of application.
The provisions of this chapter apply to standardization measures, metrology and related measures of each Party that may affect, directly or indirectly, trade in goods and services between them. The provisions of this chapter do not apply to phytosanitary and zoosanitary measures referred to in chapter V, section B.
Article 14-03 : Scope of obligations.
Each Party shall ensure, in accordance with its constitutional provisions, compliance with the obligations of this chapter, in its territory at the central or federal, state or departmental and municipal level and shall adopt the measures in this regard that are within its reach with respect to the agencies non-governmental standardization organizations in their territory.
Article 14-04 : Reaffirmation of international rights and obligations.
The Parties mutually reaffirm their current rights and obligations related to standardization measures emanating from the GATT and all other international treaties, including environmental and conservation treaties, to which the Parties are party.
Article 14-05 : Obligations and basic rights.
The Parties shall not develop, adopt, maintain or apply any standardization measure that has the purpose or effect of creating unnecessary obstacles to trade between them. To this end, each Party shall ensure that its standardization measures do not restrict trade more than is required to achieve a legitimate objective, taking into account the risks that failure to do so would create.
Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter, and in accordance with article 14-14, paragraph 3, each Party may establish the level of protection that it deems appropriate in the pursuit of its legitimate objectives in terms of safety and protection of life and human, animal and plant health; and protection of their environment and prevention of practices that may mislead consumers, without constituting an obstacle to trade. To this end, each Party may develop, apply and maintain the standardization measures that guarantee that level of protection, as well as the measures that guarantee the application and compliance with those standardization measures, including the relevant approval procedures,
With regard to its normalization measures, each Party shall grant to the goods and service providers of another Party national treatment no less favorable than that granted to similar goods and service providers of any other country.
Article 14-06 : Use of international standards.
Each Party shall use as a basis for its own standardization measures, current or imminently adopted international standards, except when those standards do not constitute an effective or adequate means to achieve its legitimate objectives; for example, due to fundamental factors of a climatic, geographical, technological or infrastructure nature, in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
Standardization measures of a Party that conform to an international standard shall be presumed to be consistent with the provisions of Article 14-05, paragraphs 1 and 3.
In the pursuit of its legitimate objectives, each Party may adopt, maintain or apply any standardization measure that achieves a higher level of protection than would have been obtained if the measure were based on an international standard due to fundamental factors of a climatic, geographical , technological or infrastructure, among others.
Article 14-07 : Compatibility and equivalence.
Recognizing the central role that standardization measures play in promoting and protecting legitimate objectives, the Parties shall work together, in accordance with this Chapter, to strengthen the level of security and protection of human life and health, animal and vegetable; of their environment and for the prevention of practices that may mislead consumers.
The Parties will make their respective technical regulations and conformity assessment procedures compatible, to the greatest extent possible, without reducing the level of safety or protection of human, animal and plant life and health; their environment or consumers, without prejudice to the rights conferred by this chapter on any Party and taking into account international standardization activities.
At the request of a Party, the other Parties shall adopt reasonable measures within their power to promote the compatibility of the specific standardization measures that exist in their territory, with the standardization measures that exist in the territory of the other Parties, taking into account the international standardization activities.
Each Party shall accept a technical regulation adopted by another Party as equivalent to its own, when, in cooperation with the importing Party, the exporting Party proves to the satisfaction of the exporting Party that its technical regulation adequately meets the legitimate objectives of the importing Party, and if appropriate will review it.
At the request of the exporting Party, the importing Party shall communicate to it the reasons for non-acceptance of a technical regulation in accordance with paragraph 4.
Each Party, whenever possible, shall accept the results of conformity assessment procedures carried out in the territory of another Party, even when those procedures differ from its own, provided that those procedures offer a satisfactory guarantee, equivalent to the one offered by the procedures that the Party carries out or that are carried out in its territory, the result of which it accepts, that the relevant good or service complies with the applicable technical regulations or with the standards that are developed or maintained in the territory of that Party, and if applicable, review the relevant standardization measure.
Prior to acceptance of the results of a conformity assessment procedure, in accordance with paragraph 6, and in order to build confidence in the continuing integrity of each Party's conformity assessment results , the Parties may consult on matters such as the technical capacity of conformity assessment bodies, taking into account verified compliance with relevant international standards and recommendations.
Article 14-08 : Conformity assessment.
The Parties recognize the convenience of achieving reciprocal recognition of their conformity assessment systems, including accreditation bodies, in order to facilitate the trade of goods and services between them and undertake to work towards the achievement of this objective.
In addition to what is established in paragraph 1, and recognizing the existence of differences in their conformity assessment procedures in their respective territories, the Parties shall make their respective conformity assessment systems and procedures compatible to the greatest extent possible. effect that they are mutually recognizable in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
For mutual and reciprocal benefit, each Party shall accredit, approve, license or recognize conformity assessment bodies in the territory of another Party on terms no less favorable than those granted to those bodies in its territory.
Each Party shall give favorable consideration to requests submitted by another Party to negotiate agreements on the mutual recognition of the results of that Party's conformity assessment procedures.
When it is required to carry out a procedure for the evaluation of conformity with technical regulations or standards, each Party shall have the obligation to:
a) not adopt, maintain or apply conformity assessment procedures that are stricter than necessary to be certain that the good or service complies with the applicable technical regulation or standard, taking into account the risks that non-conformity could create ;
b) initiate and complete that procedure in the most expeditious manner possible;
c) establish a non-discriminatory order for processing applications;
d) publish the normal duration of each of these procedures or inform, at the request of whoever requests it, the approximate duration of the procedure;
e) ensure that the competent body:
i) upon receipt of the application, promptly examine the documentation for completeness and inform the applicant of any deficiencies accurately and completely;
(ii) as soon as possible, convey to the applicant the results of the conformity assessment procedure in an accurate and complete manner, so that the applicant can take any corrective action;
iii) when the request is deficient, advance the procedure as much as possible, if the requester requests it; and
iv) report at the applicant's request the status of their application and the reasons for any delay;
f) limit to what is necessary, the information that the applicant must present to assess conformity and to determine the pertinent rights;
g) grant confidential information derived from the procedure or presented in connection with it:
i) the same treatment as confidential information regarding a good or service of the Party conducting the evaluation; Y
ii) in any case, treatment that protects the legitimate commercial interests of the applicant;
h) ensure that any fee charged for conformity assessment of a good or service that is imported from another Party is equitable in relation to any fee charged for conformity assessment of an identical or similar good or service from the other Party. Party that performs the evaluation taking into consideration the costs of communication, transportation and other related costs;
i) ensure that the location of the facilities where the conformity assessment procedures are carried out does not cause unnecessary inconvenience to the applicant or his representative;
j) where possible, endeavor to ensure that the procedure is carried out at that facility and, where appropriate, a mark of conformity is awarded;
k) in the case of a good or service that has been modified as a result of a determination of the assessment of conformity with the applicable technical regulations or standards, limit the procedure to what is necessary to determine that said good or service continues to comply with those regulations or standards; Y
l) limit to reasonableness any requirement relating to samples of a good and ensure that the selection of samples does not cause unnecessary inconvenience to the applicant or his representative.
The Parties shall apply the provisions of paragraph 5 to their approval procedures with appropriate adjustments.
CHAPTER XIV: Technical Standards
Article 14-09 : Publication and provision of information.
Each Party shall inform the other Parties of the normalization measures that it intends to adopt in accordance with the provisions of this chapter before the entry into force of those measures and not after their nationals.
When proposing the adoption or modification of any standardization measure, each Party:
a) publish a notice and inform the other Parties of its intention to adopt or modify that measure, to allow interested parties to become familiar with the proposal, at least 60 days in advance of its adoption or modification;
b) will identify in the notice and the information the good or service to which the measure will be applied, and will include a brief description of its objective and motivation;
c) provide a copy of the proposed measure to any Party or interested party that requests it and, where possible, identify provisions that deviate substantially from relevant international standards;
d) without discrimination, allow the other Parties and interested parties to make comments and, upon request, discuss and take into account those comments, as well as the results of the discussions; Y
e) ensure that, when adopting the measure, it is published expeditiously, or in some other way is made available to interested parties in the Party so that they become familiar with it.
With regard to any technical regulation of a state or departmental government, or municipal, each Party:
a) ensure that the intention of that government to adopt or modify that regulation at an appropriate early stage is published in a notice and informed to the other Parties;
b) will ensure that the notice and information identifies the good or service to which the technical regulation will apply, and will include a brief description of its objective and motivation;
c) ensure that a copy of the proposed regulation is delivered to the Parties or to any interested person who requests it;
d) take reasonable steps within its power to ensure that upon adoption of the technical regulation, it is promptly published or otherwise made available to interested parties in the Party for familiarization.
Each Party shall inform the other Parties about its standardization plans and programs.
When a Party considers it necessary to address an urgent problem related to the safety or protection of human, animal and plant life and health; of its environment or practices that mislead consumers, may omit any of the steps established in paragraph 2, literals a) and b), provided that when adopting the standardization measure:
a) immediately inform the other Parties, in accordance with the requirements established in paragraph 2, letter b), including a brief description of the urgent problem;
b) deliver a copy of the measure to any Party or interested party that requests it;
c) without discrimination, allow the other Parties and interested parties to make comments in writing and, upon request, discuss and take into account those comments, as well as the results of the discussions; Y
d) ensure that the measure is published expeditiously, or else allow interested parties to become familiar with it.
The Parties shall allow a reasonable period of time between the publication of their standardization measures and the date on which they enter into force, in order to give stakeholders the opportunity to adapt to the measures, except when necessary to address one of the urgent problems. indicated in paragraph 5.
Each Party shall designate a government authority as responsible for the application of the information provisions of this chapter at the federal or central level, and shall inform the other Parties thereof. When a Party designates two or more government authorities for this purpose, it shall inform the other Parties, without ambiguity or exceptions, of the scope of responsibilities of those authorities.
Article 14-10 : Information centers.
Each Party shall ensure that there is at least one information center within its territory capable of answering all questions and reasonable requests from another Party and interested parties, as well as providing the relevant documentation regarding:
a) any standardization measure adopted or proposed in its territory at the level of its federal or central, state or departmental, or municipal government;
b) the participation and membership of the Party, and of its relevant authorities at the federal or central, state or departmental or municipal level in standardization bodies and conformity assessment systems, international or regional, in bilateral or multilateral agreements, within the scope of this chapter, as well as the provisions of those systems and agreements;
c) the location of notices published pursuant to this chapter, or the place where such information may be obtained;
d) the location of information centers; Y
e) the Party's risk assessment processes, the factors it takes into account when carrying out the assessment and for establishing the levels of protection it deems appropriate, in accordance with Article 14-05, paragraph 2.
When a Party designates more than one information center:
a) inform the other Parties of the scope of responsibilities of each of these centers; Y
b) ensure that any request sent to the wrong information center is forwarded, expeditiously, to the correct information center.
Each Party shall take the measures that are reasonable and within its reach to ensure that there is at least one information center, within its territory, capable of answering all the questions and requests of the other Party and of the interested parties, as well as of provide relevant documentation, or information from where such documentation can be obtained related to:
a) any standard or conformity assessment process adopted or proposed by non-governmental standardization bodies in its territory; Y
b) the participation and membership, in international and regional standardization organizations and conformity assessment systems, of the relevant non-governmental organizations in their territory.
Each Party shall ensure that when another Party or interested parties, in accordance with the provisions of this chapter, request copies of the documents referred to in paragraph 1, they are provided at the same price that applies to their nationals, except the actual cost. shipping. Copies of technical regulations and mandatory conformity assessment processes requested by the Parties will be provided free of charge.
Article 14-11 : Limitations on the provision of information.
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to oblige a Party to provide any information the disclosure of which they consider contrary to their essential security interests, or detrimental to the legitimate business interests of certain companies.
Article 14-12 : Metrological standards.
The Parties will make their national metrological standards compatible, to the greatest extent possible, based on current international standards, when they constitute unnecessary obstacles to trade or create them.
Article 14-13 : Protection of health.
Medicines, medical equipment, medical instruments, pharmaceutical chemicals and other inputs for human, animal and plant health that are subject to sanitary registration within the territory of any of the Parties, will be, where appropriate, registered, recognized or evaluated by the competent authority of that Party based on a single national system of a federal or central nature of mandatory compliance.
The certificates that support compliance with the standards and technical regulations of the companies that produce or package the products referred to in paragraph 1, will be accepted only if they have been issued by the competent regulatory authorities of the federal or central government of the Parties.
The Parties will establish a mutual technical cooperation system that will work based on the following program:
a) identification of specific needs:
i) application of good manufacturing practices in the preparation and approval of medicines, particularly those for human use;
ii) application of good laboratory practices in the analysis and evaluation systems established in the ISO 9000 and 25 guides in force;
iii) development of common identification and nomenclature systems for auxiliary health products and medical instruments;
b) homologation of requirements related to labeling and strengthening of standardization and surveillance systems in relation to warning labeling;
c) training and training programs, and the organization of a common training, continuing education, training and evaluation system for sanitary officials and inspectors;
d) development of a mutual accreditation system for verification units and testing laboratories;
e) updating of regulatory legal frameworks; Y
f) strengthening of formal communication systems to monitor and regulate the exchange of products related to human, animal and plant health.
In order to carry out the activities proposed in paragraph 3, the Parties shall establish pursuant to Article 14-17, paragraph 5, a technical subcommittee in charge of monitoring and organizing such activities, to guide and recommend to the Parties when they so do. request it.
Article 14-14 : Risk assessment.
Pursuant to Article 14-05, paragraph 2, the Parties may carry out risk assessments. In doing so they will ensure that they take into account risk assessment methods developed by international organizations and that their standardization measures are based on an assessment of risk to human, animal and plant health and safety and their environment.
When conducting a risk assessment, the Party conducting it shall take into consideration all relevant scientific evidence, available technical information, intended end use, production, operation, inspection, quality, sampling or testing processes or methods, or environmental conditions.
When a Party, in accordance with Article 14-05, paragraph 2, once it has established its level of security protection that it deems appropriate, carries out a risk assessment, it shall avoid arbitrary or unjustifiable distinctions between similar goods and services at the level of protection it deems appropriate, if those distinctions:
a) have the effect of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination against goods or service providers of the other Parties;
b) constitute a disguised restriction on trade between the Parties; either
c) discriminate between similar goods or services for the same use, in accordance with the same conditions that pose the same level of risk and that grant similar benefits.
When the Party that carries out a risk assessment concludes that the scientific evidence or other information available is insufficient to complete that assessment, it may provisionally adopt a technical regulation based on the pertinent information available. Once sufficient information has been submitted to the Party to complete the risk assessment, the Party shall complete its assessment as soon as possible and review, and where appropriate, reconsider the provisional technical regulation in light of that assessment.
Article 14-15 : Handling of dangerous substances.
For the control, handling and acceptance of toxic or dangerous substances or residues, each Party shall apply the provisions, guides or recommendations of the pertinent international agreements to which they are party.
Article 14-16 : Labeling.
The labeling requirements of the goods and services that are part of the scope of this chapter shall be subject to the provisions established therein.
Each Party will apply its pertinent labeling requirements within its territory and in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
The Parties will seek to develop common labeling requirements. The proposals made by each Party will be evaluated by the Committee referred to in article 14-17.
The Committee referred to in article 14-17, may work and formulate recommendations, among others, on the following areas of labeling, packaging and packaging:
a) a common system of symbols and pictograms;
b) definitions and terminology; either
c) presentation of information.
Article 14-17 : Committee for standardization measures.
The Parties create a Committee for Standardization Measures.
The Committee is responsible for, among other functions:
a) the monitoring of the application, compliance and administration of this chapter, including the progress of the sub-committees and working groups established in accordance with paragraph 4 and the operation of the information centers established in accordance with article 14-10 paragraph one;
b) facilitate the process through which the Parties will make their standardization and metrology measures compatible;
c) provide a forum for Parties to consult on issues related to standardization and metrology measures;
d) report annually to the Commission on the application of this chapter; Y
e) develop the necessary procedural mechanisms to achieve recognition from conformity assessment bodies.
The committee:
a) It will be made up of an equal number of representatives of each Party. Each Party shall establish its procedures for the selection of its representatives;
b) meet at least once a year, as well as when requested by either Party, unless the Parties agree otherwise;
c) establish its regulations; Y
d) will make its decisions by consensus.
When the Committee considers it appropriate, it may establish the subcommittees and working groups that it deems pertinent and determine their scope of action and mandate. Each subcommittee and working group will be made up of representatives of each Party and may:
a) when deemed necessary, call to participate in its meetings or consult:
i) representatives of non-governmental organizations, such as standardization bodies, or private sector chambers and associations;
ii) scientists; either
iii) technical experts; Y
b) determine its work program, taking into account relevant international activities.
In addition to paragraph 4, the Committee shall establish:
a) the Subcommittee on Health Standardization Measures; Y
b) any other subcommittees and working groups it deems appropriate to discuss, among others, the following issues:
i) the identification and nomenclature of the goods and services subject to standardization measures;
ii) technical regulations and quality and identity standards;
iii) packaging, labeling and presentation of information for consumers, including measurement systems, ingredients, sizes, terminology, symbols and other related matters;
iv) programs for product approval and post-sale surveillance;
v) principles for the accreditation and recognition of test facilities, inspection bodies and conformity assessment bodies;
vi) development and implementation of a uniform system for the classification and reporting of hazardous chemicals and chemical hazard communication;
vii) programs to ensure compliance with current provisions, including training and inspection by personnel responsible for regulation, analysis, and compliance verification;
viii) promotion and application of good laboratory practices;
ix) the promotion and application of good manufacturing practices;
x) criteria for the evaluation of potential damage to the environment due to the use of goods or services;
xi) analysis of the procedures to simplify the requirements for the importation of goods and for the provision of specific services;
xii) guidelines for testing chemical substances, including those of an industrial type and those for agricultural, pharmaceutical and biological use; Y
xiii) means that facilitate the protection of consumers, including what refers to their compensation.
Article 14-18 : Technical consultations.
When a Party has doubts about the interpretation or application of this Chapter with respect to the standardization measures, metrology or measures related to these of another Party, the Party may alternatively turn to the Committee or to the dispute settlement mechanism of the Agreement. The Parties involved may not use both channels simultaneously.
When a Party decides to go to the Committee, it will notify it so that it can consider the matter or refer it to a subcommittee or working group, or to another competent forum, in order to obtain non-binding technical advice or recommendations from them.
The Committee will consider any matter that is referred to it, in accordance with paragraphs 1 and 2, as expeditiously as possible and, in the same way, will inform the Parties of any advice or technical recommendation that it prepares or receives in relation to that matter. Once the Parties involved receive from the Committee a technical advice or recommendation that they have requested, they will send to the Committee a written response in relation to that technical advice or recommendation, within the period determined by the Committee.
Pursuant to paragraphs 2 and 3, in the event that the technical recommendation issued by the Committee does not resolve the existing difference between the Parties involved, they may invoke the dispute settlement mechanism of the Treaty. If the Parties involved so agree, the consultations carried out before the Committee shall constitute consultations for the purposes of Article 19-05.
A Party that asserts that a standardization measure of another Party is inconsistent with the provisions of this Chapter shall have to demonstrate that inconsistency.
CHAPTER XV : Public Sector Purchases
Section A - Scope of application and national treatment
Article 15-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
construction services contract: a contract for the performance by any means of civil works or construction indicated in the appendix to annex 5 of article 15-02.
entity: an entity included in annexes 1 and 2 to article 15-02 and in the Protocol that the Parties prepare in accordance with article 15-26 for state or departmental government entities.
technical specification: a specification that establishes the characteristics of the goods or processes and related production methods, or the characteristics of services or their related methods of operation, including the applicable administrative provisions. It may also include or deal exclusively with terminology, symbols, packaging, marking or labeling requirements applicable to a good, process, or method of production or operation.
tendering procedures: open tendering procedures, selective tendering procedures or restricted tendering procedures.
open tender procedures: procedures in which all interested suppliers can submit offers.
restricted bidding procedures: procedures by which an entity communicates individually with suppliers, only in the circumstances and in accordance with the conditions described in article 15-16.
selective bidding procedures: procedures in which, under the terms of article 15-12, the suppliers whom the entity invites to do so may submit bids.
Supplier: A person who has provided or may provide goods or services in response to an entity's invitation to bid.
locally established supplier: among others, a natural person residing in the territory of the Party, a company organized or established under the laws of the Party, and a branch or representative office located in the territory of the Party.
services: among others, construction service contracts, unless otherwise specified.
Article 15-02 : Scope of application and coverage of obligations.
This Chapter applies to measures that a Party adopts or maintains in relation to purchases:
a) of a central or federal government entity indicated in annex 1 to this article; a government company indicated in annex 2 to this article; or a state or departmental government entity in accordance with what the Parties establish in the Protocol referred to in article 15-26;
b) goods, in accordance with annex 3 to this article, services, in accordance with annex 4 to this article or construction services, in accordance with annex 5 to this article; Y
c) when it is estimated that the value of the contract to be awarded equals or exceeds the value of the following thresholds, calculated and adjusted in accordance with the inflation rate of the United States of America as provided in annex 6 to this article: in the case of:
i) central or federal government entities, USD 50,000 for contracts for goods, services or any combination thereof, and USD 6.5 million for construction service contracts;
ii) government companies, US$250,000 for contracts for goods, services or any combination thereof, and US$8 million for construction service contracts; Y
iii) state and departmental government entities, the value of the applicable thresholds, in accordance with what the Parties establish in the Protocol referred to in article 15-26.
Paragraph 1 will be subject to the reservations and general notes indicated in annexes 7 and 8 to this article, respectively.
Subject to paragraph 4, where a contract to be awarded by an entity is not subject to this chapter, its provisions may not be construed to cover the components of any good or service of that contract.
None of the entities of the Parties shall conceive, prepare or structure a purchase contract in such a way as to avoid the obligations of this chapter.
Purchases include acquisitions by methods such as purchase, lease, or rental, with or without a purchase option. Purchases do not include:
a) non-contractual agreements or any form of government assistance, including cooperation agreements, transfers, loans, capital transfers, guarantees, fiscal incentives and government supply of goods and services granted to individuals or to state, departmental and regional governments; Y
b) the acquisition of services from fiscal agencies or deposits, liquidation and administration services for regulated financial institutions, or public debt sale and distribution services.
Article 15-03 : Valuation of contracts.
Each Party shall ensure that, in determining whether a contract is covered by this Chapter, its entities apply the provisions of paragraphs 2 through 7 to calculate the value of that contract.
The value of the contract will be estimated at the time of publication of the call in accordance with article 15-11.
When calculating the value of a contract, entities will take into account all forms of remuneration, including bonuses, rights, commissions and interest.
In addition to the provisions of article 15-02, paragraph 4, an entity may not choose a valuation method or divide the purchase requirements into independent contracts, in order to evade the obligations contained in this chapter.
When an individual requirement results in the award of more than one contract or the contracts are awarded in separate parts, the basis for valuation will be:
a) the actual value of similar successive or recurring contracts entered into during the preceding fiscal year or in the preceding twelve months, adjusted where possible for expected changes in quantity and value in the following twelve months; either
b) the estimated value of successive or recurring contracts to be entered into during that fiscal year or in the twelve months following the initial contract.
In the case of lease or rental contracts, with or without a purchase option, or contracts in which a total price is not specified, the basis for valuation will be:
a) In the case of contracts signed for a specific period, if this is twelve months or less, the calculation will be made on the basis of the total value of the contract during its period of validity or, if it is greater than twelve months, on the full value basis including estimated residual value; either
b) in the case of contracts for an indefinite term, the base will be the estimated monthly payment multiplied by 48.
If the entity is not certain whether a contract is for fixed or indefinite terms, it will calculate the value of the contract using the method indicated in subparagraph b).
When the bidding conditions require optional clauses, the basis for valuation will be the total value of the maximum purchase allowed, including all possible optional purchases.
Article 15-04 : National treatment and non-discrimination, and most favored nation treatment.
With respect to the measures included in this Chapter, each Party shall grant to the goods of another Party, to the suppliers of those goods and to the service providers of another Party, treatment no less favorable than the most favorable granted:
a) to its own goods, and suppliers; Y
b) to the goods and suppliers of another Party.
With respect to the measures included in this chapter, neither Party may:
a) give a supplier established in its territory less favorable treatment than that accorded to another supplier established in that territory, by reason of the degree of foreign affiliation or ownership; either
b) discriminate against a supplier established in its territory on the grounds that the goods or services offered by that supplier for a particular purchase are goods or services of another Party.
Paragraph 1 does not apply to measures relating to import taxes or other charges of any kind on or in connection with importation, the method of collection of such taxes and charges, or other import regulations, including restrictions and formalities.
Article 15-05 : Rules of origin.
For the purposes of public sector purchases covered by this chapter, no Party shall apply rules of origin to goods imported from any other Party other than the rules of origin established in Chapter VI, or incompatible with them.
Article 15-06 : Denial of benefits.
A Party may deny the benefits derived from this chapter to a service provider of another Party, after prior communication and consultation, when the Party determines that the service is being provided by a company that does not carry out important business activities in the territory of any Party and is owned or controlled by persons of a country that is not a Party.
Article 15-07 : Prohibition of special compensatory conditions.
Each Party shall ensure that its entities do not take into account, request or impose special compensatory conditions in the qualification and selection of suppliers, goods or services, in the evaluation of offers or in the award of contracts. For the purposes of this article, special compensatory conditions are the conditions that an entity imposes or takes into account before or during the purchase procedure to promote local development or improve balance of payments accounts, through local content requirements. , licensing of technology, investment, countertrade or similar requirements.
The Parties will exchange information on the results of the application of programs aimed at supporting the local industry, or of the performance of any type of committee for the same purposes, such as advisory commissions.
Each Party may resort to the Dispute Resolution mechanism of Chapter XIX if, as a result of the application of the programs or the actions of the committees referred to in paragraph 2, their suppliers are discriminated against.
Article 15-08 : Technical specifications.
Each Party shall ensure that its entities do not prepare, adopt or apply any technical specification that has the purpose or effect of creating unnecessary obstacles to trade.
Each Party shall ensure that, where applicable, any technical specifications established by its entities:
a) is defined in terms of performance criteria rather than design or descriptive features; Y
b) is based on international standards, national technical regulations, recognized national standards, or building codes.
Each Party shall ensure that the technical specifications established by its entities do not require or refer to a specific brand or trade name, patent, design or type, specific origin or producer or supplier, unless there is no other sufficiently precise or understandable way of describing the purchase requirements and provided that, in such cases, words such as "or equivalent" are included in the bidding conditions.
Each Party shall ensure that its entities do not solicit or accept, in a manner that has the effect of preventing competition, advice that could be used in preparing or adopting any technical specification in respect of a particular purchase, from a person who may have an interest. merchant on that purchase.
Section B - Tender Procedures
Article 15-09 : Tender procedures.
The bidding procedures will be applied in accordance with the provisions of the annex to this article, for the parties indicated therein.
Each Party shall ensure that the bidding procedures of its entities:
a) are applied in a non-discriminatory manner; Y
b) are consistent with this article and with articles 15-10 to 15-16.
Each Party shall ensure that its entities:
a) do not provide any supplier with information about a specific purchase in such a way that it has the effect of preventing competition; Y
b) provide all suppliers with equal access to information regarding a purchase during the period prior to the issuance of any call or bidding conditions.
Article 15-10 : Qualification of suppliers.
Pursuant to Article 15-04, in the qualification of suppliers during the bidding procedure, no entity of a Party may discriminate between suppliers of the other Parties or between national suppliers and suppliers of the other Parties.
An entity's rating procedures will be consistent with the following:
a) the conditions for the participation of suppliers in the bidding procedures will be published sufficiently in advance, so that suppliers have adequate time to start and, to the extent that it is compatible with the efficient operation of the contracting process, complete qualification procedures;
b) the conditions for participating in the bidding procedures, including financial guarantees, technical qualifications and the information necessary to prove the financial, commercial and technical capacity of the suppliers, as well as the verification that the supplier satisfies those conditions, shall be they will be limited to those essential to ensure compliance with the contract in question;
c) the financial, commercial and technical capacity of a supplier shall be determined on the basis of its global activity, including both its activity carried out in the territory of the Party of the supplier, and its activity in the territory of the Party of the purchasing entity, if the have;
d) an entity may not use the supplier qualification process, including the time it requires, in order to exclude suppliers of another Party from a list of suppliers or not consider them for a specific purchase;
e) an entity shall recognize as qualified suppliers those suppliers of another Party that meet the conditions required to participate in a specific purchase; f) an entity shall consider for a given purchase those suppliers of another Party that request to participate in the purchase and that have not yet been qualified, provided that sufficient time is available to complete the qualification procedure;
g) an entity that maintains a permanent list of qualified suppliers shall ensure that suppliers can request their qualification at any time, that all qualified suppliers who request it are included in the list within a reasonably short period of time and that all suppliers included in the list are notified of the cancellation of the list or their removal from it;
h) when, after the publication of the call in accordance with article 15-11, a supplier that has not yet been qualified requests to participate in a given purchase, the entity shall promptly initiate the qualification procedure;
i) an entity will notify any supplier that has requested its qualification, the decision on whether it has been qualified; Y
j) when an entity rejects a qualification request, or ceases to recognize the qualification of a supplier, at the request of the supplier, the entity shall promptly provide pertinent information on the reasons for its action.
Each part:
a) ensure that each of its entities uses a single rating procedure; when the entity establishes a need to resort to a different procedure and, at the request of another Party, is prepared to demonstrate that need, it may use additional qualification procedures; Y
b) will try to minimize the differences between the rating procedures of its entities.
Nothing in paragraphs 2 and 3 shall prevent an entity from excluding a provider for reasons such as bankruptcy, or misrepresentation.
Article 15-11 : Invitation to participate.
Except as provided in section 15-16, an entity shall publish an invitation to participate for all purchases, in accordance with paragraphs 2, 3 and 5, in the corresponding publication indicated in the annex to this section.
The invitation to participate will take the form of a call, which will contain the following information:
a) a description of the nature and quantity of the goods or services to be purchased, including any future purchase options and, if possible:
i) an estimate of when such options may be exercised; Y
ii) in the case of recurring contracts, an estimate of when subsequent calls may be issued;
b) an indication of whether the tender is open or selective;
c) any date to begin or conclude the delivery of the goods or services to be purchased;
d) the address to which the request must be sent to be invited to tender or to qualify on the list of suppliers and the deadline for receipt of the request;
e) the address to which the offers will be sent and the deadline for their receipt;
f) the address of the entity that will award the contract and that will provide any information necessary to obtain specifications and other documents;
g) a statement of any conditions of an economic or technical nature, and of any financial guarantees, information and documents required from suppliers;
h) the amount and method of payment of any amount to be paid for the bidding conditions; and
i) The indication of whether the entity calls for the presentation of offers for the purchase, lease or rental, with or without a purchase option.
Notwithstanding paragraph 2, an entity indicated in Annex 2 to Article 15-02 or in the Protocol that the Parties prepare in accordance with Article 15-26 for state or departmental government entities, may use as an invitation to participate a scheduled purchase call, which will contain the information in paragraph 2 to the extent that it is available to the entity, but which will include, at a minimum, the following information:
a) a description of the object of the purchase;
b) the deadlines set for the receipt of offers or requests to be invited to bid;
c) the address from which documentation related to the purchase may be requested;
d) an indication that the interested suppliers will express to the entity their interest in the purchase; Y
e) the identification of an information center in the entity where additional information can be obtained.
An entity that uses a scheduled purchase solicitation as an invitation to participate will subsequently invite suppliers that have expressed interest in purchasing to confirm their interest, based on information provided by the entity that will include, at least, the information provided in paragraph 2.
Notwithstanding paragraph 2, an entity indicated in Annex 2 to Article 15-02 or in the Protocol that the Parties prepare in accordance with Article 15-26 for state or departmental government entities, may use as an invitation to participate a call regarding the qualification system. An entity that uses this call will offer in a timely manner, in accordance with the considerations referred to in article 15-15, paragraph 8, information that allows all suppliers that have expressed interest in participating in the purchase, to have a real possibility to assess your interest. The information will normally include the data required for the call referred to in paragraph 2.
In the case of selective bidding procedures, an entity that maintains a permanent list of qualified suppliers will insert annually, in the appropriate publication referred to in the annex to this article, a notice containing the following information:
a) an enumeration of all current lists, including their headings, in relation to the goods or services, or categories of goods or services whose purchase is made through the lists;
b) the conditions that suppliers must meet to be included in the lists and the methods according to which the entity in question will verify each of those conditions; Y
c) the period of validity of the lists and the formalities for their renewal.
When, after the publication of an invitation to participate, but before the expiration of the period set for the opening or receipt of offers, as stated in the calls or in the bidding conditions, the entity considers it necessary to make modifications or reissue the the call or the bidding conditions, the entity will ensure that the new or modified call or the tender conditions are given the same dissemination that was given to the original documentation. Any material information provided to one supplier regarding a particular purchase will be simultaneously provided to the other interested suppliers, sufficiently in advance to allow all interested parties appropriate time to review the information and to respond.
An entity will indicate in the calls referred to in this article that the purchase is covered by this chapter.
Article 15-12 : Selective bidding procedures.
In order to guarantee optimal effective competition between the suppliers of the Parties in the selective bidding procedures, an entity shall invite, for each purchase, the largest number of national suppliers and suppliers of the other Parties that is compatible with the efficient operation of the shopping system.
Pursuant to the provisions of paragraph 3, an entity that maintains a permanent list of qualified suppliers may select among the suppliers included in the list, who will be invited to bid on a specific purchase. In the selection process, the entity will give equal opportunities to the suppliers included in the list.
In accordance with article 15-10, paragraph 2, letter f), an entity will allow a supplier that requests to participate in a certain purchase to submit an offer and will take it into account. The number of additional suppliers authorized to participate will only be limited for reasons of efficient operation of the purchasing system.
When it does not summon or admit a supplier to the tender, at the latter's request, an entity will provide it without delay with pertinent information on the reasons for its proceeding.
Section B - Tender Procedures
Article 15-13 : Deadlines for bidding and delivery.
An entity:
a) by setting a deadline, it will provide suppliers of another Party with sufficient time to prepare and submit bids before the closing of the bid;
b) in setting a deadline, in accordance with its own reasonable needs, it will take into account factors such as the complexity of the purchase, the anticipated degree of subcontracting and the time normally required to transmit offers by post both from places in the abroad as within the national territory; Y
c) when establishing the deadline for the receipt of offers or requests for admission to the tender, it will duly consider publication delays.
Subject to paragraph 3, an entity shall provide that:
a) in open bidding procedures, the term for the receipt of an offer is not less than forty days from the date of publication of a call, in accordance with article 15-11;
b) in selective bidding procedures that do not imply the use of a permanent list of qualified suppliers, the deadline for submitting a request for admission to bidding is not less than twenty-five days from the date of publication of a call , in accordance with article 15-11, and the term for the receipt of offers is not less than forty days from the date of publication of a call; Y
c) in selective bidding procedures that imply the use of a permanent list of qualified suppliers, the term for the receipt of offers is not less than forty days from the date of the first invitation to bid, but when the latter date does not coincide with the publication of a call referred to in article 15-11, no less than forty days will elapse between the two dates.
An entity may shorten the periods provided in paragraph 2 in accordance with the following:
a) According to the provisions of article 15-11, paragraph 3 or 5, when a call has been published within a period of not less than forty days and not more than twelve months, the period of forty days for the receipt of offers may be reduced to not less than twenty-four days;
b) in the case of a second publication or a subsequent publication related to recurring contracts, in accordance with article 15-11, paragraph 2, literal a) the period of forty days for the receipt of offers may be reduced to no less than twenty-four days;
c) when, for reasons of urgency duly justified by the entity, the established deadlines cannot be observed, in no case will these deadlines be less than ten days, counted from the date of publication of a call in accordance with article 15- eleven; either
d) When one of the entities indicated in Annex 2 to Article 15-02 or in the Protocol that the Parties prepare in accordance with Article 15-26 for state or departmental government entities, uses as an invitation to participate a call to the one referred to in article 15-11, paragraph 5, the entity and the selected providers may set, by mutual agreement, the deadlines; however, in the absence of an agreement, the entity may set terms sufficiently long to allow the due submission of offers, which in no case shall be less than ten days.
In establishing the delivery date of the goods or services and in accordance with its reasonable needs, an entity shall take into account factors such as the complexity of the purchase, the anticipated degree of subcontracting, and the time realistically estimated to be necessary for the delivery of goods or services. production, dispatch and transportation of the goods from the different places of supply.
Article 15-14 : Bidding conditions.
When the entities provide bidding conditions to the suppliers, the documentation will contain all the necessary information that allows them to duly present their offers, including the information that must be published in the call referred to in article 15-11, paragraph 2, except for the information required in accordance with article 15-11, paragraph 2 literal h) of that article. The documentation will also include:
a) the address of the entity to which the offers should be sent;
b) the address where requests for additional information should be sent;
c) the closing date and time for the receipt of offers and the period during which the offers will remain valid;
d) the persons authorized to attend the opening of the offers and the date, time and place of that opening;
e) a statement of any conditions of an economic or technical nature, and of any financial guarantees, information and documents required from suppliers;
f) a full description of the goods or services to be purchased and any other requirements, including technical specifications, certificates of conformity, and necessary plans, drawings and instructions;
g) the criteria on which the award of the contract will be based, including any factor, other than price, that will be considered in the evaluation of the offers and the cost elements that will be taken into account when evaluating the prices of the same, such such as transportation, insurance and inspection costs and, in the case of goods or services of the other Parties, import taxes and other import charges, taxes and currency of payment;
h) the terms of payment; and
i) any other requirement or condition.
An entity:
a) provide the bidding conditions at the request of a supplier participating in open bidding procedures or requesting to participate in selective bidding procedures, and will promptly respond to any reasonable request for clarification thereof; Y
b) respond without delay to any reasonable request for relevant information from a supplier participating in the tender, provided that such information does not give that supplier an advantage over its competitors in the contract award procedure.
Article 15-15 : Presentation, reception and opening of offers and awarding of contracts.
The entity will use procedures for the presentation, reception and opening of offers and the awarding of contracts that are consistent with the following:
a) Bids will normally be submitted in writing, either directly or by post;
b) when bids transmitted by telex, telegram, telefacsimile or other means of electronic transmission are accepted, the bid submitted shall include all the information necessary for its evaluation, in particular the final price proposed by the supplier and a statement that the supplier accepts all the clauses and conditions of the call;
c) offers submitted by telex, telegram, telefacsimile or other means of electronic transmission shall be confirmed without delay by letter or by signed copy of the telex, telegram, telefacsimile or electronic message;
d) the content of the telex, telegram, telefacsimile or electronic message will prevail in case there is a difference or contradiction between it and any other documentation received after the term for the receipt of offers has expired;
e) it will not be allowed to submit bids by telephone;
f) Applications to participate in a selective bidding may be submitted by telex, telegram, telefacsimile and, when permitted, by other means of electronic transmission; Y
g) The opportunities to correct formal errors, which are granted to suppliers during the period between the opening of the offers and the award of the contract, may not be used in such a way as to discriminate between suppliers.
For the purposes of paragraph 1, "electronic means of transmission" includes the means by which the recipient can produce a hard copy of the offer at the place of destination of the transmission.
No entity will penalize the provider whose offer is received at the office designated in the bidding conditions after the expiration of the established term, when the delay is due solely to an oversight of the entity.
All the offers requested by an entity in the public or selective bidding procedures will be received and opened in accordance with the procedures and under the conditions that guarantee the regularity of the opening of the offers. The entity will keep the information corresponding to the opening of the offers. The information will remain available to the competent authorities of the Party to be used, if required, in accordance with Articles 15-17, 15-18 or Chapter XIX.
An entity will award contracts in accordance with the following:
a) For an offer to be considered for the award, it must comply, at the time of opening, with the requirements established in the call or in the bidding conditions and come from suppliers that meet the conditions of participation. ;
b) if the entity receives an offer that is abnormally lower in price than the other offers, it may check with the supplier to ensure that the supplier satisfies the conditions for participation and is or will be able to comply with the terms of the contract;
c) unless for reasons of public interest it decides not to award the contract, the entity shall award it to the supplier that it has considered capable of performing the contract and whose offer is the lowest price or the most advantageous in accordance with the specific criteria evaluation established in the call or in the bidding conditions;
d) the awards will be made in accordance with the criteria and requirements established in the bidding conditions; Y
e) clauses relating to options shall not be used in order to circumvent this chapter.
No entity of a Party may condition the award of a contract on the fact that a supplier has previously been assigned one or more contracts by an entity of that Party, or on the supplier's previous work experience in the territory of that Party.
An entity:
a) upon express request, it will promptly inform the participating providers of the decisions on the contracts awarded and, if they so request, do so in writing; Y
b) at the express request of a supplier whose offer has not been chosen, it will provide the relevant information to that supplier about the reasons why its offer was not chosen, the characteristics and advantages of the selected offer and the name of the winning supplier.
Within a maximum period of seventy-two days from the award of the contract, an entity will communicate directly to the participating providers or insert a notice in the appropriate publication referred to in the annex to article 15-11 containing the following information:
a) a description of the nature and quantity of the goods or services that are the subject of the contract;
b) the name and address of the entity that awards the contract;
c) the award date;
d) the name and address of each selected supplier;
e) the value of the contract, or of the highest and lowest price bids considered for the award of the contract; Y
f) the bidding procedure used.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 1 through 8, an entity may refrain from disclosing certain information about the award of the contract, when its disclosure:
a) could impede compliance with the law or be contrary to the public interest;
b) would harm the legitimate business interests of a particular person; either
c) out to the detriment of fair competition between suppliers.
Article 15-16 : Restricted bidding.
An entity of a Party may, in the circumstances and in accordance with the conditions described in paragraph 2, use the restricted bidding procedures and accordingly deviate from the provisions of Articles 15-09 through 15-15, provided that restricted bidding procedures are not used to avoid the maximum possible competition or in a way that constitutes a means of discrimination between suppliers of the other Parties or of protection of national suppliers.
An entity may use restricted tendering procedures in the following circumstances and under the following conditions, as applicable:
a) in the absence of offers in response to a call for public or selective bidding or when the offers submitted have resulted from collusion or do not comply with the essential requirements of the bidding conditions, or when the offers have been made by suppliers that do not meet the conditions for participation provided in accordance with this chapter, provided that the initial purchase requirements are not substantially changed in the award of the contract;
b) when, because they are works of art, or for reasons related to the protection of patents, copyrights or other exclusive rights, or reserved information or when for technical reasons there is no competition, the goods or services can only be supplied by a determined provider without there being other reasonable alternatives or substitutes;
c) to the extent strictly necessary, when, for reasons of extreme urgency due to events that the entity cannot foresee, it would not be possible to obtain the goods or services on time through public or selective bidding;
d) in the case of additional deliveries from the initial supplier either as replacement parts or continuing services for existing materials, services or facilities, or as an extension of existing materials, services or facilities, where a change of supplier would require the entity to acquire equipment or services that do not meet the requirement to be interchangeable with existing equipment or services, including software, to the extent that the initial purchase of the software was covered by this chapter;
e) when an entity acquires prototypes or a first good or service that are manufactured at its request in the course and for the execution of a specific research, experimentation, study or original manufacturing contract. Once the contracts of this class have been fulfilled, the purchase of goods or services that are made as a result of them will be adjusted to articles 15-09 to 15-15. The original development of a first good may include its production in limited quantity in order to take into account the results of field tests and to demonstrate that the product lends itself to mass production meeting acceptable quality standards, but does not include series production to determine commercial viability or to recover research and development costs;
f) for goods purchased on a commodity market;
g) for purchases made under exceptionally favorable conditions that are only offered in the very short term, such as extraordinary sales made by companies that are not normally suppliers; or to the alienation of assets of companies in liquidation or under judicial administration, but does not include ordinary purchases made from habitual suppliers;
h) for contracts to be awarded to the winner of an architectural design competition, provided that the competition is:
i) organized in accordance with the principles of this chapter, including in relation to the publication of the invitation to qualified suppliers to bid;
ii) organized in such a way that the design contract is awarded to the winner; Y
iii) submitted to an independent jury; and
i) when an entity requires consulting services related to aspects of a confidential nature, the disclosure of which could reasonably be expected to compromise confidential information of the public sector, cause serious economic damage or, similarly, be contrary to the public interest.
Entities shall prepare a written report on each contract they have awarded under paragraph 2.
