Each report shall contain the name of the procuring entity, the value and type of goods or services procured, the country of origin, and a statement of the circumstances and conditions described in paragraph 2 that justified the use of restricted bidding. The entity will retain each report. These will remain at the disposal of the competent authorities of the Party to be used, if required, in accordance with articles 15-17, 15-18 or chapter XIX.
Section C - Challenge Procedures and Dispute Resolution.
Article 15-17 : Challenge procedures.
The challenge procedures will be applied in accordance with the provisions of the annex to this article for the Parties indicated therein.
In order to promote fair, open, and impartial procurement procedures, each Party shall adopt and maintain challenge procedures for purchases covered by this chapter, in accordance with the following:
a) each Party shall allow suppliers to resort to the challenge procedure in relation to any aspect of the purchasing process that, for the purposes of this article, begins from the moment an entity has defined its purchase requirement and continues until the award of the contract;
b) before initiating a challenge procedure, a Party may encourage the supplier to seek a solution to its complaint with the procuring entity;
c) each Party shall ensure that its entities give timely and impartial consideration to any complaint or challenge regarding purchases covered by this chapter;
d) whether or not a supplier has attempted to resolve its complaint with the entity, or after a satisfactory resolution has not been reached, no Party may preclude the supplier from initiating a challenge procedure or bringing other recourse;
e) a Party may request a supplier to notify the entity of the initiation of a challenge procedure;
f) a Party may limit the term within which a supplier may initiate the challenge procedure, but in no case shall this term be less than ten business days, from the moment the supplier knows or is considered to have known the basis of the complaint;
g) each Party shall establish or designate a reviewing authority with no substantial interest in the outcome of the purchases to receive challenges and issue the pertinent resolutions and recommendations;
h) upon receiving the challenge, the reviewing authority will proceed to investigate it expeditiously;
i) a Party may require its reviewing authority to limit its considerations to the challenge itself;
j) when investigating the challenge, the reviewing authority may delay the award of the proposed contract until the resolution of the challenge, except in cases of urgency or when the delay could be contrary to the public interest;
k) The reviewing authority will issue a recommendation to resolve the challenge, which may include guidelines for the entity to re-evaluate the offers, terminate the contract, or submit it again to the competition;
l) generally, entities will follow the recommendations of the reviewing authority;
m) at the conclusion of the challenge proceeding, each Party shall empower its review authority to submit further written recommendations to an entity, regarding any phase of its procurement process that was found to be problematic during the challenge investigation, including recommendations for make changes to the entity's purchasing procedures so that they are consistent with this chapter;
n) The reviewing authority will provide in a timely manner and in writing the results of its inquiries and its recommendations regarding the challenges, and will make them available to the Parties and interested persons;
o) each Party shall specify in writing and make generally available all of its challenge procedures; Y
p) in order to verify that the procurement process was carried out in accordance with this chapter, each Party shall ensure that each of its entities maintains complete documentation relating to each of its purchases, including a written record of all communications that substantially affect each purchase, for a period of at least three years from the date the contract was awarded.
A Party may request the start of the challenge procedure only after the call has been published or, in case of not being published, after the bidding conditions are available. When a Party establishes this requirement, the term of ten business days referred to in paragraph 2, letter f), will not begin to run before the date on which the call has been published or the bidding conditions are available.
Article 15-18 : Settlement of disputes.
When a Party considers that a measure of another Party is inconsistent with the obligations of this Chapter or could cause nullification or impairment within the meaning of the annex to Article 19-02, at the option of the complaining Party, the following shall apply:
a) the provisions of Chapter XIX; either
b) the provisions of chapter XIX with the modifications provided for in paragraphs 2 to 9.
Any consulting Party may request in writing the constitution of an arbitral tribunal whenever a matter is not resolved in accordance with article 19-05 within a period of thirty days following the request for consultations.
For the participation of the third Party as a complaining Party, instead of the period established in Article 19-07, paragraph 3, a period of five days will be observed.
For the constitution of the arbitral tribunal, instead of the terms established in article 19-09, the following will be observed:
a) the terms established in paragraph 1, literal b), will be ten days and three days respectively;
b) the term established in paragraph 1, literal c), will be five days;
c) the terms established in paragraph 2, literal b), will be 10 days and three days respectively; Y
d) The period established in paragraph 2, literal c), will be five days.
For the challenge, instead of the period established in article 19-10, a period of ten days will be observed.
For the preliminary decision, instead of the deadlines established in article 19-14, the following will be observed:
a) the period established in paragraph 1 shall be sixty days; Y
b) the period established in paragraph 2 shall be ten days.
For the final decision, instead of the deadlines established in article 19-15, the following will be observed:
a) the period established in paragraph 1 shall be twenty days; Y
b) the period established in paragraph 3 shall be ten days.
In accordance with article 19-16, paragraph 1, when ordering the term for the Parties to comply with the final decision, the arbitral tribunal shall take into account the need to establish a reduced term in the case of disputes arising from this chapter.
For the final decision, instead of the period established in article 19-17, a period of forty days will be observed.
The provisions of this article do not prevent a supplier of a Party from initiating the judicial or administrative instances that may arise under the domestic law of each Party.
Section D - General Provisions
Article 15-19 : Exceptions.
Nothing in this Chapter shall be construed to prevent a Party from taking any action or refraining from disclosing information that it considers necessary to protect its essential security interests in connection with the purchase of arms, ammunition or war materiel, or any other essential contracting for national security or for national defense purposes.
As long as these measures are not applied in such a way that they constitute a means of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination between the Parties where the same conditions exist or that they imply a disguised restriction on trade between the Parties, nothing in this Chapter shall be interpreted as meaning to prevent a Party from establishing or maintaining measures:
a) necessary to protect morality, public order or safety;
b) necessary to protect human, animal or plant life and health;
c) necessary to protect intellectual property; either
d) related to the goods or services of disabled people, charitable institutions or penitentiary work.
Article 15-20 : Provision of information
This Article shall be applied in accordance with the provisions of Annex 1 thereto, for the Parties indicated in that Annex.
Pursuant to Chapter XXI, each Party shall promptly publish any law, regulation, jurisprudence, administrative ruling of general application, and any procedure, including model contractual clauses relating to public sector procurement covered by this Chapter, by inserting it into publications pertinent to which annex 2 refers to this article.
Each part:
a) explain to another Party, upon request, its public sector procurement procedures;
b) ensure that its entities, upon request from a supplier, promptly explain their public sector procurement practices and procedures; Y
c) designate upon the entry into force of this Agreement one or more information centers for:
i) facilitate communication between the Parties; Y
ii) answer, upon request, all reasonable questions from the other Parties in order to provide relevant information on aspects covered by this chapter.
A Party may request additional information on the award of the contract that may be necessary to determine whether a purchase was made in accordance with the provisions of this chapter with respect to offers that have not been selected. For this purpose, the Party to which the purchasing entity belongs will provide information on the characteristics and relative advantages of the winning bid and the price of the contract. When disclosure of this information may prejudice competition in future tenders, the requesting Party may not disclose the information except after consulting with and obtaining the consent of the Party that provided the information.
Each Party shall provide to another Party, upon request, information available to that Party or its entities about its entities' covered purchases and about individual contracts awarded by its entities.
No Party may disclose confidential information, the disclosure of which may harm the legitimate business interests of a particular person or be detrimental to fair competition between suppliers, without the formal authorization of the person who provided such information to the Party.
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to require a Party to provide confidential information the disclosure of which would impede law enforcement or otherwise be contrary to the public interest.
In order to enable effective monitoring of purchases covered by this chapter, each Party shall collect statistics and provide the other Parties with an annual report in accordance with the following requirements, unless the Parties otherwise agree:
a) statistics on the estimated value of contracts awarded, both below and above the value of the applicable thresholds, broken down by entity;
b) statistics on the number and total value of contracts above the value of the applicable thresholds, broken down by entity, by categories of goods and services established in accordance with the classification systems developed pursuant to this chapter and by country of origin of the goods and services purchased;
c) statistics on the number and total value of contracts awarded pursuant to article 15-16, broken down by entity, by category of goods or services, and by country of origin of the goods and services purchased; Y
d) statistics on the number and total value of contracts awarded in accordance with the exceptions to this chapter established in annex 7 to article 15-02, broken down by entity.
Each Party may organize by state or department any portion of the report referred to in paragraph 7 that corresponds to the entities established in the Protocol that the Parties prepare in accordance with Article 15-26 for state or departmental government entities. .
Each Party will make available to the other Parties and to the suppliers that request it, during the first quarter of the year, its annual purchasing program. This provision shall not constitute a purchase commitment for the entities.
Article 15-21 : Technical Cooperation.
The Parties shall cooperate, on mutually agreed terms, to achieve a better understanding of their public sector procurement systems, with a view to achieving the greatest access to public sector procurement opportunities for suppliers of either Party.
Each Party shall provide to the others and to the suppliers of these Parties, on a cost-recovery basis, information concerning training and orientation programs related to its public sector procurement systems, and access, without discrimination, to any program that effect.
The training and orientation programs referred to in paragraph 2 include:
a) training of public sector personnel directly involved in public sector procurement procedures;
b) training of suppliers interested in taking advantage of public sector purchasing opportunities;
c) the explanation and description of specific aspects of the public sector procurement system of each Party, such as its challenge mechanism; Y
d) information regarding public sector procurement market opportunities.
Upon the entry into force of this Agreement, each Party shall establish at least one contact point to provide information on the training and orientation programs referred to in this article.
Article 15-22 : Joint participation programs for micro, small and medium industry.
The Parties create the Micro, Small and Medium Industry Committee, made up of representatives of each Party. The committee will meet by agreement of the Parties, but not less than once a year, and will report annually to the Commission on the efforts of the Parties to promote public sector procurement opportunities for their micro, small, and medium-sized industries.
The committee will work to facilitate the following activities of the Parties:
a) the identification of opportunities available for the training of the personnel of micro, small and medium-sized industries in matters of public sector purchasing procedures;
b) the identification of micro, small and medium-sized industries interested in becoming trading partners of micro, small and medium-sized industries in the territory of another Party;
c) the development of databases on micro, small and medium-sized industries in the territory of each Party to be used by entities of another Party that wish to make purchases from smaller-scale companies;
d) conducting consultations regarding the factors that each Party uses to establish its eligibility criteria for any program for micro, small, and medium-sized industries; Y
e) carrying out activities to deal with any related matter.
Article 15-23 : Rectifications or modifications.
A Party may modify its coverage under this chapter only in exceptional circumstances.
When a Party modifies its coverage under this chapter:
a) communicate the modification to the other Parties;
b) incorporate the change to the corresponding annex; Y
c) propose to the other Parties appropriate compensatory adjustments to their coverage, in order to maintain a level of coverage comparable to that existing before the modification.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2, a Party may make exclusively formal rectifications and minor amendments to its lists of Annexes 1 to Article 15-02, as well as to the Protocol that the Parties prepare in accordance with Article 15- 26 for state or departmental government entities, provided that such rectifications are communicated to the other Parties, and no Party expresses its objection to the proposed rectifications within a period of thirty days. In those cases, it will not be necessary to propose compensation.
It shall not be necessary to propose compensation when a Party reorganizes its entities including through programs for the decentralization of the purchases of those entities or when the corresponding public functions cease to be performed by any public sector entity, whether or not it is covered by this chapter. No Party may carry out such reorganizations or programs in order to evade compliance with the obligations of this chapter.
A Party may resort to the dispute settlement procedure under Chapter XIX when a Party considers that:
a) the adjustment proposed in accordance with paragraph 2, letter c) is not adequate to maintain a level comparable to that of the mutually agreed coverage; either
b) a minor rectification or amendment in accordance with paragraph 3 or a reorganization in accordance with paragraph 4 does not meet the requirements stipulated in those paragraphs and as a consequence requires compensation.
Article 15-24 : Alienation of entities.
Nothing in this chapter prevents a Party from disposing of an entity covered by this chapter.
If, through the public offering of shares of an entity contained in Annex 2 to Article 15-02 or through other methods, the entity is no longer subject to federal or central government control, the Party may remove that entity from its list at that time. annex and remove the entity from the coverage of this chapter, prior communication to the other Parties.
When a Party objects to the withdrawal of the entity on the grounds that it remains subject to federal or central government control, that Party may resort to the dispute settlement procedure under Chapter XIX.
Article 15-25 : Future negotiations.
The Procurement Committee will recommend to the Parties that they initiate negotiations with a view to achieving the subsequent liberalization of their respective public sector procurement markets.
In those negotiations, the Parties will review all aspects of their public sector procurement practices for the purposes of:
a) evaluate the operation of their public sector procurement systems;
b) seek to expand the coverage of the chapter; Y
c) review the value of the thresholds.
Prior to that review, the Parties shall consult with their state or departmental governments with a view to reaching commitments, on a voluntary and reciprocal basis, for the incorporation into this chapter of the purchases of state or departmental entities and companies owned by them, or under their control.
Article 15-26 : Annexed protocols.
In order to reflect the outcome of the negotiations referred to in Article 15-25, the Parties shall draw up Protocols.

Annex 3 to article 15-02 : List of goods
Section A - General Provisions
This chapter applies to all property, except as provided in paragraphs 2, 3 and 4.
In relation to Colombia, the strategic assets indicated in section B acquired by the Ministry of Defense or its affiliated entities are excluded from the coverage of this chapter, in accordance with the provisions of article 15-19.
In relation to Mexico, the strategic assets indicated in section B acquired by the Ministry of National Defense and the Ministry of the Navy are excluded from the coverage of this chapter, in accordance with the provisions of article 15-19.
In relation to Venezuela, the strategic assets indicated in section B acquired by the Ministry of Defense are excluded from the coverage of this chapter, in accordance with the provisions of article 15-19.
Section B - List of certain assets
Note: The Parties agreed that the design of the Common Classification System for Goods will be finalized before the entry into force of this Agreement. This system may follow the Federal Supply Classification (FSC).

Annex 4 article 15-02 : List of services
Section A - General Provisions
This chapter applies to all services that are purchased by the entities indicated in annexes 1 and 2 to article 15-02.
The list of services indicated in the appendix to this annex is indicative of the services purchased by the entities of the Parties. The Parties will use the list of services for reporting purposes and will update the appendix to this annex when they agree.
Annex 5 to article 15-02 applies to contracts for construction services.
General notes:
For Colombia:All services related to those goods acquired by the Ministry of Defense or its attached entities that are not identified as subject to the coverage of this chapter, (Annex 3 to article 15-02), will be excluded from the disciplines of this chapter.
All services acquired in support of military forces located outside the territory will be excluded from the coverage of this chapter.
For Mexico:
All services related to those goods acquired by the Secretary of National Defense and the Secretary of the Navy that are not identified as subject to the coverage of this chapter, (Annex 3 to article 15-02), will be excluded from the disciplines of this chapter.
All services acquired in support of military forces located outside the territory will be excluded from the coverage of this chapter.
For Venezuela:
All services related to those goods acquired by the Ministry of Defense that are not identified as subject to the coverage of this chapter, (Annex 3 to article 15-02), will be excluded from the disciplines of this chapter.
All services acquired in support of military forces located outside the territory will be excluded from the coverage of this chapter.
Appendix to annex 4 of article 15-02 : Common classification system for services
Notes:
The Parties agreed that the design of the Common Classification System for Services will be finalized before the entry into force of this Agreement.
The Parties will continue to work on developing definitions relating to the categories and other improvements to the classification system.
The Parties will continue to review pertinent technical issues that may arise from time to time.
This common classification system may follow the following format:
group = one digit
Subgroup = two digits
Class = four digits
A. Research and Development
                     
Definition of Research and Development Contracts
Purchases of research and development services include the acquisition of specialized advice in order to increase scientific knowledge; apply advanced scientific knowledge or exploit the potential of scientific discoveries and technological improvements to advance existing technological knowledge; and systematically use increases in scientific knowledge and advances in existing technology to design, develop, test, or evaluate new products or services.
Research and Development Codes
Research and development codes are made up of two alphabetic digits. The first digit is always the letter A to identify Research and Development, the second code is alphabetical, from A to Z, to identify the main subgroup.

B. Special Studies and Analysis - not Research and Development
                    
Definition of Special Studies and Analysis
Acquisitions of special studies and analysis include the acquisition of organized analytical judgments, which help understand complex issues or improve policy development or decision making. In such acquisitions, the product obtained is a structured formal document that includes data and other information that constitute the basis for conclusions or recommendations.

W. Equipment Leasing and Rental
 
        W0 Leasing or Rental of Equipment
Annex 5 to Article 15-02 : Construction services
This chapter applies to all construction services specified in the appendix to this annex, which are acquired by the entities indicated in annexes 1 and 2 of article 15-02.
The Parties may update the appendix to this annex when they so agree.
Appendix to annex 5 of article 15-02 : Common classification system
Building Services Codes
The Parties agreed that the design of the Common Classification System for Construction Services will conclude before the entry into force of this Agreement.
The Common Classification System for Construction Services may follow the following format:
Note: Based on Central Product Classification (CPC) division 51
Definition of construction services:
Pre-building work; new construction and repair, alteration, restoration, and maintenance work to residential construction, non-residential construction, or civil engineering work. This work can be carried out by general contractors who carry out the construction work in its entirety for the project owner, on their own account, or by subcontracting some part of the construction work to specialized contractors, eg. in construction installation, where the value of the work performed by the subcontractor becomes part of the main contractor's work. The products classified here are services that are essential in the production process of different types of construction, the final inputs of construction activities.
Annex 6 to article 15-02 : Indexation and conversion of the value of the thresholds
The calculations referred to in article 15-02, paragraph 1 literal c), will be made according to the following:
a) the inflation rate of the United States of America will be measured by the Wholesale Price Index for finished products published by the United States Bureau of Labor Statistics;
b) the first adjustment for inflation, which will take effect on January 1, 1997, will be calculated based on the period from January 1, 1995 to December 31, 1996;
c) all subsequent adjustments will be calculated over biennial periods, beginning on the 1st. November, and will take effect on the 1st. January of the immediately following year;
d) the inflationary adjustment will be estimated according to the following formula:
        
           T0 x (1+ TTi)= T1;
            
                where
            
         T0 : threshold value in the base period;
         TTi : cumulative rate of inflation in the United States  
                        in the i-th biennial period; Y
         T1 : new threshold value.
The exchange rate for determining the value of the thresholds, for the purposes of this chapter, will be the current value of the Colombian peso, the Mexican peso and the Venezuelan bolivar in relation to the US dollar as of the date of publication of the notice of the projected contract. The Parties will calculate and convert the value of the thresholds into their own currencies. It is understood that these calculations will be based on the official exchange rate of the Bank of Mexico, the Central Bank of Venezuela and the representative market rate disclosed by the Banking Superintendence of Colombia.

         1995 1996 1997 1998 1999
         50% 45% 45% 40% 40%  

         2000 2001 2002 2003 2004 onwards
         35% 35% 30% 30% 0%
The value of purchase contracts financed by loans from multilateral and regional financial institutions shall not be included in the calculation of the total value of purchase contracts in accordance with paragraphs 1 and 2. Purchase contracts financed by such loans shall also not be subject to to any of the provisions indicated in this chapter.
Colombia will ensure that the total value of the purchase contracts in the same Federal Supply Classification (FSC) class, or another classification system agreed between the Parties, that are reserved by the entities indicated in paragraph 1, literal a), numerals i) to viii), in accordance with paragraphs 1 and 2 for any year, does not exceed 10% of the total value of the purchase contracts that may be reserved by the entities indicated in paragraph 1, literal a), numerals i) to viii), for that year.
Colombia will ensure that, after December 31, 1998, the entities indicated in paragraph 1, literal a), numerals i) to viii), make all reasonable efforts to ensure that the total value of the purchase contracts within of the same FSC class or another classification system agreed between the Parties, which are reserved by any of the entities indicated in paragraph 1, literal a), numerals i) to viii), in accordance with paragraphs 1 and 2 for any year, does not exceed 50% of the total value of all purchase contracts of the entities indicated in paragraph 1, literal a), numerals i) to viii), within that FSC class or another classification system agreed between Parties for that year.
This chapter will not apply, until the 1st. January 2002, to purchases of medicines made by the Ministry of Health, the Social Security Institute (ISS), the Colombian Family Welfare Institute (ICBF), the Social Welfare Fund (CAJANAL) and the Ministry of Defense , which are not currently patented in Colombia or whose Colombian patents have expired. Nothing in this paragraph shall prejudge any right included in Chapter XVIII.
Permanent Reserves
This chapter does not apply to purchases made:
a) with a view to commercial resale by government stores;
b) in accordance with loans from regional or multilateral financial institutions to the extent that those institutions impose different procedures, except for local content requirements; either
c) between one entity and another in Colombia.
This chapter does not apply to the purchase of transportation services that are part of or related to a purchase contract.
National security exceptions include purchases made in support of safeguarding nuclear materials or technology.
Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter, Colombia may reserve purchase contracts for the obligations of this chapter, for an amount equivalent to 5% of its total annual purchases.

Purchase contracts financed by such loans shall also not be subject to to any of the provisions indicated in this chapter.
Venezuela will ensure that the total value of the purchase contracts in the same Federal Supply Classification (FSC) class, or another qualification system agreed between the Parties, that are reserved by Petróleos de Venezuela and its affiliated companies, CVG and its companies subsidiaries, CA Metro de Caracas and CA Energía Eléctrica de Venezuela in accordance with paragraphs 21 and 22 for any year, does not exceed 10% of the total value of the purchase contracts that Petróleos de Venezuela and its affiliated companies, CVG and its subsidiary companies, CA Metro de Caracas and CA Energía Eléctrica de Venezuela, for that year.
Venezuela will ensure that, after December 31, 1998, Petróleos de Venezuela and its affiliated companies, CVG and its affiliated companies, CA Metro de Caracas and CA Energía Eléctrica de Venezuela make all reasonable efforts to ensure that the full value of purchase contracts within the same FSC class or another qualification system agreed between the Parties, which are reserved by Petróleos de Venezuela and its affiliated companies, CVG and its affiliated companies, CA Metro de Caracas and CA Energía Eléctrica de Venezuela, in accordance with paragraphs 21 and 22 for any year, does not exceed 50 of the total value of all purchase contracts of Petróleos de Venezuela, CVG and its affiliated companies,CA Metro de Caracas and CA Energía Eléctrica de Venezuela within that class of the FSC or another qualification system agreed between the Parties, for that year.
Permanent Reserves
This chapter does not apply to purchases made:
a) with a view to commercial resale by government stores;
b) pursuant to lending from regional or multilateral financial institutions to the extent that those institutions impose different procedures except for local content requirements; either
c) between one and another entity of Venezuela.
This chapter does not apply to the purchase of transportation services that are part of a purchase contract, or are related to it.
National security exceptions include purchases made in support of safeguarding nuclear materials or technology.
Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter, Venezuela may reserve purchase contracts for the obligations of this chapter, for an amount equivalent to 5% of its total annual purchases.
This chapter does not apply to purchases made in relation to social programs (such as "Dairy Scholarship", "Food Scholarship", "Cereal Bonus", "School Supplies and Uniforms", "Daily Care Homes", "Program Maternal-Child Alimentary"), carried out by the Ministries of Education, Family and Health, are directed to the attention of education, health and food.
Annex 8 to article 15-02 : General notes
Any significant modification to the legislation, regulations, procedures and practices regarding public sector procurement of one Party shall be communicated to the other Parties sufficiently in advance of its entry into force, so that, where appropriate, those Parties adopt the measures necessary to maintain the original balance in the scope of the chapter
A modification resulting from legislative changes to the amounts from which public bidding must be made in accordance with the legislation of a Party, does not imply a modification of the coverage, unless such modification results in discriminatory treatment against providers. of the other Parties.
Without prejudice to article 15-25, and in order to promote greater opportunities for access to public sector procurement, the Parties may establish or modify the bidding procedures contained in this chapter, taking into account the disciplines of the Government Procurement Code. of the GATT.
The percentages agreed by the Parties for the calculation of their temporary reserve in accordance with the provisions of Annex 7 to Article 15-02, may be modified before the end of the year prior to its application, when necessary to guarantee compliance with the principle of relative equivalence in the application of that reservation. This principle means that the Parties will reserve each year an equivalent percentage of the value of their total purchases. The Procurement Committee will be in charge of reviewing these percentages based on the information exchanged between the Parties corresponding to public sector purchases in the immediately preceding year and will decide, when necessary, adjustments to the percentage for the following year, in accordance with the values ​​originally agreed between the Parties.
The Parties create a Purchasing Committee that will supervise the application of the provisions of this chapter. The activities of the Committee will include, among others, compliance with the principle of relative equivalence for the application of the transitory reservation agreed between the Parties. The Committee will also define a Common Asset Classification System agreed between the Parties and will evaluate the possibility of replacing the list of entities covered by this chapter with a list of entities not covered.
Annex to article 15-09 : Provisions applicable to Colombia and Venezuela regarding bidding procedures
Notwithstanding the provisions of this chapter, Colombia and Venezuela will apply their national legislation regarding purchasing procedures.
Colombia and Venezuela will grant to Mexico, regarding bidding procedures, a treatment no less favorable than the most favorable granted to any other country that is not a Party.
Colombia and Venezuela will apply the procedures of Articles 15-09 to 15-16, except for the provisions of sections A to F.
Section A - Qualification of suppliers.
Article 15-10, paragraph 2, letters e), f), h), i), j), do not apply to Colombia and Venezuela.
Section B - Invitation to participate.
Article 15-11 does not apply to Colombia and Venezuela.
When a tender procedure is used, the entity will publish an invitation to participate that will contain the following information:
a) a description of the object and characteristics of the goods and services to be acquired;
b) the address to which the request to participate in the tender should be sent; Y
c) the deadline for the receipt of offers.
When, after the publication of an invitation to participate but before the deadline for the receipt of offers, the entity considers it necessary to make changes or reissue the invitation to participate, the entity will ensure that this invitation is made under the same conditions than the original.
Section C - Selective Bidding Procedures.
Article 15-12 does not apply to Colombia and Venezuela. If, as a result of modifications to their respective internal legislation, Colombia or Venezuela decide to establish selective bidding procedures, they will be obliged to apply the disciplines of article 15-12.
Section D - Deadlines for bidding and delivery.
Article 15-13, paragraphs 2 and 3 do not apply to Colombia and Venezuela.
Section E - Bidding Terms.
Article 15-14 does not apply to Colombia and Venezuela.
When the entities provide bidding bases or specifications to the suppliers, the documentation will contain all the necessary information that allows them to duly present their offers. This information of the bidding bases will contain objective, fair and clear rules that avoid the declaration of desertion of the bidding or contest, among others:
a) the objective requirements necessary to participate;
b) the address of the entity to which the offers must be sent;
c) the closing date and time for the receipt of offers;
d) the date, time and place of the opening of the offers;
e) a description of the goods or services to be purchased and any other necessary requirements;
f) the criteria on which the award of the contract will be based; Y
g) any other requirement or condition.
Section F - Presentation, reception and opening of offers and award of contracts.
Article 15-15 does not apply to Colombia and Venezuela.
An entity shall endeavor to use procedures for the submission, receipt, and opening of bids and the award of contracts that are consistent with the following:
a) Offers will be submitted directly in writing to the entity or to the Colombian or Venezuelan consulate where the supplier is located; Y
b) It will not be allowed to submit offers by telephone, telex, telegram, telefacsimile or other means of electronic transmission.
All the offers requested by an entity in the bidding procedures will be received and opened in accordance with the procedures and conditions that guarantee the regularity of the opening of the offers. The entity will try to keep the documents related to the opening of the tenders.
An entity, when awarding contracts shall take into consideration the following:
a) In order for a bid to be considered for awarding, it must comply at the time of opening with the requirements stipulated in the invitation to participate or in the bidding bases or specifications and come from suppliers that comply with the conditions of participation; Y
b) the awards will be made in accordance with the criteria and requirements established in the bidding conditions or specifications.
Within a period of seventy-two days from the award of the contract, the entity will publish the results of the award.
Section G - Restricted Bidding.
Article 15-16 does not apply to Colombia and Venezuela.
Colombia and Venezuela will not use the restricted bidding procedures or any other supplier selection procedure, in such a way that they diminish or eliminate the benefits granted in this chapter.
Annex to article 15-11 : Publications for purchase calls in accordance with article 15-11 "Invitation to participate"

Article 15-17 does not apply to Colombia and Venezuela.
Annex 1 to article 15-20 : Provision of information.
Paragraph 4 does not apply to Colombia and Venezuela.
Colombia and Venezuela may defer the preparation of the annual report referred to in paragraphs 9 and 10, for a period of three years from the entry into force of this Agreement.
Mexico agrees to collaborate with Colombia and Venezuela in a technical cooperation program to facilitate compliance with the obligations of article 15-20.

When this publication is established, it will replace those indicated in paragraphs 1 and 2 for this purpose.

CHAPTER XVI : Policy on State companies
Article 16-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
Designation: The establishment, authorization, or expansion of the scope of a government monopoly to include an additional good or service, after the date of entry into force of this Agreement.
company: any entity constituted or organized under applicable law, whether or not for profit, including any partnership, trust, association, sole proprietorship, joint venture or other association, except for State companies.
state enterprise: an enterprise owned by, or controlled by, a Party through equity participation.
market: the geographic and commercial market for a good or service.
monopoly: an entity, including a consortium or government body, which, in any relevant market in the territory of a Party, has been designated as the sole supplier or purchaser of a good or service. It does not include an entity that has been granted an exclusive intellectual property right arising solely from that grant.
government monopoly: a monopoly owned or controlled by a Party or another government monopoly through equity participation.
according to commercial considerations: in accordance with the normal business practices carried out by the private companies that make up that industry.
non-discriminatory treatment: the best treatment between national treatment and most favored nation treatment, in the manner established in the relevant provisions of this Agreement.
Article 16-02 : Monopolies and state companies.
Each Party undertakes that its State companies grant legal or natural persons of the other Parties non-discriminatory treatment in their territory, with regard to the sale of goods and provision of services for similar commercial operations.
Each Party undertakes that its government monopolies and state companies:
a) act solely on commercial considerations in the purchase or sale of the monopolized good or service on the relevant market in the territory of that Party, including as to its price, quality, availability, saleability, transportation, and other terms and conditions for its purchase and sale; Y
b) do not use their monopoly position in their territory to carry out anti-competitive practices in a non-monopolistic market, which may adversely affect the persons of another Party.
Paragraph 2 does not apply to the acquisition of goods or services by government monopolies or state companies, for official purposes, and:
a) not for the purpose of commercial resale;
b) without the purpose of using them in the production of goods for commercial sale; either
c) without the purpose of using them in the provision of services for their commercial sale.
Regarding the sale price of a good or service, paragraph 2, literal a), applies only to the sale by government monopolies and state companies of:
a) goods or services to persons engaged in the production of industrial goods;
b) services to persons engaged in commercial resale; either
c) services to companies producing industrial goods.
The provisions of paragraph 2, literal a) shall not apply to those activities of a government monopoly that are carried out in accordance with the terms of its designation, and respect the principles enshrined in paragraphs 1 and 2, literal b).
Article 16-03 : Committees.
Within three months of the entry into force of this Agreement, the Commission shall establish the following committees:
a) a competition committee, made up of representatives of each Party, which will submit reports and recommendations to the Commission regarding the subsequent work that may proceed on relevant issues regarding the relationship between competition laws and policies; and trade in the free trade zone;
b) a committee that, in order to detect those practices of state companies that could be discriminatory or contrary to the provisions of this chapter, will prepare reports and recommendations regarding those practices.
CHAPTER XVII : Investment
Section A - Investment
Article 17-01 : Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
business : any entity incorporated, organized, or protected under applicable law, whether for profit or not, and whether privately or government owned, including partnerships, foundations, companies, branches, trusts, shares, sole proprietorships, joint ventures, or other associations;
investment : resources transferred to the national territory of a Party or reinvested in it by investors of another Party, including:
a) any type of good or right whose purpose is to produce economic benefits;
b) the participation of investors of a Party, in any proportion, in the capital stock of companies constituted or organized in accordance with the legislation of another Party;
c) companies that are owned or effectively controlled by an investor of that Party, that have been incorporated or organized in the territory of the other Party; Y
d) any other resources considered as investment under the legislation of that Party.
Investment does not include credit or debt operations, including:
a) a payment obligation of the State or a State company, nor the granting of a credit to the State or a State company;
b) pecuniary rights derived exclusively from:
i) commercial contracts for the sale of goods or services by a national or company in the territory of a Party to a company in the territory of another Party; either
ii) the granting of credit in connection with a commercial transaction, such as trade financing.
investor of a Party : any of the following persons who is the holder of an investment in the territory of another Party:
a) the Party itself or any of its public entities or state enterprises;
b) a natural person who has the nationality of that Party in accordance with its laws;
c) a company incorporated, organized or protected under the laws of that Party;
d) A branch located in the territory of that Party that carries out business activities therein;
Article 17-02 : Scope of Application.
This Chapter applies to measures adopted or maintained by a Party relating to:
a) investments of investors of another Party made in its territory;
b) investors of another Party in everything related to their investment; Y
c) with regard to Article 17-04, to all investments in the territory of the Party.
This Chapter shall not apply to measures adopted or maintained by the Parties in the area of ​​financial services, in accordance with Chapter XII, except as expressly provided in that Chapter.
This chapter applies throughout the territory of the Parties and at any level or order of government.
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to prevent a Party from adopting or maintaining measures designed to preserve its national security or public order, or to apply the provisions of its criminal laws.
Article 17-03 : National Treatment and Most Favored Nation Treatment.
Each Party shall grant to the investors of another Party, and to the investments of those investors, treatment no less favorable than that which it grants, in similar circumstances, to its own investors and investments.
Each Party shall accord to investors of another Party, and to the investments of those investors, treatment no less favorable than that which it accords, in similar circumstances, to investors and their investments of another Party or of a country that is not a Party. The most favored nation treatment shall not apply to the provisions of article 17-01.
The provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2 shall extend to any measure adopted or maintained by a Party in relation to losses due to armed conflicts, civil strife, disturbances of public order, acts of God or force majeure.
No Party shall be obliged to extend to investors or investments of another Party the advantages that it has granted or will grant to investors or investments of another Party or of a country that is not a Party, by virtue of a treaty to avoid double taxation.
Article 17-04 : Performance requirements.
No Party shall establish performance requirements through the adoption of investment measures that are mandatory or enforceable for the establishment or operation of an investment, or compliance with which is necessary to obtain or maintain an advantage or incentive, and that prescribe:
a) the purchase or use by an enterprise of products of national origin of that Party, or from national sources of that Party, whether specified in terms of particular products, in terms of volume or value of the products, or as proportion of the volume or value of its local production;
b) that the purchase or use of imported products by a company is limited to an amount related to the volume or value of the local products that the company exports;
c) restrictions on the importation by a company of products used in its local production or related to it, limiting the company's access to foreign currency to an amount related to the inflow of foreign currency attributable to that company;
d) restrictions on the export or sale for export of products by a company, whether specified in terms of particular products, in terms of volume or value of products, or as a proportion of volume or value of its local production .
The provisions contained in:
a) paragraph 1, letters a) and d), do not apply in relation to the requirements for qualification of goods with respect to export promotion programs;
b) paragraph 1, letter a), does not apply in relation to the purchase or use by a Party or by a State enterprise;
c) paragraph 1, letter a), above does not apply in relation to the requirements imposed by an importing Party related to the necessary content of the goods to qualify for preferential tariffs or quotas.
Nothing in this article shall be construed as an impediment for a Party to impose, in relation to any investment in its territory, requirements for the geographic location of productive units, job creation or labor training, or activities carried out in research and development matter.
In the event that, in the opinion of a Party, the imposition by another Party of any other requirement not provided for in paragraph 1 negatively affects the flow of trade, or constitutes a significant barrier to investment, the matter will be considered by the Commission.
If the Commission finds that the requirement in question does affect negatively the flow of trade or constitutes a significant barrier to investment, it will recommend the Party in question to suspend the respective practice.
Article 17-05 : Employment and Business Management.
The limitations regarding the number or proportion of foreigners who can work in a company or perform managerial or administrative functions as provided by the legislation of each Party, may not in any case prevent or hinder the exercise by an investor of control of his investment. .
Article 17-06 : Preparation of Reserves.
Within eight months of signing the Agreement, the Parties will prepare a Protocol that will consist of 4 lists that will contain the sectors and subsectors on which each Party can maintain measures that are not in accordance with Articles 17-03, 17-04 and 17- 05, according to the following criteria:
a) With respect to the measures contained in list 1, no Party will increase the degree of non-conformity with those articles on the date of signing this Agreement. Any amendment to any of those measures will not decrease the degree of compliance of the measure as it was in effect immediately prior to the amendment;
b) with respect to the measures contained in list 2, each Party may adopt or maintain new measures that do not conform to those articles or make those measures more restrictive;
c) List 3 will contain the economic activities reserved to the State;
d) List 4 will contain exceptions to Article 17-03, paragraph 2, in relation to international bilateral or multilateral treaties signed or to be signed by the Parties.
The Parties, in the negotiations referred to in list 2 of paragraph 1, will seek to reach agreements on the basis of reciprocity, aimed at achieving a global balance in the concessions granted.
Article 17-07 : Transfers.
Each Party shall permit all transfers related to the investment of an investor of another Party in the Party's territory to be made freely and without delay.
Those transfers include:
a) profits, dividends, interest, capital gains, royalty payments, administration expenses, technical assistance, profits in kind and other amounts derived from the investment;
b) products derived from the sale or liquidation, total or partial, of the investment;
c) payments made pursuant to a contract to which an investor or his investment is a party;
d) payments derived from compensation for expropriation concept; Y
e) Payments that come from the application of the provisions related to the dispute resolution system.
Each Party shall allow transfers to be made in freely convertible currencies and at the exchange rate prevailing in the market on the date of the transfer, for cash transactions in the currency to be transferred, without prejudice to the provisions of paragraph 6.
Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2, each Party may, to the extent and for the time necessary, prevent transfers, through the equitable, non-discriminatory application of its laws in the following cases:
a) bankruptcy, insolvency or protection of the rights of creditors;
b) issue, trade and operations of securities;
c) criminal or administrative offences; either
d) guarantee of compliance with rulings in contentious proceedings.
Likewise, each Party may, through the equitable and non-discriminatory application of its laws, request information and establish requirements regarding reports of currency transfers or other monetary instruments.
Each Party may retain laws and regulations establishing income and supplementary taxes by means such as withholding taxes applicable to dividends and other transfers, provided they are not discriminatory.
Notwithstanding the provisions of this article, each Party shall have the right, in circumstances of exceptional or serious balance of payments difficulties, to limit transfers temporarily and in an equitable and non-discriminatory manner, in accordance with internationally accepted criteria.
Article 17-08 : Expropriation and Compensation.
No Party, except as provided in the annex to this article, shall expropriate or nationalize, directly or indirectly, an investment of an investor of another Party in its territory, nor take any measure equivalent to the expropriation or nationalization of that investment (expropriation). , unless it is:
a) for reasons of public utility;
b) on non-discriminatory grounds;
c) in accordance with the principle of legality; Y
d) by compensation in accordance with paragraphs 2 to 4.
The compensation will be equivalent to the fair market value of the investment at the time of expropriation, and will not reflect any change in value due to the fact that the intention to expropriate was known prior to the date of expropriation. The valuation criteria will include the declared fiscal value of tangible assets, as well as other criteria that are appropriate to determine the fair market value.
The payment of the indemnity will be fully payable and freely transferable under the terms of article 17-07.
Payment will be made without delay. The time that elapses between the moment the indemnity is established and the moment of payment may not cause damages to the investor. Consequently, its amount will be sufficient to ensure that the investor can, if he decides to transfer it, obtain, at the time of payment, an equal amount of the international currency normally used as a reference by the Party expropriating. The payment will also include interest at the current market rate for the reference currency.
Article 17-09 : Special Formalities and Information Requirements
Nothing in Article 17-03 shall be construed to prevent a Party from adopting or maintaining a measure that prescribes special formalities related to the establishment of investments by investors of another Party, such as investments being constituted in accordance with the laws and regulations of the Party, provided that such formalities do not substantially impair the protection afforded by a Party under this Chapter.
Notwithstanding the provisions of Articles 17-03 and 17-04, each Party may require an investor of another Party or its investment, in its territory, to provide information regarding that investment, in accordance with the provisions of the legislation of that part. Each Party shall protect information that is confidential from any disclosure that could negatively affect the competitive situation of the investment or the investor.
Article 17-10 : Relationship with other Chapters
In the event of any inconsistency between any provision of this chapter and another provision of this Agreement, the latter shall prevail to the extent of the inconsistency.
Article 17-11 : Denial of Benefits.
A Party, after communication and consultation with the other Party, may deny the benefits of this Chapter to an investor of another Party that is an enterprise of that Party and to investments of that investor, if investors from a country that is not a Party hold the majority of the capital of the company or control it, and the company does not have substantial business activities in the territory of the Party under whose law it is constituted or organized.
Article 17-12 : Extraterritorial Application of the Legislation of a Party.
No Party, in relation to the investments of its investors constituted and organized in accordance with the laws and regulations of another Party, may exercise jurisdiction or adopt any measure that has the effect of the extraterritorial application of its legislation or the obstruction of trade between the Parties, or between a Party and a country that is not a Party.
Article 17-13 : Measures Related to the Environment.
No Party shall eliminate domestic measures applicable to health, safety or the environment, or undertake to exempt from their application the investment of an investor from any country, as a means to induce the establishment, acquisition, expansion or conservation of the investment in its territory. If a Party believes that another Party has encouraged an investment in such a way, it may request consultations with that other Party.
Article 17-14 : Promotion of Investments and Exchange of Information.
With the intention of increasing reciprocal investment participation, the Parties will design and implement mechanisms for the dissemination, promotion and exchange of information related to investment opportunities.
The Parties undertake to establish mechanisms related to the exchange of fiscal and tax information.
Article 17-15 : Double Taxation.
The Parties agree to initiate, among themselves, bilateral negotiations aimed at the conclusion of agreements to avoid double taxation, according to the calendar established between the respective competent authorities.
Section B - Settlement of disputes between a Party and an investor of another Party
Article 17-16 : Purpose and Scope of Application.
This section and the annex to this article are intended to ensure equal treatment for investors of each Party on the basis of reciprocity and compliance with the norms and principles of international law, with the due exercise of hearing and defense guarantees. in legal proceedings before an impartial court.
The mechanism established in this section shall be applied to claims made by an investor of a Party (disputing investor) against a Party (disputing Party) regarding the violation of an obligation established in this chapter from the entry into force of this Treaty. The foregoing is without prejudice to the disputing investor and the disputing Party (disputing parties) attempting to settle the dispute through consultation or negotiation.
Article 17-17 : Assumptions for the Filing of a Claim.
The investor of a Party may, on its own behalf or on behalf of a company owned or under its effective control, submit to arbitration a claim based on the fact that another Party has violated an obligation established in this chapter, provided that the investor has suffered loss or damage by virtue of or as a consequence of the breach.
An enterprise that is an investment may not submit a claim to arbitration under this section.
The investor may not file a claim under this section, if more than three years have elapsed from the date on which he knew or should have known of the alleged violation, as well as of the losses or damages suffered.
The investor who initiates proceedings before any judicial court with respect to the measure allegedly in violation of the provisions of this chapter, may not file a claim under this section. The investor may also not bring a claim under this section on behalf of an enterprise owned or controlled by the investor that has commenced proceedings in any court of law with respect to the same infringing action. The foregoing does not apply to the exercise of administrative remedies before the executing authorities of the allegedly infringing measure, provided for in the law of the disputing Party.
The investor who files a claim pursuant to this section or the company on whose behalf the claim is filed may not initiate proceedings before any court of law regarding the measure allegedly in violation.
Article 17-18 : Communication and Submission of the Claim to Arbitration.
The disputing investor who intends to submit a claim to arbitration under the terms of this section shall notify the disputing Party.
As long as ninety days have elapsed since the communication referred to in the preceding paragraph and six months since the measures giving rise to the claim took place, a disputing investor may submit the claim to arbitration in accordance with:
a) The Rules of the Convention on Settlement of Investment Disputes between States and Nationals of other States, concluded in Washington on March 18, 1965 ("ICSID Convention"), when the disputing Party and the investor Party are States part thereof;
b) the ICSID Additional Facility Rules, when the disputing Party or the investor Party, but not both, are State parties to the ICSID Convention; either
c) the Arbitration Rules of the United Nations Commission on International Trade Law ("UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules"), approved by the United Nations General Assembly on December 15, 1976, when the disputing Party and the of the investor are not a State party to the ICSID Convention, or it is not available.
The rules of each of the arbitration procedures mentioned in the previous paragraph will be applicable except to the extent established by this section.
Each Party agrees to submit the claims to arbitration in accordance with the provisions of this section.
Article 17-19 : Accumulation of Procedures.
If any of the disputing parties requests the accumulation of proceedings, a consolidation tribunal will be installed in accordance with the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules and will proceed in accordance with the provisions of those rules, except as provided in this section.
Procedures will accumulate in the following cases:
a) when an investor presents a claim on behalf of a company that is under his effective control and in parallel another or other investors who have participation in the same company, without having control of it, present claims on their own account as a result of the same violations; either
b) when two or more claims are submitted to arbitration that raise common questions of fact and law with respect to the same violation of a Party.
The consolidation tribunal will examine these claims jointly, unless it determines that the interests of one of the disputing parties would be harmed.
Article 17-20 : Applicable Law
Any tribunal established under this section shall decide disputes submitted to it in accordance with this Agreement and the applicable rules of international law.
The Commission's interpretation of a provision of this Agreement shall be binding on any court established pursuant to this section.
Article 17-21 : Final Award
When a tribunal established under this section makes an award unfavorable to a Party, that tribunal may only order:
a) the payment of pecuniary damages and the corresponding interest; either
b) the restitution of the property. In this case, the award will provide that the disputing Party may pay pecuniary damages, plus the applicable interest, instead of restitution, indicating the respective amount.
When the claim is made by an investor representing a company:
a) The award that provides for the restitution of the property will provide that the restitution or, where appropriate, the substitute compensation be granted to the company;
b) The award that provides for the payment of pecuniary damages and corresponding interest will establish that the sum of money be paid to the company.
The award will be rendered without prejudice to the rights that any person with a legal interest may have regarding the reparation of the damages they have suffered, in accordance with the applicable legislation.
Article 17-22 : Payments under insurance or guarantee contracts.
The disputing Party shall not adduce as a defense, counterclaim, right of compensation or others, that the disputing investor received or will receive, in accordance with an insurance or guarantee contract, compensation or other compensation for all or part of the damages for which restitution is requested.
Article 17-23 : Finality and execution of the award.
The award rendered by any court established pursuant to this section shall be binding only on the disputing parties and only with respect to the specific case.
The disputing Party shall abide by and comply with the award without delay and provide for its due execution.
If the Party whose investor was a party to the arbitration procedure considers that the disputing Party has breached or contempt of the final award, it may resort to the dispute settlement procedure between the Parties, established in Chapter XIX, to obtain, where appropriate, , a resolution in the sense that the disputing Party observes the final award and conforms to it.
The disputing investor may resort to the enforcement of an arbitral award in accordance with the ICSID Convention, the United Nations Convention on the Recognition and Enforcement of Foreign Arbitral Awards, held in New York on June 10, 1958; (New York Convention) or the Inter-American Convention on International Commercial Arbitration, held in Panama on January 30, 1975; (Inter-American Convention), regardless of whether or not the procedures contemplated in paragraph 3 have been initiated.
Article 17-24 : Exclusions.
The measures that a Party adopts by virtue of Article 17-02, paragraph 4, nor the decision that prohibits or restricts the acquisition of an investment in its territory by an investor of other part.
Annex to Article 17-08
Colombia reserves the full application of article 17-08 of this chapter. Colombia will not establish more restrictive measures in terms of nationalization, expropriation and compensation, than those in force at the entry into force of this Agreement.
Mexico and Venezuela will only apply the aforementioned article with respect to Colombia from the moment that Colombia notifies them of the withdrawal of its reservation.
Annex to Article 17-16 : Rules of procedure
Rule 1: Communication of the intention to submit the claim to arbitration.
The disputing investor, when notifying the disputing Party of its intention to submit a claim to arbitration, shall indicate the following points:
a) the name, company name and address of the disputing investor and the name or company name and address of the company when the claim has been made on its behalf, proving ownership or effective control thereof;
b) the provisions allegedly breached and any other applicable provision;
c) the facts on which the claim is based; Y
d) the reparation requested and the approximate amount of the damages claimed.
Rule 2: Conditions prior to submitting a claim to the arbitration procedure.
A disputing investor for its own account and an investor representing a company may submit a claim to the arbitration procedure in accordance with section B of this chapter and this annex, only if:
a) in the case of the self-employed investor, he agrees to submit to arbitration under the terms of the procedures established in section B of this chapter and this annex;
b) in the case of an investor representing a company, both the investor and the company agree to submit to arbitration under the terms of the procedures established in section B of this chapter and this annex; Y
c) the investor or the company, or both, as the case may be, undertake in writing not to initiate proceedings before any judicial court with respect to the alleged violation of this chapter. The foregoing does not apply to the exercise of administrative remedies before the very authorities that have adopted the allegedly infringing measure, provided for in the legislation of the disputing Party.
The consent required by this rule shall be in writing, delivered to the disputing Party, and included in the submission of the claim to arbitration.
The investor's consent to submit the claim to arbitration will be considered sufficient to meet the requirements indicated in:
a) Chapter II of the ICSID Convention and the Additional Facility Rules which require the written consent of the Parties;
b) Article II of the New York Convention which requires a written agreement; Y
c) Article I of the Inter-American Convention, which requires an agreement.
Rule 3: Number of arbitrators and method of appointment.
The court will be made up of three arbitrators. Each of the disputing parties will appoint an arbitrator; the third arbitrator, who will be the president of the arbitral tribunal, will be appointed by the disputing parties by mutual agreement. The foregoing is with the exception of the provisions for the accumulation court in accordance with article 17-19 of this chapter and without prejudice to the disputing parties agreeing otherwise.
Rule 4: Integration of the court in the event that one of the disputing parties does not appoint an arbitrator or an agreement is not reached in the appointment of the president of the arbitral tribunal.
The ICSID Secretary General (Secretary General) shall appoint arbitrators in arbitration proceedings, in accordance with this Annex.
When a tribunal, other than the accumulation tribunal, is not integrated within a period of ninety days from the date the claim is submitted to arbitration, the Secretary General, at the request of any of the disputing parties, appoint, at its discretion, the arbitrator or arbitrators not yet appointed, but not the president of the court, who will be appointed in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 3 of this rule.
The Secretary General shall appoint the president of the tribunal from among the arbitrators from the list referred to in paragraph 4, ensuring that the president of the tribunal is not a national of the disputing Party or a national of the Party of the disputing investor. In the event that an arbitrator available to preside over the tribunal is not found on the list, the Secretary General shall designate, from the ICSID Panel of arbitrators, the president of the arbitral tribunal, provided that he is of a different nationality from that of the disputing Party or the on behalf of the disputing investor.
As of the date of entry into force of this Agreement, the Parties will establish and maintain a list of 15 arbitrators as possible presidents of the arbitral tribunal. These arbitrators will meet the qualities established in the ICSID Convention. The members of the list will be appointed by consensus regardless of their nationality.
Rule 5: Consent for the appointment of arbitrators.
For the purposes of Article 39 of the ICSID Convention and Article 7 of Part C of the Additional Facility Rules, and without prejudice to objecting to an arbitrator on grounds other than nationality:
a) the disputing Party accepts the appointment of each of the members of a tribunal established in accordance with the ICSID Convention or the Additional Facility Rules;
b) a disputing investor, whether on its own account or on behalf of a company, may submit a claim to arbitration or continue proceedings under the ICSID Convention or the Additional Facility Rules, only on the condition that the disputing investor and, if their case, the company they represent, express their consent in writing on the appointment of each of the members of the court.
Rule 6: Accumulation of proceedings.
When an accumulation tribunal determines that the claims submitted to arbitration in accordance with article 17-17 of this chapter raise common issues of fact and law, the accumulation tribunal, in the interest of their fair and expeditious resolution, and having heard to the disputing parties, may agree:
a) assume jurisdiction, process and resolve any or all claims, jointly; either
b) assume jurisdiction, process and resolve one or more of the claims on the basis that this will contribute to the resolution of the others.
A disputing party that seeks cumulation to be determined under the terms of paragraph 1 shall request the ICSID Secretary-General to set up an accumulation tribunal and shall specify in its request:
a) the name of the disputing Party or of the disputing investors against whom the cumulation agreement is sought;
b) the nature of the cumulation agreement requested; Y
c) the grounds on which the requested petition is based.
Within a period of 60 days from the date of the petition, the ICSID Secretary General shall designate the three members of the accumulation tribunal from the list referred to in rule 5, paragraph 4 of this annex, indicating who will preside over it. In the event that the list referred to does not find the persons necessary to make these appointments, the ICSID Secretary General will make them from the ICSID Panel of Arbitrators. If there are no arbitrators available on that panel, the ICSID Secretary General will make the remaining appointments at his discretion. One member of the tribunal shall be a national of the disputing Party, and the other member shall be a national of the Party to which one of the disputing investors belongs.
When an accumulation tribunal has been established, the disputing investor who has submitted a claim to arbitration, and has not been named in the application for accumulation made in accordance with paragraph 2, may request in writing that accumulation tribunal be include in the joinder request made in accordance with paragraph 1, and specify in that request:
a) the name and domicile of the disputing investor and, where appropriate, the name or corporate name and domicile of the company;
b) the nature of the cumulation agreement requested; Y
c) the grounds on which the petition is based.
The accumulation court will provide, at the expense of the interested investor, a copy of the accumulation petition to the disputing investors against whom the accumulation agreement is sought.
Once the accumulation court has assumed jurisdiction over a claim, the jurisdiction of the court constituted to hear it will cease. At the request of a disputing party, the accumulation tribunal may, pending its decision on its jurisdiction with respect to a claim, order that the arbitral tribunal constituted to resolve it suspend the proceedings.
Within a period of 15 days from the date of receipt, the disputing Party will send the Commission a copy of:
a) the request for arbitration made pursuant to paragraph 1 of Article 36 of the ICSID Convention; b) notice of arbitration under the terms of Article 2 of Part C of the ICSID Additional Facility Rules;
c) the communication of arbitration in the terms provided by the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules;
d) the accumulation request made by a disputing investor;
e) the request for consolidation made by the disputing Party; either
f) the request for inclusion in an accumulation request made by a disputing investor.
The Commission shall keep a record of the documents referred to in this paragraph.
Rule 7: Communication
The disputing Party will send to the other Parties:
a) communication of a claim that has been submitted to arbitration within 30 days from the date of submission of the claim to arbitration; Y
b) if requested, and at their expense, a copy of the communications presented in the arbitration proceedings.
Rule 8: Participation of a party.
Upon communication to the disputing parties, a Party may submit to any tribunal established under section B of this chapter, its opinion on a matter of interpretation of this Agreement.
Rule 9: Documentation.
Each Party shall be entitled to receive, upon request and at its expense, from the disputing Party a copy of:


a) evidence offered to any court established under section B of this chapter; Y
b) the written communications presented by the disputing parties.
The Party that receives information in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 1 shall treat it as confidential.
Rule 10: Headquarters of the arbitration procedure.
Any tribunal established under section B of this chapter, unless otherwise agreed by the disputing parties, shall conduct the arbitration proceeding in the territory of one of the Parties.
Rule 11: Interpretation of the annexes of reservations and exceptions.
The Commission's interpretation of any provision of this Agreement shall be binding on any court established pursuant to section B of this chapter.
The arbitral tribunal, at the request of the Party, will request the interpretation of the Commission when that Party alleges, as a defense, that a measure allegedly in violation of this Treaty is included in the scope of a reservation or exception consigned in any of its annexes. If the Commission does not present its interpretation in writing within a period of sixty days from the delivery of the request, the arbitral tribunal will decide on the matter.
Rule 12: Provisional or precautionary measures.
The court constituted under section B of this chapter may adopt provisional measures to establish its jurisdiction or preserve the rights of the disputing parties. The court may not order coercive precautionary measures or the suspension of the application of the measure allegedly in violation of this Treaty.
Rule 13: Finality and execution of the award .
The disputing party may request the enforcement of a final award provided that:
a) in the case of a final award rendered under the ICSID Convention:
i) 120 days have elapsed from the date the award was rendered without any disputing party requesting its review or annulment; either
ii) the review or annulment procedures have been completed; Y
b) in the case of a final award made under the ICSID Additional Facility Rules or the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules:
i) three months have elapsed from the date the award was rendered without any disputing party having initiated a review or annulment proceeding; either
ii) a court of the disputing Party has rejected or has declared a request for review or annulment of the award and this decision cannot be appealed.
For the purposes of Article I of the New York Convention and Article I of the Inter-American Convention, it will be considered that the claim submitted to arbitration pursuant to Section B of this chapter arises from a commercial relationship or operation.
Rule 14: General provisions.
A claim is considered submitted to arbitration under the terms of section B of this chapter when:
a) the request for arbitration under paragraph 1 of Article 36 of ICSID has been received by the Secretary-General;

b) the notice of arbitration, pursuant to Article 2 of Part C of the ICSID Additional Facility Rules, has been received by the Secretary-General; either

c) the communication of arbitration contemplated in the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules, has been received by the disputing Party.
The delivery of communications and other documents to a Party shall be made to the national section of that Party at the address referred to in Article 20-02, paragraph 1.
The final awards will be published only in the event that there is a written agreement on the matter between the disputing parties.
CHAPTER XVIII: Intellectual property
Section A - General Provisions.
Article 18-01 : Basic principles.
