Each Party shall grant in its territory to the nationals of another Party adequate and effective protection and defense of intellectual property rights under the same conditions as to the nationals themselves and shall ensure that the measures aimed at defending those rights do not in turn become in obstacles to legitimate trade.
With respect to the existence, acquisition, scope, maintenance, use and observance of the intellectual property rights referred to in this chapter, any advantage, favour, privilege or immunity that a Party grants to the holders of intellectual property rights of any another country, shall be granted immediately and without conditions to the holders of intellectual property rights of the other Parties.
Each Party may grant in its legislation protection to intellectual property rights that is broader than that required in this chapter, provided that such protection is not incompatible with it, nor with the commitments acquired by the Parties in international agreements.
Nothing in this Chapter shall prevent each Party from contemplating in its legislation, practices or conditions related to the granting of licenses that, in particular cases, may constitute an abuse of industrial property rights with a negative effect on competition in the corresponding market. Each Party may accept or maintain, in accordance with other provisions of this Agreement, appropriate measures to prevent or control such practices or conditions.
No Party may grant licenses for the reproduction or translation of protected works in accordance with Article 18-03, when they violate the normal exploitation of the work or cause unjustified damage to the economic interests of the owner of the respective right.
The Parties will make every effort to adhere to the Paris Convention for the Protection of Industrial Property (1967 Act and its subsequent amendments), if they are not already party to it on the date of entry into force of this Agreement.
Section B - Copyright and related rights.
Article 18-02 : Basic principles.
In order to provide adequate and effective protection and defense of copyright and related rights, each Party shall apply, at least, this chapter and the substantive provisions of:
a) Berne Convention for the Protection of Literary and Artistic Works, Paris Act, 1971;
c) International Convention for the Protection of Interpreting and Performing Artists, Producers of Phonograms and Broadcasting Organizations, Rome, 1961;
d) International Convention for the Protection of Producers of Phonograms against Unauthorized Reproduction of their Phonograms, Geneva, 1971.
No Party may require the holders of copyright and related rights to comply with any formality or requirement, as a condition for the enjoyment and exercise of their respective rights.
Article 18-03 : Category of works.
Each Party shall protect the works set forth in Article 2 of the Berne Convention, including any works already known or to be known, which constitute original expression within the spirit of the Berne Convention, including:
a) computer programs (software), in their character of literary works in the sense conferred on the term by the Berne Convention; Y
b) the compilations of facts or data, expressed by any form or procedure, known or yet to be known, provided that due to the selection or arrangement of their content, they constitute creations of an intellectual nature.
The protection provided by each Party under paragraph 1, letter b), does not extend to the facts or data themselves, nor does it affect any copyright on pre-existing works that are part of the compilation.
Article 18-04 : Copyright content.
In addition to the moral rights recognized in their respective legislation, the Parties agree that adequate and effective protection of copyright must contain, among other economic rights, the following:
a) the right to prevent the importation into the territory of the Party of copies of works made without the authorization of the owner;
b) the right to authorize or prohibit the first public distribution of the original and each copy of the work by sale, rental or any other means of distribution to the public;
c) the right to authorize or prohibit the communication of the work to the public, understood as any act by which a plurality of people who do not exceed the domestic sphere can have access to the work, through its dissemination by any procedure or in any form. , known or to be known, of signs, words, sounds or images; Y
d) the right to authorize or prohibit the reproduction of the work by any procedure or in any form, known or to be known. Each Party shall provide that the placing on the market of the original or a copy of the work, including computer programs (software), with the consent of the right holder, shall not exhaust the rental right.
The exercise of the rights referred to in this article does not constitute an obstacle to legitimate trade.
Each Party shall provide that for copyright and related rights:
a) the person who holds economic rights by any title may freely and separately transfer them under the terms of the legislation of each Party for the purposes of exploitation and enjoyment by the holder; Y
b) any person who holds economic rights by virtue of a contract, including employment contracts whose object is the creation of any type of work or the production of phonograms, has the capacity to exercise those rights in their own name and to fully enjoy the benefits derived from those rights.
Each Party will circumscribe the limitations or exceptions to the rights established in this article, to determined special cases that do not prevent the normal exploitation of the work, nor cause unjustified prejudice to the legitimate interests of the right holder.
Any assignment, authorization or license to use economic rights shall be understood to be limited to the forms of exploitation agreed upon in the contract, unless the Parties have expressly agreed otherwise. Each Party shall provide for the adoption of necessary measures to ensure the protection of rights with respect to modes of exploitation not provided for in the contract.
When the ownership of economic rights over a literary or artistic work is held by a legal person, the term of protection shall not be less than fifty years, counted from the first publication of the work or, failing this, from its disclosure. or realization, when applicable.
Article 18-05 : Rights of performers.
The rights of interpreters or performers will be recognized in accordance with the international treaties to which each Party is a party and in accordance with their legislation.
The term of protection of the rights of interpreters or performers may not be less than fifty years, counted from that in which the interpretation or performance took place, or from its fixation, if this were the case.
Article 18-06 : Phonograms.
Without prejudice to the rights established in the Rome Convention, producers of phonograms will have:
a) the right to authorize or prohibit the direct and indirect reproduction of their phonograms;
b) the right to authorize or prohibit the importation into the territory of the Party of copies of the phonogram made without the authorization of the producer;
c) the right to authorize or prohibit the first public distribution of the original and each copy thereof, by sale, rental or any other means of distribution to the public. This distribution right is not exhausted with the introduction to the market of legitimate copies of the phonogram; Y
d) the right to receive remuneration for the use of the phonogram or copies thereof for commercial purposes, when the legislation of each Party establishes it. This remuneration may be shared with the performing artists under the terms of the legislation of the respective Party.
Each Party will circumscribe the limitations or exceptions to the rights established in this article, to determined special cases that do not prevent the normal exploitation of the phonogram, nor cause unjustified prejudice to the legitimate interests of the right holder.
The term of protection of the rights of phonogram producers may not be less than fifty years, counted from the end of the year in which the first fixation was made.
The protection provided for in this article will leave intact and will not affect in any way the protection of copyright over the works. Therefore, none of the provisions set forth in this article may be interpreted in detriment of that protection.
Article 18-07 : Rights of broadcasting organizations.
. The broadcast referred to in the Rome Convention includes, among others, the production of satellite signals carrying programs destined for a broadcasting or telecommunication satellite; likewise, it includes dissemination to the public by an entity that issues or broadcasts the emissions of another, received through any of the aforementioned satellites.
Retransmission by an issuing entity other than that of origin may be by wireless diffusion of signs, sounds, or images, or by wire, cable, fiber optics, or another analogous procedure.
Each Party may establish exceptions in its legislation to the protection granted by this section in the following cases:
a) in the case of a use for private use;
b) when brief fragments have been used for information on current events;
c) in the case of an ephemeral fixation carried out by a broadcasting organization by its own means and by its own broadcasts; Y
d) when it is used exclusively for educational or scientific research purposes.
The term of protection of the rights of broadcasting organizations may not be less than fifty years, counted from the end of the year in which the broadcast was made.
Within one year of the entry into force of this Agreement, each Party shall criminalize:
a) manufacturing, importing, selling, leasing or any act that allows having a device or system that is essential to decrypt an encrypted satellite signal carrying programs, without the authorization of the legitimate distributor of that signal; either
b) the retransmission, fixation, reproduction or dissemination of a broadcast by a broadcasting organization, through any sound or audiovisual medium, without the prior and express authorization of the owner of the broadcasts, as well as the reception, broadcast or distribution by any medium, of broadcasting without the prior and express authorization of the owner.
In any case, the conduct indicated in paragraph 4, literals a) and b), will be cause for civil liability, jointly or not with criminal liability, in accordance with the legislation of each Party.
Section C - Industrial property
Article 18-08 : Matter subject to trademark protection
The Parties may establish as a condition for the registration of trademarks, that the signs are visible or perceptible if they are capable of graphic representation. A brand shall be understood as any sign capable of distinguishing in the market the goods or services produced or marketed by a person, from the identical or similar goods or services produced or marketed by another person. Collective trademarks will also be understood by trademarks.
The right to the exclusive use of the trademark will be acquired by registering it before the respective competent national office, notwithstanding that any Party recognizes previous rights, including those sustained on the basis of use, in accordance with its legislation.
The nature of the goods or services to which a trademark will be applied shall in no case constitute an obstacle to the registration of the trademark.
Article 18-09 : Rights conferred by trademarks.
The owner of a registered trademark shall have the right to prevent all persons, who do not have the consent of the owner, from using identical or similar signs in commerce for goods or services that are identical or similar to those for which the trademark has been registered. owner's trademark, when such use creates a probability of confusion. The probability of confusion will be presumed when an identical or similar sign is used for identical or similar goods or services.
When in two or more Parties there are registrations of an identical or similar trademark in the name of different owners, to distinguish identical or similar goods or services, the marketing of the goods or services identified with that trademark in the territory of the other Party where is also registered, unless the owners of those trademarks sign agreements that allow the aforementioned commercialization.
In the event of reaching the agreements mentioned in paragraph 2, the parties must adopt the necessary provisions to avoid public confusion regarding the origin of the goods or services in question, including matters relating to the identification of the origin of the goods. or services in question with prominent characters and proportional to them for proper information to the consuming public. These agreements must comply with the rules on commercial practices and promotion of competition and be registered with the competent national offices.
In any case, the importation of a good or service that is in the situation described in paragraph 2 shall not be prohibited, when the trademark is not being used by its owner in the territory of the importing Party, unless the owner of that trademark presents valid reasons supported by the existence of obstacles to use. Each Party shall recognize as valid reasons for non-use, circumstances beyond the control of the owner of the trademark that constitute an obstacle to the use of the trademark, such as import restrictions or other government requirements applicable to goods or services identified. for the brand.
It will be understood that a trademark is in use when the goods or services that it distinguishes have been placed on the market or are available on the market under that trademark, in the quantity and in the manner that normally corresponds, taking into account the nature of the trademark. the goods or services and the modalities under which their commercialization is carried out in the market.
When it is done in good faith and does not constitute use as a trademark, third parties may, without the consent of the owner of the registered trademark, use their own name, pseudonym or address, a geographical name, or any other certain indication in the market. relative to the kind, quality, quantity, destination, value, place of origin or time of production of your goods or the provision of your services or other characteristics thereof, provided that:
a) are clearly distinguishable from a registered trademark;
b) are limited to informational purposes;
c) are not capable of misleading the public about the origin of the goods or services; Y
d) do not constitute acts of unfair competition.
Provided that the use made by a third party of a registered trademark is in good faith, is limited to the purpose of informing the public, is not likely to mislead or confuse the business origin of the respective goods and does not constitute an act of competition. unfair, the registration of the trademark does not grant its owner the right to prohibit the use of the trademark to that third party to:
a) advertise, offer for sale or indicate the existence or availability of legitimately marked goods or services in the territory of the Party that granted the registration; either
b) indicate the compatibility or adequacy of spare parts or accessories usable with the goods of the registered trademark.
The owner of the registered trademark may exercise the actions of the case against third parties that use in the market without his consent, an identical or similar trademark or sign to distinguish identical or similar goods or services, when that identity or similarity misleads the public. .
Article 18-10 : Well-known trademarks.
Article 6 bis of the Parés Agreement will also apply, with the corresponding modifications, to service marks. It shall be understood that a mark is well-known in a Party when the mark is known to the relevant sector of the public or business circles of that Party as a result of commercial activities carried out in a Party or outside them, by a person who uses that Party. brand in connection with your goods or services. In order to demonstrate the notoriety of the brand, all the means of proof admitted in the Party in question may be used.
The Parties will not register as a trademark those signs that are the same or similar to a well-known trademark, to be applied to any good or service, in any case in which the use of the trademark by the person requesting its registration could create confusion or risk of association with the person referred to in paragraph 1, or constitutes an unfair advantage of the prestige of the brand. This prohibition will not apply when the registrant is the person referred to in paragraph 1.
The person who initiates the corresponding action against a trademark registration granted in violation of paragraph 2 must prove that he is the owner of the well-known trademark that he claims.
Article 18-11 : Signs not registrable as trademarks.
The Parties may deny the registration of trademarks that violate morality and good customs, that reproduce national symbols or that are misleading.
Article 18-12 : Publication of the trademark application or registration.
Under the terms and conditions established by the legislation of each Party, the competent national office shall order the publication, either of the application or of the registration, as the case may be, so that any person with a legitimate interest can submit observations to the request or exercise the corresponding actions against the registry.
Article 18-13 : Cancellation, expiration or nullity of trademark registration.
The competent national office of each Party, in accordance with its legislation, will cancel or declare the registration of a trademark expired at the request of any interested person, when the trademark has not been used in the Party in which the registration was granted without justifiable reason. , by the owner or by its licensee, during the three consecutive years preceding the date on which the corresponding action is initiated.
The following means of proof of the use of the brand shall be understood as, among others:
a) the commercial invoices that demonstrate the regularity and the quantity of commercialization, at least during the year previous to the date of initiation of the corresponding action;
b) Inventories of goods identified with the brand whose existence is certified by an auditor or notary public that demonstrates regularity in production or sales, or both, at least during the year prior to the date of initiation of the action. correspondent;
c) any other means of proof permitted by the legislation of the Party where the corresponding action is requested.
Proof of use of the trademark will correspond to the owner of the registration. The registration may not be canceled or declared expired when the owner of the trademark presents valid reasons supported by the existence of obstacles to use. The Parties will recognize as valid reasons the circumstances referred to in article 18-09, paragraph 4.
In accordance with the legislation of each Party, the respective office or the competent national authority, as the case may be, will cancel or declare the nullity of the registration of a trademark, at the request of the legitimate owner, when it is identical or similar to a trademark that had been well known, under the terms of article 18-10, at the time of requesting registration.
Article 18-14 : Duration of trademark protection.
The registration of a trademark will have a duration of ten years from the date of filing of the application or from the date of its granting and may be renewed indefinitely for successive periods of ten years, under the terms established by the laws of each Part.
Article 18-15 : Licenses and assignment of trademarks.
The Parties may establish conditions for the licensing and assignment of trademarks, it being understood that compulsory trademark licenses will not be allowed and that the owner of a registered trademark shall have the right to assign it, with or without the transfer of the company to which the trademark belongs. brand.
Article 18-16 : Protection of appellations of origin and geographical indications
Each Party shall protect appellations of origin and geographical indications, under the terms of its legislation.
Each Party may declare the protection of appellations of origin or, where appropriate, of geographical indications, as provided by its legislation, at the request of the competent authorities of the Party where the appellation of origin or geographical indication is protected.
Appellations of origin or geographical indications protected in a Party shall not be considered common or generic to distinguish the good, while their protection subsists in the country of origin.
In relation to appellations of origin and geographical indications, the Parties will establish the legal means so that interested persons can prevent:
a) the use of any means that, in the designation or presentation of the good, indicates or suggests that the good in question comes from a territory, region or locality other than the true place of origin, so as to mislead the public as to the geographical origin of the product;
b) any other use that constitutes an act of unfair competition, in the sense established in article 10 bis of the Parés Agreement.
Article 18-17 : Protection of industrial secrets.
Whoever lawfully has control of an industrial secret will be protected against the disclosure, acquisition or use of said secret without their consent, in a manner contrary to fair trade practices, by third parties, to the extent that:
a) the information is secret in the sense that as a whole or in the precise configuration and composition of its elements, it is not generally known or easily accessible to the people who are members of the circles that normally handle the type of information in question ;
b) the information has actual or potential commercial value because it is secret; Y
c) in the given circumstances, the person legally in control of it has taken reasonable steps to keep it secret.
The information contained in an industrial secret must necessarily refer to the nature, characteristics or purposes of the goods, to the production methods or processes, or to the means or forms of distribution or commercialization of goods or provision of services.
Article 18-18 : Information not considered as an industrial secret.
For the purposes of this chapter, information that is in the public domain, information that is evident to a technician in the field, or information that must be disclosed by law or court order shall not be considered as an industrial secret.
2. It shall not be understood that information that is provided to any authority by a person who possesses it enters the public domain or is disclosed by legal provision, when provided for the purpose of obtaining licenses, permits, authorizations, registrations or any other acts of authority.
Article 18-19 : Support of the industrial secret.
The information that is considered as an industrial secret must appear in documents, electronic or magnetic means, optical discs, microfilms, films or other similar elements.
Article 18-20 : Validity of the protection of the industrial secret.
The protection granted in accordance with article 18-17 will last as long as the conditions established therein exist.
Article 18-21 : Obligations of the user of a trade secret.
Whoever keeps an industrial secret may transmit it or authorize its use to a third party. The authorized user will have the obligation not to disclose the industrial secret by any means. He may only transfer it or authorize its use with the express consent of the person who authorized the use of that secret.
2. In the agreements in which technical knowledge, technical assistance or provision of basic or detailed engineering are transmitted, confidentiality clauses may be established to protect the industrial secrets contained therein. These clauses will specify the aspects that are considered confidential.
Any person who, due to their work, employment, position, position, performance of their profession or business relationship, has access to an industrial secret about the confidentiality of which they have been warned, must refrain from using it and disclosing it without just cause and without consent of the person keeping that secret or its authorized user.
Violation of the provisions of this article will subject the offender to the corresponding penal and administrative sanctions, as well as the obligation to indemnify the damages caused by his conduct, in accordance with the legislation of each Party.
Article 18-22 : Data protection of pharmaceutical or agrochemical goods.
If, as a condition of approving the marketing of pharmochemical goods or agrochemical goods using new chemical constituents, a Party requires the submission of unpublished experimental or other data necessary to determine their safety and efficacy, that Party The Party will protect the referred data as long as its generation implies a considerable effort, except when the publication of said data is necessary to protect the public or when measures are adopted to guarantee the protection of the data against any unfair commercial use.
Each Party shall provide, with respect to the data referred to in paragraph 1 that is submitted to it after the date of entry into force of this Agreement, that no person other than the person who submitted the data may, without the latter's authorization, have such data. data in support of a request for approval of a good for a reasonable period after its submission. For this purpose, a reasonable period will normally be understood as a period of not less than five years counted from the date on which the Party has granted the person who produced the data, the approval to place his good on the market, taking into account the nature of the data and the effort and expense of the individual to generate it. Subject to this provision,
Article 18-23 : Protection of plant varieties.
In accordance with its legislation, each Party shall grant protection to plant varieties. The Parties shall endeavor, to the extent that their systems are compatible, to comply with the substantive provisions in force of the International Convention for the Protection of New Varieties of Plants (UPOV Convention).
Section D - Technology transfer.
Article 18-24 : Promotion of technology transfer.
The Parties shall contribute to the promotion of technological innovation and the transfer and diffusion of technology through favorable government regulations for industry and commerce that are not anti-competitive.
Section E - Enforcement of Intellectual Property Rights.
Article 18-25 : Application of existing guarantees.
This chapter does not impose any obligation on the Parties to establish a judicial system for the enforcement of intellectual property rights, different from the one already existing for the application of the legislation in general. None of its provisions creates obligations with respect to the distribution of the economic resources assigned between the means destined to achieve the observance of intellectual property rights and those destined to the application of laws in general.
Article 18-26 : Guiding principles.
The Parties declare that an adequate and effective protection of intellectual property rights must be inspired by principles of equity, speed, efficiency and procedural effectiveness and respect for a fair process. To this end, the Parties shall ensure such protection in accordance with the following rules, applied in such a way as to avoid the creation of barriers to legitimate trade and to provide safeguards against inappropriate or excessive application of procedures.
Article 18-27 : Essential procedural guarantees.
Each Party undertakes that its legislation guarantees that:
a) the parties in a process are duly notified of all procedural acts and the guarantees of hearing and legality are respected;
b) the parties are duly represented in a process;
c) means to identify and protect confidential information are included;
d) in the process, evidence that is in the possession of the opposing party may be presented, which is pertinent to the solution of the dispute;
e) every judicial decision is based on the evidence regularly and opportunely submitted to the process, ex officio or at the request of a party;
f) the judgments and other acts that put an end to the process, will contain an analysis of the facts of the dispute, the evidence as a whole, the pertinent legal norms and the arguments of the parties, and based on that analysis, the petitions will be resolved, in such a way that there is no pending issue between the parties for the same facts;
g) the judgments and other acts that put an end to the process, as well as the precautionary or precautionary measures may be subject to appeal, review or other resources that legally correspond;
h) the holder of the right is granted an adequate payment as compensation for the damage suffered as a result of the infringement. When the infringement consists of the use of an intellectual property right, the economic value of the use will be considered, among other factors.
Article 18-28 : Measures to prevent or repair damage.
The legislation of each Party shall empower the competent authority to order, quickly and effectively, the following measures:
a) The order to the alleged infringer or to a third party to immediately cease the illegal activity, including the order to prevent goods that infringe an intellectual property right from entering the commercial circuits of its jurisdiction. In the case of imported goods, the order may be issued immediately after customs clearance. In the case of trademarks, the mere removal of a trademark illegally affixed to the goods will not be sufficient to allow their circulation, except in exceptional cases provided by the legislation of that Party.
b) the embargo or preventive seizure, as appropriate, of assets that infringe any of the rights recognized in this chapter;
c) the seizure, confiscation or kidnapping of the instruments used for the commission of the crime;
d) the preservation of evidence related to the alleged infringement;
e) the adoption of the measures contemplated in this article, without having heard the other party, provided that an adequate bond or guarantee is granted and there is a sufficient degree of certainty that:
i) the applicant is the owner of the right;
ii) the right of the applicant is being infringed, or that infringement is imminent; Y
(iii) any delay in issuing those measures is likely to cause irreparable harm to the right holder, or there is a verifiable risk that evidence is being destroyed;
f) Prompt notification to the affected party, immediately after the execution of the measures in the cases provided for in subparagraph e). These measures will be revoked or left without effect, at the request of the affected party, when the procedure on the merits of the matter has not been initiated within the period determined by the legislation of each Party;
g) Ordering the plaintiff, upon request of the defendant, to pay adequate compensation for the damage caused by these measures, when they are revoked, expire due to any act or omission of the applicant, or it is subsequently determined that there was no infringement or threat of infringement of an intellectual property right;
h) the requirement that an applicant for precautionary or precautionary measures provide the necessary information for the identification of the relevant assets by the authority that will carry out the precautionary or precautionary measures.
When considering the issuance of the indicated measures, the judicial authorities will take into account the need for proportionality between the seriousness of the infringement and the measures ordered, as well as the possible impact on the rights of third parties.
Article 18-29 : Compensation and costs.
Each Party shall empower its judicial authorities to order:
a) the payment to the victim of an adequate indemnity as compensation for the damages suffered as a result of the violation;
b) that the infringer assumes the payment of the costs of the process in which the plaintiff has incurred, in accordance with the applicable legislation;
c) the necessary measures so that the goods that constitute infringement of the right are withdrawn from the trade, liquidated outside the commercial channels, or are destroyed, without any compensation, so as to minimize the risk of future infringements;
d) that the materials and instruments predominantly used in the production of illicit goods are, without any compensation, destroyed or placed outside the commercial circuits, under the terms provided in their legislation.
Each Party may, at least with respect to works protected by copyright and phonograms, authorize the judicial authorities to order the recovery of profits or the payment of previously determined damages, or both, even if the infringer did not know or did not have reasonable grounds to know that you were engaged in infringing activity.
Article 18-30 : Administrative procedures.
The principles contained in this section will be applied, as appropriate, if any of the Parties contemplates in its legislation administrative procedures for the protection of the rights recognized in this chapter.
Article 18-31 : Criminal proceedings.
The Parties shall contemplate in their legislation sufficient dissuasive measures of imprisonment, a fine, or both, to punish violations of the rights recognized in this chapter, equivalent to the level of sanctions applied to crimes of a similar magnitude. In any case, they will establish criminal sanctions when there is willful falsification of trademarks or copies protected by copyright on a commercial scale.
The criminal sanctions will include the seizure and confiscation of the goods that constitute a violation of the law, as well as the materials or instruments used predominantly in the production of the illicit goods, and these, without any compensation, will be destroyed or placed out of commerce in the terms provided by the legislation of each Party.
Article 18-32 : Defense of intellectual property rights at the border.
1. Each Party shall adopt procedures so that the holder of a right who has valid reasons to believe that goods identified with counterfeit trademarks or illegal copies protected by copyright or related rights are being imported may submit to the competent authorities, administrative or judicial, a request in order for the customs authorities to order the suspension of the clearance of those goods for free circulation. Neither Party shall be required to apply these procedures to goods in transit.
Each Party may authorize the submission of a request referred to in paragraph 1 with respect to goods that imply other infringements of intellectual property rights, provided that the requirements of this chapter are met.
Each Party may establish similar procedures related to the suspension by the customs authorities of the release of goods destined for export from its territory.
Article 18-33 : Withholding procedures initiated ex officio.
When a Party requires its competent authorities to act on their own initiative and suspend the release of assets for which those authorities have evidence that, prima facie, suggests that they infringe an intellectual property right:
a) The competent authorities may at any time request from the right holder any information that may assist them in the exercise of these powers;
b) the importer and right holder shall be promptly notified by the Party's competent authorities of the suspension. When the importer has requested a reconsideration of the suspension before the competent authorities, this will be subject, with the appropriate modifications, to article 18-28, paragraph 1, literal h), and paragraph 2;
c) The Party will only exempt the authorities and public officials from the responsibility that the appropriate corrective measures give rise to, in the case of acts carried out or disposed of in good faith.
Article 18-34 : Applicable principles.
All the enforcement provisions contained in this section are applicable to the defense of intellectual property rights at the border, when applicable.
Each Party may exclude from the application of measures to defend intellectual property rights at the border, small quantities of goods that are not of a commercial nature and are part of the personal baggage of travelers or are sent in small non-repeated batches.
CHAPTER XIX : Settlement of disputes.
Article 19-01 : Cooperation.
The Parties shall always endeavor to reach agreement on the interpretation and application of this Agreement through cooperation and consultation and shall endeavor to reach a mutually satisfactory solution to any matter that might affect its operation.
Article 19-02 : Scope of application.
Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, this chapter shall apply:
a) to the prevention or settlement of all disputes between the Parties relating to the application or interpretation of this Agreement; Y
b) when a Party considers that a measure of another Party is incompatible with the obligations of this Agreement, or could cause nullification or impairment in the sense of the annex to this article.
If a Party increases an import tax, the Parties may negotiate an appropriate compensation mechanism before initiating a dispute settlement procedure.
Article 19-03 : Settlement of disputes under the GATT.
Any controversy that arises in relation to the provisions of both this Treaty and the GATT, in the agreements negotiated in accordance with the same, may be resolved in one or the other forum, at the choice of the complaining Party.
Before the complaining Party initiates a GATT dispute settlement procedure against another Party alleging reasons substantially equivalent to those it could invoke under this Agreement, the following rules shall apply:
a) the complaining Party shall communicate its intention to do so to the Party or Parties other than the Party against which it intends to initiate proceedings; Y
b) If one or more of the Parties that have received the respective communication wish to resort to the dispute resolution procedure in this chapter regarding the same matter, they and the claimant shall try to agree on a single forum.
Once a Party has initiated a dispute settlement procedure under Article 19-06 or one under the GATT, it may not resort to the other forum on the same matter.
For the purposes of this article, dispute settlement procedures under the GATT shall be considered initiated when a Party requests:
a) the composition of a panel in accordance with Article XXIII:2 of the GATT; either
b) investigation by a Committee of those established in the agreements negotiated in accordance with the GATT.
Article 19-04 : Settlement of disputes in accordance with the Cartagena Agreement.
The Parties will submit to the competition rules that are stated below:
a) Controversies that arise between Colombia and Venezuela in relation to the provisions of both this Treaty and the legal system of the Cartagena Agreement, will be submitted to the jurisdiction of the bodies of the Cartagena Agreement;
b) Controversies that arise between Colombia and Venezuela in relation to the commitments acquired exclusively in this Agreement will be resolved in accordance with the provisions of this chapter;
c) Controversies that arise between Mexico and any of the other Parties in relation to the provisions of this Agreement shall be resolved in accordance with the provisions of this chapter; Y
d) Controversies that arise between the three Parties in relation to the provisions of this Agreement shall be resolved in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
The submission of a controversy to the competence of the bodies of the Cartagena Agreement will not affect the rights that Mexico may have under this Agreement.
Article 19-05 : Consultations.
Any Party may request in writing to the other Parties consultations regarding any measure or regarding any other matter that it considers might affect the operation of this Agreement.
The Party that initiates consultations pursuant to paragraph 1 shall deliver the request to the responsible national bodies of the other Parties.
The third Party that considers to have a substantial interest in the matter, shall have the right to participate in the consultations by delivering a communication to the responsible national bodies of the other Parties.
The consulting Parties:
a) provide the information that allows examining the way in which the measure or any other matter could affect the operation of this Agreement;
b) will endeavor to avoid any solution that adversely affects the interests of the third Party; Y
c) treat confidential information exchanged during consultations in the same manner as the Party that provided it.
Article 19-06 : Intervention of the Commission, good offices, conciliation and mediation.
Any consulting Party may request in writing that the Commission meet whenever a matter is not resolved pursuant to Article 19-05 within forty-five days after delivery of the request for consultations.
A Party may also request in writing that the Commission meet when consultations have been held under Article 5-30 or Article 14-18.
The Party initiating the procedure shall mention in the request the measure or any other matter that is the subject of the claim, shall indicate the provisions of this Agreement that it considers applicable, and shall deliver the request to the responsible national bodies of the other Parties.
The Commission will meet within the ten days following the delivery of the request and, in order to achieve a mutually satisfactory solution to the dispute, it may:
a) convene technical advisers or create the working or expert groups that it deems necessary;
b) resort to good offices, conciliation, mediation or other dispute resolution procedures; either
c) make recommendations.
The Commission shall have the power to combine two or more procedures related to the same measure that are submitted to it in accordance with this article. The Commission may consolidate two or more proceedings regarding other matters that it is aware of in accordance with this article, when it deems appropriate to examine them jointly.
Article 19-07 : Appeal to the arbitral tribunal.
Any consulting Party may request in writing the constitution of an arbitral tribunal when the Commission has met in accordance with the provisions of Article 19-06, paragraph 4 and the matter has not been resolved within:
a) the forty-five days following the meeting; either
b) the forty-five days following the day on which the Commission met to discuss the most recent matter submitted to it, when several proceedings have been accumulated in accordance with article 19-06, paragraph 5.
The requesting Party shall submit the request to the responsible national bodies of the other Parties. Upon delivery of the application, the Commission will establish an arbitral tribunal.
When the third Party considers that it has a substantial interest in the matter, it shall have the right to participate as a complaining Party after notifying the national bodies responsible for the disputing Parties of its intention to intervene. The communication will be delivered as soon as possible, but in no case later than seven days from the date on which one of the Parties has delivered the request for the establishment of the arbitral tribunal.
The third Party that decides not to intervene as a complaining Party pursuant to paragraph 3, must with respect to the same matter and in the absence of a significant change in economic or commercial circumstances, refrain from initiating a dispute settlement procedure pursuant to:
a) this Agreement; either
b) the GATT, invoking reasons substantially equivalent to those that that Party may invoke in accordance with this Agreement.
Article 19-08 : List of arbitrators.
The Commission will integrate a list of up to thirty individuals who have the necessary qualities and disposition to be arbitrators.
The members of the list:
a) have knowledge or experience in law, international trade, other matters related to this Agreement, or in the settlement of disputes arising from international trade agreements;
b) they will be appointed strictly based on their objectivity, reliability and good judgment;
c) they will be independent, they will not be linked to the Parties, and they will not receive instructions from them; Y
d) they will comply with the Code of Conduct established by the Commission.
Article 19-09 : Constitution of the arbitral tribunal.
When there are two disputing Parties, the following procedure shall apply:
a) the arbitral tribunal shall be made up of five members;
b) The disputing Parties shall endeavor to designate the president of the arbitral tribunal within the fifteen days following the delivery of the request for its integration. In the event that the disputing Parties do not reach an agreement within this period, one of them, chosen by lot, will designate it within five days. The individual designated as president:
i) may not be of the nationality of the Party that designates it; Y
ii) in the case of the controversies referred to in Article 19-04, paragraph 1, letter c), may not be a national of any Party to this Agreement;
c) within fifteen days of the election of the chair, each disputing Party shall select two arbitrators who are nationals of the other disputing Party; Y
d) If a disputing Party does not select an arbitrator within that period, the arbitrator shall be selected by lot from among the members of the list who are nationals of the other disputing Party.
When there are three disputing Parties, the following procedure shall apply:
a) the arbitral tribunal shall be made up of five members;
b) The disputing Parties shall endeavor to agree on the appointment of the president of the arbitral tribunal within fifteen days following the delivery of the request for its integration. In the event that the disputing Parties do not reach an agreement within this period, it will be chosen by drawing whether it will be the defendant Party or the complaining Parties who will designate it, and must select it within a period of ten days. The individual selected as chair may not be of the nationality of the Party or Parties that designate him;
c) within fifteen days of the selection of the chair, the Party complained against shall select two arbitrators, each of whom shall be a national of each of the complaining Parties. The complaining Parties will select two arbitrators who are nationals of the Party complained against; Y
d) If any disputing Party does not select an arbitrator within that period, the arbitrator shall be designated by lot in accordance with the nationality criteria in subparagraph c).
Normally, the arbitrators will be chosen from the list referred to in article 19-08.
Article 19-10 : Disqualification.
Any disputing Party may present a challenge without expression of cause, within the fifteen days following that in which the proposal is made, against any individual who does not appear on the list referred to in article 19-08 and who is proposed as arbitrator. .
Article 19-11 : Remuneration and payment of expenses.
The Commission will set the amounts of remuneration and expenses that must be paid to the arbitrators.
The remuneration of the arbitrators, their transportation and lodging expenses, and all general expenses of the arbitral tribunal shall be covered in equal proportions by the disputing Parties.
Each arbitrator will keep a record and present a final account of his time and expenses, and the arbitral tribunal will keep a similar record and will render a final account of all general expenses.
Article 19-12 : Rules of procedure.
The Commission will establish Rules of Procedure, which will be applied by the arbitral tribunals constituted in accordance with this chapter. These rules will include, among others, provisions regarding the Referee Code of Conduct. For the elaboration of the rules, the Commission will take into consideration the following principles:
a) the procedures shall guarantee, as a minimum, the right to a hearing before the arbitral tribunal, as well as the opportunity to present arguments and replies or responses in writing; Y
b) The hearings before the arbitral tribunal, the deliberations and the preliminary decision, as well as all the writings and communications with it, will be confidential.
Article 19-13 : Participation of the third Party.
The non-disputing Party, after delivering communications to the national bodies responsible for the disputing Parties, shall have the right to attend all hearings, to present written and oral communications to the arbitral tribunal and to receive a copy of the briefs submitted by the disputing Parties. .
Article 19-14 : Preliminary decision.
Unless otherwise agreed between the disputing Parties, within ninety days following the appointment of the last arbitrator, the arbitral tribunal will submit to the disputing Parties a preliminary decision that will contain:
a) findings of fact;
b) the determination of whether the measure in question is incompatible with the obligations derived from this Agreement, or is cause for nullification or impairment within the meaning of the annex to article 19-02; Y
c) the draft operative part.
The disputing Parties may make written observations to the arbitral tribunal on the preliminary decision within fourteen days following its presentation.
In the case referred to in paragraph 2, and after examining the written observations, the arbitral tribunal may, ex officio or at the request of any disputing Party:
a) carry out any diligence it deems appropriate;
b) request the observations of any disputing Party or of any Party that has delivered the communication referred to in article 19-13; Y
c) reconsider its preliminary decision.
Article 19-15 : Final decision.
The arbitral tribunal will submit to the Commission a final decision and, if applicable, the saved votes on the issues with respect to which there has not been a unanimous decision, within thirty days from the presentation of the preliminary decision.
Neither the preliminary decision nor the final decision will reveal the identity of the arbitrators who have voted with the majority or with the minority.
The final decision of the arbitral tribunal will be announced fifteen days after its communication to the Commission.
Article 19-16 : Compliance with the final decision.
The final decision of the arbitral tribunal shall be binding on the disputing Parties in the terms and within the terms that it orders.
When the final decision of the arbitral tribunal declares that the measure is inconsistent with this Agreement, the defendant Party, whenever possible, will refrain from executing the measure or will repeal it.
When the decision of the arbitral tribunal declares that the measure is cause for nullification and impairment within the meaning of the annex to Article 19-02, it will determine the level of nullification or impairment and may suggest adjustments mutually satisfactory to the disputing Parties.
Article 19-17 : Suspension of benefits.
The complaining Party may suspend the application of benefits of equivalent effect to the defendant Party if the arbitral tribunal resolves:
a) that a measure is incompatible with the obligations of this Agreement and the Party complained against does not comply with the final resolution within the term that the arbitral tribunal has established; either
b) that a measure is cause for nullification or impairment within the meaning of the annex to Article 19-02 and the disputing Parties do not reach a mutually satisfactory settlement of the dispute within the term established by the arbitral tribunal.
The suspension of benefits will last until the defendant Party complies with the final decision of the arbitral tribunal or until the disputing Parties reach a mutually satisfactory settlement of the dispute, as the case may be.
In considering the benefits to be suspended under paragraph 1:
a) the complaining Party shall first seek to suspend the benefits within the same sector or sectors that are affected by the measure, or by another matter that the arbitral tribunal has considered incompatible with the obligations derived from this Agreement, or that has been cause for annulment. or impairment within the meaning of the annex to article 19-02; Y
b) the complaining Party that considers that it is not feasible or effective to suspend benefits in the same sector or sectors, may suspend benefits in other sectors.
At the written request of any disputing Party, communicated to the responsible national bodies of the other Parties, the Commission shall establish an arbitral tribunal to determine whether the level of benefits that a complaining Party has suspended in accordance with paragraph 1 is manifestly excessive. To the extent possible, the arbitral tribunal will be made up of the same members that made up the one that issued the final decision referred to in article 19-15.
The arbitral tribunal constituted for the purposes of paragraph 4, will present its final decision within sixty days following the appointment of the last arbitrator, or in any other period agreed upon by the Parties.
Article 19-18 : Interpretation by the Commission.
The Commission will endeavor to agree, as soon as possible, on an appropriate interpretation or response when:
a) a Party considers that a matter of interpretation or application of this Agreement, arising or to arise in a judicial or administrative proceeding of another Party, merits interpretation by the Commission; either
b) a Party receives a request for an opinion on a question of interpretation or application of this Agreement from a court or administrative body of a Party.
The Party in whose territory the court or administrative body is located shall present to them any interpretation agreed upon by the Commission, in accordance with the procedures of that forum.
When the Commission fails to reach an agreement, either Party may submit its own opinion to the court or administrative body, in accordance with the procedures of that forum.
Article 19-19 : Alternative means for dispute resolution.
To the extent possible, each Party shall promote and facilitate the use of arbitration and other alternative means for the resolution of international commercial disputes between individuals.
To this end, each Party shall have adequate procedures to ensure compliance with arbitration agreements and the recognition and enforcement of arbitral awards pronounced in such disputes. These procedures will take into consideration the provisions of the United Nations Convention on the Recognition and Enforcement of Foreign Arbitral Awards, of 1958, or the Inter-American Convention on International Commercial Arbitration, of 1975.
The Commission may establish a Private Business Dispute Advisory Committee composed of persons who have specialized knowledge or experience in the resolution of private international business disputes. The Committee will present reports and recommendations to the Commission on general questions sent by it regarding the existence, use and effectiveness of arbitration and other procedures for the settlement of such controversies.
Annex to article 19-02 : Nullification and impairment
The Parties may resort to the dispute resolution mechanism of this chapter, when by virtue of the application of a measure that does not contravene the Treaty, they consider that the benefits that they could reasonably have expected to receive from the application of chapters III are annulled or impaired. to IX except for what is established regarding investment in the automotive sector, chapter X, chapter XIV, chapter XV or chapter XVI.
2. Paragraph 1 shall apply even when the Party against which the appeal is filed invokes a general exception provided for in Article 22-01, except in the case of a general exception applicable to cross-border trade in services.
CHAPTER XX : Administration of the Treaty
Article 20-01 : The Administrative Commission.
The Parties create the Administrative Commission, made up of the heads of the responsible national bodies indicated in Annex 1 to this article, or by the persons they designate.
It will correspond to the Commission:
a) ensure compliance and correct application of the provisions of this Agreement;
b) evaluate the results achieved in the application of this Agreement, monitor its development and recommend to the Parties the modifications it deems appropriate;
c) intervene in disputes under the terms established in Chapter XIX;
d) supervise the work of all the committees and working groups established in this Agreement and included in Annex 2 to this article, which will report to the Commission;
e) monitor pricing practices and policies in specific sectors in order to detect those cases that could cause distortions in trade between the Parties;
f) recommend to the Parties the adoption of the necessary measures to implement their decisions; Y
g) hear about any other matter that could affect the operation of this Agreement or that is attributed to it by any provision thereof.
The Commission may:
a) establish and delegate responsibilities in ad hoc committees or permanent committees, working groups and experts and supervise their work;
b) request the advice of individuals or groups without governmental ties; Y
c) if agreed by the Parties, adopt any other action for the exercise of its functions.
The Commission will establish its rules and procedures and all its decisions will be unanimous.
The Commission shall meet at least once a year in ordinary session, which shall be successively chaired by each Party.
Article 20-02 : National Sections.
The responsible national body of each Party shall designate its office or permanent official dependency that shall act as the national section of that Party and shall communicate to the other Parties:
a) the name and position of the official responsible for his national section; Y
b) the address of their national section, to which communications should be addressed.
The Commission shall supervise the coordinated functioning of the national sections of the Parties.
It will correspond to the national sections:
a) provide assistance to the Commission;
b) provide administrative support to arbitral tribunals;
c) on instructions from the Commission, support the work of the other committees and groups established under this Agreement; Y
d) fulfill the other functions entrusted to it by the Commission.
Annex 1 to article 20-01 : Responsible national bodies
The national body responsible for each Party shall be:
a) in the case of Colombia, the Ministry of Foreign Trade or the body that replaces it;
b) in the case of Mexico, the Ministry of Commerce and Industrial Development or the body that replaces it; Y
c) in the case of Venezuela, the Foreign Trade Institute or the body that replaces it.
Annex 2 to article 20-01 : Committees, Subcommittees and Working Groups
Committees:
Automotive Sector Committee (article 4-03) -Agricultural
Trade Committee (article 5-10)
-Phytosanitary and Zoosanitary Measures Committee (article 5-29)
-Sugar Analysis Committee (annex 3 to article 5-04)
-Committee of Financial Services (article 12-11)
-Committee for Standardization Measures (article 14-17)
-Micro, Small and Medium Industry Committee (article 15-22)
-Purchasing Committee (annex 8 to article 15-02)
-Committee on Competition Matters (article 16-03) -State
Company Practices Committee (article 16-03)
subcommittees
Subcommittee on Health Standardization Measures (article 14-17)
Work groups:
Working Group on Agricultural Technical and Marketing Standards (article 5-09)
-Working Group on Rules of Origin (article 6-17)
-Working Group on Customs Procedures (7-11)
-Working Group on Professional Services ( annex 1 to article 10-02)
-Temporary Entry Working Group (article 13-06)
CHAPTER XXI : Transparency
Article 21-01 : Information Center.
Each Party shall designate a unit or office as an information center to facilitate communication between the Parties on any matter covered by this Agreement.
When requested by a Party, the information center of another Party will indicate the agency or official responsible for the matter and will provide the support required to facilitate communication with the requesting Party.
Article 21-02 : Publication.
Each Party shall ensure that its laws, regulations, procedures and administrative rulings of general application that refer to any matter covered by this Agreement are promptly published or made available for the information of the Parties and any interested party.
Each Party shall endeavor to:
a) publish in advance any measures; Y
b) provide the Parties and any interested party with a reasonable opportunity to comment on the measure.
Article 21-03 : Provision of information.
Each Party shall communicate, to the extent possible, to any other Party that has an interest in the matter, any measure that the Party considers could affect or substantially affect the interests of that other Party under the terms of this Agreement.
Each Party, at the request of another Party, shall provide it with information and prompt responses to its questions regarding any measure, regardless of whether or not that other Party has been previously notified of that measure.
The communication or supply of information referred to in this article will be carried out without prejudging whether or not the measure is compatible with this Treaty.
Article 21-04 : Hearing guarantees, legality and due process.
The Parties reaffirm the guarantees of hearing, legality and due process enshrined in their respective legislation.
Each Party shall maintain tribunals and judicial or administrative procedures for the review and, when appropriate, the correction of the final acts related to this Agreement.
Each Party shall ensure that in the judicial and administrative procedures related to the application of any measure that affects the operation of this Agreement, the essential formalities of the procedure are observed, and the legal cause of the same is founded and motivated.
CHAPTER XXII : Exceptions
Article 22-01 : General exceptions.
Article XX of the GATT and its interpretative notes are incorporated into this Agreement and form an integral part thereof, for the purposes of:
a) Chapters III to IX, except to the extent that any of their provisions apply to services or investment; Y
b) Chapter XIV, except to the extent that any of its provisions apply to services,
Nothing in the provisions of:
a) Chapters III to IX, to the extent that any of its provisions apply to services;
b) Chapter XIV, to the extent that any of its provisions apply to services; Y
c) Chapters X and XI,
shall be construed to prevent any Party from adopting or enforcing the measures necessary to ensure compliance with laws or regulations that are not inconsistent with the provisions of this Agreement, including those relating to health and safety, and consumer protection; provided that such measures are not applied in a manner that constitutes a means of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination between countries where the same conditions prevail, or a disguised restriction on trade between the Parties.
Article 22-02 : National security.
Other than as provided in Article 15-19, nothing in this Agreement shall be construed to mean:
a) compel a Party to provide or give access to information the disclosure of which it considers contrary to its essential security interests;
b) prevent a Party from taking any measure it deems necessary to protect its essential security interests:
i) regarding the trade in arms, ammunition and war materiel and trade and operations on goods, materials, services and technology that are carried out with the direct or indirect purpose of providing supplies to a military institution or other defense establishment ;
ii) adopted in time of war or other emergencies in international relations; either
iii) regarding the application of national policies or international agreements on the non-proliferation of nuclear weapons or other nuclear explosive devices; either
c) prevent any Party from adopting measures in accordance with its obligations under the United Nations Charter for the Maintenance of International Peace and Security.
Article 22-03 : Disclosure of information.
Nothing in this Agreement shall be construed to oblige a Party to provide or give access to information the disclosure of which would impede compliance with the laws of the Party or would be contrary to its Constitution or its laws as regards the protection of the privacy of people, financial affairs and bank accounts of individual clients of financial institutions, among others.
CHAPTER XXIII: Final provisions
Article 23-01 : Annexes.
The annexes to this Agreement constitute an integral part thereof.
Article 23-02 : Amendments.
The Parties may agree to any modification or addition to this Agreement.
The agreed modifications and additions will enter into force once they are approved according to the corresponding legal procedures of each Party and will constitute an integral part of this Agreement.
Article 23-03 : Convergence.
The Parties will promote the convergence of this Treaty with other integration agreements of the Latin American countries, in accordance with the mechanisms established in the 1980 Montevideo Treaty.
Article 23-04 : Entry into force.
This Treaty will enter into force on January 1, 1995, once the communications certifying that the necessary legal formalities have been completed are exchanged.
The provisions of paragraph 1 do not prevent a Party, in accordance with its legislation, from provisionally applying this Agreement.
Article 23-05 : Validity.
This Agreement will have a minimum validity of three years. Once that period has elapsed, its duration will be indefinite.
Article 23-06 : Reserves.
This Treaty may not be subject to reservations or interpretative declarations at the time of its ratification.
Article 23-07 : Accession.
This Treaty will be open to the accession of the countries of Latin America and the Caribbean, either for a country or group of countries, after negotiation between that country or group of countries and the Parties.
The accession will enter into force once the communications certifying that the legal formalities have been completed are exchanged.
Article 23-08 : Complaint.
Any Party may denounce this Agreement. This denunciation will take effect 180 days after it is communicated to the other Parties and the denunciation is communicated to the General Secretariat of ALADI, without prejudice to the fact that the Parties may agree on a different term.
The denunciation of this Agreement by one Party does not affect its validity between the other Parties.
Article 23-09 : Evaluation of the Treaty.
The Parties will periodically evaluate the development of this Agreement in order to seek its improvement and consolidate the integration process in the region, promoting an active participation of the productive sectors.
